# CLAUDE.md

AI-facing project guide. Loaded into every Claude session for this repo — keep tight, keep operational, keep current. **If you make a non-trivial architectural change, update this file.** The goal is that a fresh session can pick up the project without re-deriving its conventions from the code.

This file is for *behavior* (what to do / not do, where to look, what not to violate). For *how things work*, link into [DESIGN.md](DESIGN.md). For *what changed*, see [Tracker.md](Tracker.md).

---

## What this is

Lichborne is a DragonRealms (text MUD) game client. Electron + React + TypeScript. Connects via Lich5 (recommended) or direct SGE login. Windows x64 only. Single-developer project with a small, reachable tester pool.

**Product position (DESIGN.md §1, §24):** **display and configuration layer over Lich**, not a Lich-replacement. Lich owns automation (scripts, variables, triggers, repository). Lichborne owns rendering, themes, the panel system, profile portability, and surfacing Lich state. **Push back on requests that head toward duplicating Lich functionality** — say so before implementing. **Lich-first nuance (Principle #2):** Lich is the optimal route; the native automation layer (highlights / triggers / macros / aliases / mutes / substitutes) is a deliberate *backwards-compat regression path* for direct-SGE (no-Lich) players, NOT a Frostbite/Genie-style scripting engine — finite and GUI-configured by design.

---

## Principles (rules of the road)

1. **YAML is truth for user state. localStorage is a working copy.** New per-character settings need only a `scopedKey(character, ...)` write + `saveProfile()` call. Shared settings live in `_shared.yaml` and need typed entries in `SharedProfile` + `buildSharedProfile` + `importSharedProfile`.
2. **Lich-first, with a backwards-compatible direct-connect path.** Lich is the *optimal, recommended* way to play — it owns the heavy automation and unlocks the features that need it (maps, spell timers, variables, scripts, repository). But a player can connect **directly to the game (SGE, no Lich)**, and Lichborne must stay genuinely usable that way: every feature either works without Lich or **degrades gracefully** to a native fallback — never a hard "you need Lich" wall (a Lich-optimal feature with a *degraded* no-Lich mode is fine; full parity is NOT required). Lichborne's **native automation (highlights, triggers, macros, aliases, mutes/substitutes) IS that backwards-compat regression layer** — and a GUI convenience for non-scripters. The line we hold: that native layer is **finite and GUI-configured — we do NOT reinvent a scripting engine** (Frostbite's embedded Ruby, Genie's `#command` language); heavy/conditional automation stays Lich's job — *surface* it, don't *host* a script runtime. Lich integration is additive on top. This is the Lich analogue of §32's "AI enhances, never gates" — an optional power tier over a working baseline. (Full articulation: DESIGN §24.1; sharpened 2026-06-09 from the prior "Lich is optional but recommended / every feature must work without Lich" — graceful degradation replaces the parity absolute.)
3. **No silent data loss.** If a file can't be processed (future-version YAML, malformed XML), log it and **preserve it on disk**. Never overwrite content the code doesn't understand.
4. **Theme any new UI — and do a theme pass on every new feature.** All colors come from CSS custom properties in `themes.ts`; use `color-mix(in srgb, var(--x) N%, transparent)` for tints. When you add UI, audit its CSS: every surface / text / border color must be a `var(--…)`, and **eyeball it on a light theme** (Classic Light, Ivory, Mist, Parchment) — the `--bg-raised/sunken/base/hover` scale is spread out on dark themes but compressed near-white on light ones, so a literal that looks fine in the default dark theme can vanish on a light one (this is the single most-recurring bug class here: pitfalls #34, #55; B108 / B112 / B140 / B141 were ALL this). **The only color literals that are acceptable** (do NOT try to theme these): dark **drop-shadows** under menus/popovers (`rgba(0,0,0,.5)` — dark shadows read fine on light themes too); **text-halos over a *saturated* fill** (white text + `rgba(0,0,0,.9)` stroke on vital / exp bars — works on every theme precisely because the fill is always saturated, e.g. `.vital-text`, `.exp-rxp-bar-text`); and `var(--x, #fallback)` **fallbacks** (the fallback never fires since `darkBase` is the floor every theme merges over). Anything else hardcoded is a light-theme bug waiting to happen — let the cascade do the work. The v0.10.0 top-chrome features (app-bar, More menu, compact vitals, active-glow) were built/audited to this bar; the native Electron menu is the deliberate exception (Win32-native, not themeable) — the About dialog USED to be one too but was converted to a themed modal in v0.17.0.
5. **Stream IDs preserve case end-to-end.** A Lich script that pushes to `LichScripts` lands in a panel called `LichScripts`. The `NEVER_DISCOVER` filter is the only case-insensitive check.
6. **Per-session everything.** Every IPC payload carries `sessionId`; every listener filters by it; every per-character state lives under `lichborne.{character}.{suffix}`. Cross-session bleed is the most common bug class.
7. **Fix root causes, not symptoms.** Past root-cause fixes (B14, B17, B20, B33, B36, B53, etc.) left inline comments explaining the current shape of the code. Read them before patching nearby logic.
8. **Ship reversibly.** Bold changes welcome (v0.6.3 maps rewrite, login redesign). Pair them with migration paths (profile schema versioning, NSIS rescue hook) so a bad rev never costs a tester their data.
9. **Wire every UI-manipulating setting to every surface it should affect — defining it isn't enough, and "new feature" means "make the settings reach it."** This is as load-bearing as theming (Principle #4): a setting that silently doesn't apply to a new surface is a bug. **Font size / line height:** game-area UI scales ONLY if it uses `var(--game-font-size)` / `var(--game-line-height)` — directly, or via `em` inheriting from a container anchored to those vars. **`rem` does NOT scale** — it's anchored to the html root (16px), not the per-character setting; never use `rem` for game-area text (pitfall #45). It's exactly why the icon bar, vitals bar, and Mode button silently stopped tracking the font setting. When you add a game-area strip/panel/button, **anchor its container to `font-size: var(--game-font-size)` and size children (and their heights/paddings) in `em`** so the whole thing scales without clipping — copy how `.panel-frame-body` ([panel-frame.css](src/renderer/styles/panel-frame.css)) and the panel roots in [panels.css](src/renderer/styles/panels.css) do it. **Accessibility:** high-contrast, color-blind, large-print, and epilepsy-safe are applied by `applySettingsToDOM` (re-applied after every theme write via the hook — pitfall #33); new UI inherits them only if it draws from the theme/overlay vars. **The check (do it for every new surface):** toggle each relevant setting — font size, line height, high contrast, color blind, large print, epilepsy-safe — and confirm the surface actually responds. App-chrome modals MAY deliberately opt out of game-font scaling (they have their own sizing), but that's a conscious call, not an accident.

10. **Evidence over guesses — and a guess must be NAMED as one, not slipped in as fact. This is not just for bug-hunting; it governs ALL work** (features, refactors, answering a question, proposing a design, "this is safe because…"). Every claim about how the code behaves comes from reading the actual file *this session* (the Iron rule, generalized) and every decision rests on a chain of code-confirmed links — see "Investigating a reported bug" for the discipline; it applies the same whether or not there's a tester report. When grounding *is* available, get it before acting: grep + read the lines, trace the path end-to-end, simulate the condition (a `tmp-*` repro / a harness), or add a `[diag]` log and reproduce — don't pattern-match a plausible answer onto a symptom (the v0.14.1 macro "fix" did exactly that and shipped a regression). **When grounding is genuinely NOT available** — the behavior is external/unknowable from here, the cost of proving it is prohibitive, or it's a real design judgment with no single right answer — **do NOT silently proceed on a hunch. Say so out loud, label it speculation, and get explicit mutual agreement that we're "going in blind" before acting.** Surface what you can't prove, propose the cheapest way to reduce the uncertainty (read X, run Y, ask Sekmeht), and only take the blind path by shared decision — never as a unilateral guess dressed up as confidence. A fix that is *provably safe regardless of the residual unknown* (B191's `document.hidden` guard) is always preferable to one that's only correct *if the guess holds*.

11. **Every user-facing feature ships with its slash-command surface — and every feature CHANGE updates the registry in lockstep (Sekmeht, 2026-07-04).** The `/` command registry (DESIGN §37, [slashCommands.ts](src/renderer/slashCommands.ts)) is a FIRST-CLASS control surface for Lichborne — as load-bearing as theming (#4) and settings-wiring (#9) — not a bolt-on that covers whatever existed when it shipped. A feature reachable only by mouse is half-wired; a slash command whose hints/summaries/behavior have drifted from the feature it drives is WORSE than none (it teaches users wrong things with confidence). Three obligations:
    - **ADD a feature → ask "what's its `/command`?"** New rule type → the full verb set (`add`/`remove`/`list`/`edit` + the panel's `openRuleId` plumbing); new toggle/setting → an on/off/toggle command (the `/timestamps` shape); new panel/surface → open/close/list coverage; new selectable values → extend the palette's `SlashLiveData` completion chips. The registry is declarative, so one entry buys the parser, the palette, and `/help` at once. **Not every feature fits** (pure-visual polish, one-time setup dialogs, drag-only interactions) — the requirement is to ASK the question explicitly and record the "no command because X" decision in the feature's DESIGN section, never to skip it silently.
    - **CHANGE a feature → grep `slashCommands.ts` for its noun and update in lockstep.** New option on a rule type → add the `key=value` to its `add` entry (+ hint + example); renamed/removed field → fix the executor, the summary formatter, and the hints; changed semantics → re-read every entry touching that subsystem and re-run the harness. The summaries (`hlSummary`, `muteSummary`, …), signature hints, examples, and error messages are USER-FACING documentation — stale ones are bugs, same class as a stale tooltip.
    - **REMOVE/RENAME a feature → its commands fail helpfully, never silently.** Retired command → remove the entry (fail-closed handles the rest with the `/help` hint); renamed concept → keep the old noun as a `nounAliases` entry so muscle memory survives (the `/gag`→mute precedent).
    The enforcement hook is **pre-merge check #5** below; the extension mechanics (registry entry shape, ctx conventions, live-data prop) are in the "Slash commands & toasts" architecture section.

---

## UX/UI polish standards (make a feature look *finished*, not just functional)

A feature that works but looks rough reads as unfinished — and in a single-developer client with a small tester pool, "looks unfinished" is the impression that sticks. **Treat a deliberate polish pass as a named, mandatory step before any new UI goes to testers**, distinct from "does it function." The worked example is the Automation Analytics v0.14.4 pass (the AnalyticsReview banner / per-row badges); the conventions below are extracted from it and apply to every new surface. They sit alongside Principle #4 (theme everything) and #9 (wire settings everywhere) — same bar, the *visual-finish* axis.

1. **Quiet by default — every glyph on screen should mean "look at me."** A clean / empty / zero state must read as clean *at a glance*, never as a wall of zeros. Concretely: **hide** zero-count chips/badges entirely (don't render `0`); collapse "nothing here" to a single affirmative marker (a green **"✓ no issues"** chip) instead of a row of zeros; use a **faint neutral dash** (`var(--text-faint)`, low opacity) for an idle/uneventful row rather than a loud emoji. Noise trains the eye to ignore the surface; absence of noise is what makes the real signal pop.

2. **Consistent shape beats conditional presence.** Render the SAME structure whether or not a section has content — an empty category still shows as its collapsible "report-card" row (muted, body reads "None."), so the layout is predictable and nothing pops in or out as data arrives. **Mute** the empties (≈50% opacity summary + faded count badge) so the populated ones stand out; don't omit them. A user scanning a stable set of rows reads faster than one watching rows appear and vanish.

3. **Order by severity / importance, not declaration or insertion order.** When listing issues, categories, chips, or rows, sort by what the user cares about first (Analytics: broken → conflict → duplicate → obsolete → no-op → quiet). Declaration order is an implementation accident; the user reads top-down and expects the most important thing first.

4. **Stateful/collapsible UI must SURVIVE re-render — HOIST helper components to module scope.** A React component defined *inside* a render function is a brand-new component TYPE on every render, so React unmounts+remounts it and any state it owns — including native `<details>` open/closed — is lost. In a panel that re-renders on every game line (every Automations sub-panel does), this manifests as **"the section I expanded collapses itself the moment new text scrolls in."** Fix: define sub-components at MODULE level, give each rendered section a stable `key`, and lift any user-controlled "is this expanded" state somewhere that persists across renders. (This was the literal v0.14.4 collapse-on-scroll bug — the AnalyticsReview `Section`/`Jump`/`Chip` helpers were inline and got hoisted to `AASection`/`AAJump`/`AAChip` to fix it.) **Any new collapsible/disclosure UI inside a frequently-re-rendering panel: check this first.**

5. **Visual hierarchy comes from MUTING and dividers, not just spacing.** Reduced opacity / faded color on inactive, empty, or secondary elements does more for "looks finished" than adding margins. A labeled divider — uppercase, letter-spaced, `var(--text-faint)`, a thin `color-mix` top border — to separate two *kinds* of content (Analytics: health issues vs. usage counts) reads as deliberate structure rather than a pile of rows.

6. **Polish colors are theme-safe by construction (ties to Principle #4, pitfalls #34/#55/#63).** Success greens, severity reds/ambers, muted/idle backgrounds all come from `color-mix(in srgb, <fixed-hue> N%, var(--bg-*/--text-*))` so the hue stays meaningful while contrast self-corrects per theme — and **eyeball every newly-polished surface on a light theme** (Classic Light / Ivory / Mist / Parchment) before calling it done. A polished-looking chip on the default dark theme that vanishes on white is not polished.

7. **A polished strip is text-height + minimal padding (pitfalls #75b/#77).** Header/footer/chip/badge text in a short container must pin `line-height: 1` (it otherwise inherits the game line-height and balloons the box), action icons stay ≤1em with `line-height: 1`, vertical padding 2–3px. A strip rendered taller than its own text, or bigger than the content it relates to, is the most common "why does this look clunky" smell.

8. **The UI must EXPLAIN ITSELF — a label or icon that names a feature without saying what it does is half-built.** Every category, mode, toggle, badge, status chip, or icon whose meaning isn't obvious from its single word needs an in-UI explanation: a `title=` hover tooltip at minimum, and visible descriptive text (a one-line `desc` under a section, a placeholder, a short caption) where there's room — with a concrete EXAMPLE when the concept is abstract (Automation Analytics' "Obsolete (covered by regex)" reads *“a regex rule already matches everything this rule matches — e.g. `joins the .+` covers `joins the adventure`”*). Two specific rules this came from: **(a)** show the explanation in the EMPTY state too — a clean report card whose every row says only "None." teaches the user nothing; render the `desc` even at count 0 so "what is this category?" is answerable without first having an entry in it. **(b)** put the tooltip on the always-visible affordance (a collapsible section's `<summary>`, not its hidden body) so it's reachable while collapsed. The test: a tester opening the feature for the first time, with nothing in it yet, should be able to learn what every word on screen means without asking. "Broken / Conflicts / Obsolete / Quiet" meant nothing until each got a tooltip + visible description (Sekmeht: *"It's not apparent at all through the UI"*) — bake the explanations in **as you build the feature**, not after a tester asks.

**The pass itself:** before handing a feature to a tester, re-read its UI asking — *does the clean/empty state look intentional? does anything collapse or jump on re-render? is the most important thing on top? does it hold up on a light theme? can a first-time user tell what every label/icon means without asking?* — not just "does it work." That review is the difference between "shipped" and "shipped and looks like we meant it."

---

## Architecture (pointers, not duplication)

### Process split
- **`src/main/`** — Electron main (Node). Sockets, XML parsing, Lich child process, file I/O. Built with esbuild (`build-main.mjs`).
- **`src/renderer/`** — React UI. Built with Vite. Talks to main only via `window.api.*` (preload.ts contextBridge).
- **`src/shared/types.ts`** — single source of truth for IPC payloads and game-event shapes. Imported by both sides.

### Multi-session model (DESIGN.md §13)
N character sessions across one OR MORE windows (v0.11.0). `src/main/main.ts` holds `sessions = Map<SessionId, Session>`; each Session owns its own `ConnectionManager`, `StormFrontParser`, `LichBridge`. Every push channel (`game-event`, `connection-status`, `raw-xml`, `error`) carries `sessionId`. **When adding any IPC, include `sessionId` in the payload.**

### Multi-window & decouple (v0.11.0)
A tabbed character can be **decoupled into its own OS window** while everything stays in ONE process — so cross-character features (Quick Send) keep working, Lich-launch stays coordinated, and profiles/localStorage aren't raced by a second exe. The model:

- **Main owns the session ROSTER; windows are views.** Pre-v0.11.0 `SessionsContext` ([SessionsContext.tsx](src/renderer/SessionsContext.tsx)) was the renderer-local source of truth for the session list. Now main is authoritative: each `Session` carries `meta` (characterId/account/character/game/useLich) + `ownerWindowId`, and `broadcastRoster()` pushes a `RosterEntry[]` (`session-roster` channel) to EVERY window on any change. [RosterContext.tsx](src/renderer/RosterContext.tsx) mirrors it; `useRoster()` exposes `roster` (all windows' sessions, for Quick Send), `windowId`, `isPrimary`, `myRoster` (owned). `SessionsContext` still drives this window's *own* tabs (rich `SessionStatus` stays local); the **decouple-sync effect in AppShell** ([App.tsx](src/renderer/App.tsx)) keeps it aligned: PULL owned sessions on mount (`get-owned-sessions`) + react to PUSH `session-acquire`/`session-release`.
- **Window registry + owner-targeted routing.** `windows: Map<webContentsId, BrowserWindow>` + `primaryWindowId`. Per-session output routes via `ownerWindow(s)` (falls back to primary if the owner is gone); app-global output goes to primary (auto-update), focused (menu), or sender (flash). `ownerWindowId` is the calling window's `event.sender.id`, set in the LOGIN handler.
- **Decouple = move ownership, NEVER touch the socket.** `session:move-window(sessionId, 'new' | 'main' | windowId)` reassigns `ownerWindowId`; the source window drops the tab (`session-release` → local `removeSession`) and the target mounts a fresh GameWindow. The socket/parser/LichBridge are untouched (verified: GameWindow unmount cleanup doesn't disconnect — pitfall #59). Three entry points: right-click tab, Window menu, Bulk Connect "separate windows" checkbox (persisted in `_shared.yaml` as `bulkConnectSeparateWindows`, default off). **Last-character guard** at 3 levels (main backstop + greyed Window-menu item + disabled right-click) — can't empty a window. The tab right-click menu (v0.11.6) hosts the move options alongside Reconnect/Disconnect and shows only the actionable ones — see pitfall #69.
- **Lifecycle.** Closing a **secondary** window = graceful **logout** of its character(s) (`runSecondaryWindowClose`); **re-home** is explicit via Window → "Move Character to Main Window" (auto-closes the emptied window, no disconnect). Closing the **primary** = app quit (`runAppShutdown` flushes EVERY window's debounced profile saves, then drains all sessions). **Multiple exe instances are deliberately NOT gated** (isolated character sets); the shared-`userData` hardening is a separate deferred item.
- **State replay (seamless takeover) — see pitfall #60.** A window taking over a session gets a render-only replay (scrollback + every vital/room/etc.), gated so it never re-fires triggers or double-logs.
- **Cross-window state — three rules.** (1) **App-wide settings applied to the DOM** (the theme) don't auto-cross windows — each window has its own document. The fix is a `storage`-event listener in App that re-applies on change (`lichborne.theme`/`myThemes` → `initTheme()`); the window that made the change applied it directly and gets no storage event (no double-apply). App-wide settings that are READ FRESH per use (session-log settings, advanced/Lich settings) need NO sync. Per-character settings live in one window (the owner), so no cross-window race. (2) **Anything app-level that acts on "the active character in another window"** must route through main to that window: Profile Transfer remounts a moved-in target via `session:reload` → owner window (pitfall #56); the modal's active-target detection uses the **roster** (all windows), not the local `sessions`, or a cross-window target is mis-treated as inactive and its owner window overwrites the import. (3) **The native menu is one global menu for the focused window** — `refreshMenuState()` scopes Next/Prev/Close/Move enabled-state to the FOCUSED window's owned-session count (re-run on `win.on('focus')`), and `sendMenuAction` routes to the focused window. Don't gate Window-menu items on global counts.

### Lich launch & connect (v0.7.0; GTK-friendly spawn v0.9.x)
`LichConnection.launch()` spawns `rubyw lich.rbw --stormfront --dragonrealms` as a **detached** child (not a service). Lich takes its force-mode path: bind `127.0.0.1:11024`, then `accept` **exactly one** front-end and **close the listener** — one Lich = one session. Readiness is **not** a fixed delay: `connectWithRetry()` retries the real connection (250ms cadence, ≥30s cap) until the port accepts — the first success IS the session socket (no throwaway probes). `launch()` resolves on the child's `spawn` event and watches `exit` so a Lich that dies on startup fails fast (with its launch-log tail). Because each Lich serves one front-end then frees 11024, multi-character logins **must serialize** their spawn→connect window — `serializeLichLaunch()` in [ConnectionManager.ts](src/main/connection/ConnectionManager.ts) is a module-level promise chain shared across all per-session managers. SGE/eaccess auth runs outside that chain so it overlaps the queue wait. A failed launch `killProcess()`es its Lich so it can't squat the port.

**Spawn shape is GTK-friendly (v0.9.x).** Lich runs as a normal Windows GUI-subsystem process so Ruby/GTK scripts get a proper process/desktop context — the community-standard shape (matches how Frostbite / Genie launch Lich). Three things make it so, all in `launch()`: (1) it runs **`rubyw.exe`** (GUI subsystem), not `ruby.exe` (console) — `resolveRubyw()` derives `rubyw.exe` from the configured ruby path (`/ruby\.exe$/i` → `rubyw.exe`), falling back to the given path if the derived file doesn't exist (so a path already pointing at `rubyw.exe` is used verbatim); (2) **no `windowsHide`** (rubyw is windowless by nature — nothing to hide); (3) **no stderr pipe** — Lich's stdout+stderr are redirected to a per-character log file at `{userData}/Logs/lich-launch/{Character}.log` (truncated per launch), and `describeExit()` reads that file's tail for the error banner instead of an in-memory pipe. The redirected-console **pipe** of the old shape was the prime suspect for GTK flakiness (the kind of non-GUI process context that made widget pumps racy), which is why diagnostics moved to a file. `detached` + `unref()` + the child handle are kept (Lich is the proxy, must outlive us; the handle lets `exitInfo` fail a dead launch fast). The settings/default ruby path stays `ruby.exe` ([lichSettings.ts](src/renderer/lichSettings.ts)) — derivation handles rubyw at launch time, no migration.

**Ruby GTK script windows — product stance REVERSED (v0.9.x), VERIFIED WORKING (2026-07-03).** The prior decision was "do NOT support GTK" (2026-05-30/06-01), on the theory that Lichborne's launch shape made GTK irredeemably flaky. **That decision is reversed** (Sekmeht, "I need to revisit the connection stuff to allow for GTK — it's the only way"). The v0.9.x **GTK-friendly spawn shape** (above: `rubyw.exe`, no `windowsHide`, no stderr pipe) was changed specifically to give Ruby/GTK a normal GUI-subsystem process context — the same shape Frostbite/Genie use, under which the same scripts work. **Status: empirically VERIFIED working (Sekmeht, 2026-07-03)** — GTK script windows paint and behave correctly under the new spawn. GTK support is a confirmed capability, not a bet.

The historical root-cause analysis (still useful background): GTK scripts (`Gtk.queue { ... }` + `Gtk::Window.new`) showed (a) windows that failed to paint, (b) windows that painted only **intermittently** (kill-counter often surfaced only after a start→kill→restart cycle — timing-dependent, not categorically "never paints"), and (c) crashes on widget interaction (the `;vars setup` shape — a window that *did* paint could still take Lich down on interaction). The loop itself WAS running (`lich.rbw:135` calls `Gtk.main` unconditionally; `gtk.rb:148-155` yields via `GLib::Idle.add`), so the failure was a subtler process-context problem — which the old console-subsystem (`ruby.exe`) + hidden-window + redirected-stderr-pipe spawn produced, and which the new GUI-subsystem (`rubyw.exe`) plain spawn removed (confirmed by the 2026-07-03 verification). **When a tester reports a GTK script not working:** first confirm they're on a v0.9.x+ build (the new spawn); if it still misbehaves, that's a real bug worth investigating (capture the launch log at `{userData}/Logs/lich-launch/`), not expected behaviour. The `<streamWindow>` / `<pushStream>` XML approach (see `newkill-counter.lic`) remains the more portable recommendation for script authors (works in every front-end with no GTK runtime), and Lichborne-native equivalents are still preferred where they exist (`;vars setup` → the Lich Dashboard → Variables editor, v0.9.0). **The v0.9.0 proactive `--- Lichborne:` GTK advisory (the GTK detector + `client-notice` channel) was REMOVED in v0.9.x** alongside this launch change — it assumed GTK is broken, which is no longer the operating assumption (see the #54 tombstone). Pitfall #52 (the `;vars setup` GTK root-cause analysis) is kept as useful background. Pitfall #53 (write-through-Lich editor pattern) is unaffected.

**Lich version compatibility (verified against Lich 5.18.0, 2026-07-16).** Lichborne presents to Lich as **`--stormfront`** — a deliberate, permanent choice. The whole integration surface was re-verified against the 5.18 diff and every touchpoint holds unchanged: the force-mode loopback bind + one-FE-then-close-listener model (Lich still defaults `bind_address` to `127.0.0.1`; Lichborne passes neither `--bind-address` nor `--reconnect`); the `inventory_boxes_off` downstream-hook + `_flag Display Inventory Boxes 1` workaround (pitfall #80 — the hook now carries `persist: true`, still installed for stormfront/GSL FEs); the `;eq Vars[…]; Vars.save` write path + Marshal reader (pitfalls #53/#91 — `vars.rb` untouched); `cmd\r\n` command sends (the 5.18 CRLF→LF normalization is on `StringProc` script-source, NOT the FE socket); the `;listall` poll + `interceptLine` (pitfalls #22/#76 — output format unchanged); and the parser's existing handling of `<d>` command links, `<output class="mono">`, and an inline-prepended `<dialogData id='AimTimerDialog'>…</dialogData>text` (pitfall #87). Three things to KNOW for tester support: **(1) Lich 5.18 now requires Ruby 4.0** (was 2.6/3.2) — it alerts + refuses to launch on older Ruby, which surfaces in Lichborne's launch-log error banner as a failed launch; a "Lich won't start after updating" report on 5.18+ ⇒ check the tester's Ruby version FIRST. **(2) Lich core now natively injects the room-number + obvious-exits display** (`;display roomlinks`/`roommono`, #1438), replacing the retired dr-script `roomnumbers.lic`; DR defaults are **mono + plain text** (not `<d>` links), which Lichborne's `monoMode` renders correctly — testers may just SEE room-number/exit lines they didn't before (gated on the game room-number flag / `display_uid`/`display_lichid`). **(3) The `(u12345)` subtitle gap** — see pitfall #65. **Do NOT present as the new `--saga` frontend.** Saga is NOT a new XML dialect: in Lich's capability registry ([front-end.rb](file:///c:/temp/lich-dev/lich-5/lib/common/front-end.rb)) `saga = stormfront's exact caps (xml/streams/mono/room_window) + one extra: sentinel`. The `sentinel` capability makes Lich prefix **every** downstream line with `\x1f` (0x1F, `ORIGIN_SENTINEL`) — a whole-stream "this feed came through Lich" marker for Saga's detachable/cloud-profile-sync architecture (attach/detach over LAN/tailscale, keyed on `<playerID>`), NOT a per-line Lich-injected-vs-game discriminator. So adopting saga would give Lichborne the SAME content it already gets as stormfront, plus a sentinel byte to strip from every line (and re-audit every `^`-anchored parser rule against — room-info detection, the hand-glance patterns #78, prompt handling) for ZERO functional gain. Revisit only if a future Lich feature becomes saga/`sentinel`-GATED (nothing in 5.18 is), or if Saga ever ships local config files worth an import parser (today it's cloud-only, no user base). Saga is a **sibling front-end**, not a config format to import — "supporting" it would only ever mean identifying AS it, which is all downside.

**Re-verified against Lich 5.19.1 (2026-07-21, the current release): the integration surface HOLDS unchanged — no Lichborne change needed.** The 5.19.0→5.19.1 delta is all safe: **#1452** (resilient ActiveSessions ownership + a shutdown watchdog, `lib/main/main.rb` + new `shutdown_watchdog.rb`) only hardens Lich's TEARDOWN — it arms a watchdog so a hung `before_dying`/`Vars.save`/socket-close can't leave the process alive holding port 11024; it does NOT touch the force-mode FE listener/accept model, and it's mildly BENEFICIAL for us (faster port release on Lich exit). **#1450** (fix(**gs**)) ingests newly-exposed GS-ONLY fields — mindState `ascension_exp/exp/fashlonae/lumnis/rpa` and `<roommeta weather/inside/water/sanctuary/realm/bonfire>` numeric codes into `XMLData` — which DR never sends, and Lichborne's tokenizer ignores as unknown roommeta attributes regardless (note: if DR ever exposes `<roommeta weather>` too, that'd be a STRUCTURED weather signal worth revisiting the §34.9 "no passive weather feed" conclusion — GS-only today). **The one MAJOR issue was Lich 5.19.0-ONLY, already fixed upstream:** #1443 rewrote the ARGV frontend-flag checks to `a == /regex/`, and `String == Regexp` is ALWAYS false in Ruby, so `--stormfront` (which Lichborne passes) never matched → `$frontend` fell through to `'wizard'` → GSL/Wizard-protocol tokens leaked into the client instead of XML (a tester hit exactly this). **#1456 (shipped in 5.19.1) fixes it** (`==`→`=~`, verified in `lib/main/argv_options.rb:283-332`: `a =~ /^--stormfront$/i` → `$frontend='stormfront'`). **TESTER SUPPORT: a tester on 5.19.x seeing raw protocol garbage / unformatted tokens instead of the normal game feed is on 5.19.0 — have them update to 5.19.1+** (Lich-side bug, Lich-side fix; no Lichborne change). The DR-facing part of the 5.18→5.19 delta was already absorbed in v0.16.1 (assess parser #1413, `(prone)/(sitting)` posture #1442, AimTimerDialog unload #1414, combat-position #1400, roomlinks/roommono #1438). The only changes NEW since that review are **connection-only and never touch the FE socket**: **#1449** lowers the GAME socket's TCP keepalive idle 120s→30s ([games.rb](file:///c:/temp/lich-dev/lich-5/lib/games.rb) `Game.open`; the commit body states "No effect on the [FE] socket"), and **#1437** adds bind-host keywords for `--detachable-client`/`--headless` (Lichborne uses neither; the FE listener still defaults to `127.0.0.1`, main.rb:298/448). The rest of the new XML work is **GemStone-specific or Lich-INTERNAL, so it never reaches a DR front-end**: GS creature XML/templates (#1425/#1427, `lib/gemstone/*`), climate/terrain feeds (#1388, GS weather), a `reserve` pushStream id (#1379, GS), and the REXML→Ox parser migration (#1396, Lich's own state parse — the FE still gets the raw XML passthrough). **Backwards-compat is inherent** (Sekmeht's rule 2026-07-20 — features stay compatible with at least the previous major Lich): the connection model, the `$frontend`-flag lever, and the XML passthrough are all version-agnostic, and **Lichborne's parser degrades gracefully on ANY unknown tag** — the tokenizer strips every `<…>` (tags never leak as text), an unhandled tag falls through the `tagStart` switch ([StormFrontParser.ts](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts) ~355) and is ignored, and its inner text still shows. So a future Lich/DR tag can't break the client; the only thing that does is a whole-protocol swap away from XML (e.g. Lich emitting GSL/Wizard text), because GSL isn't XML and the tokenizer would leak it — but that's a `$frontend`-mode problem (the flag), not a parser gap.

### Game-text pipeline
`SGEConnection`/`LichConnection` → `ConnectionManager` (line events) → `LichBridge.interceptLine` → `StormFrontParser.parse` (stateful XML tokenizer) → `GameEvent[]` → batched IPC → `GameWindow`.

`StormFrontParser` is **stateful** (boldDepth, color stack, monoMode, injuryBuf, etc.). Call `parser.reset()` on new login. `<prompt>` is a good boundary for transient state.

Main text rendering uses **react-virtuoso**. Scroll pinning is a delicate state machine: `pinnedRef` snapshots before commit, `suppressUntilRef` gates programmatic scrolls, `onWheel` un-pins synchronously. **As of v0.11.6 (B155), Virtuoso's `followOutput` is OFF — we own pinned auto-scroll ourselves** (`followOutput` under-measures the fractional last row and two-steps; don't re-enable it). **As of v0.11.8 (B158), ONE primitive owns every auto-scroll path: `stickToBottom(reindex?)`** — a self-cancelling rAF **settle loop** that re-asserts the DOM-truth bottom (`scrollTop = scrollHeight − clientHeight`) every frame until `scrollHeight` is **stable for two consecutive frames** (or a 20-frame cap). This replaced the THREE mechanisms that used to race the same target (the old inline sync+1rAF in `totalListHeightChanged`, the `resnapToBottom` settle loop, and the inline `ResizeObserver` write). **Why a loop:** Virtuoso measures the just-appended last row ASYNCHRONOUSLY (its ResizeObserver fires a frame or two late), so `scrollHeight` keeps growing after content renders — any single write (even rAF-deferred) can land on the short pre-measure bottom = the intermittent "rests one line short, wheel down once to fix it" bug. The loop rides out the measurement tail; requiring TWO stable frames is what guarantees the async grow is captured. The per-batch path (`totalListHeightChanged`) does a **synchronous first write before paint** (last line flush in the same frame new content renders) THEN the settle loop; `reindex=true` paths (badge/End, font change, tab show, focus regain, replay) issue ONE `scrollToIndex({index:'LAST'})` first because the target row may be off-screen/unmounted. The loop writes ONLY `scrollTop` (no re-render), so it's safe to call from the scroller's height-gated `ResizeObserver` (viewport resize) without the re-render→re-fire feedback loop a `scrollToIndex`-based resnap caused. Keeping the loop alive across a flood (cancel+restart per batch) keeps the bottom flush every frame, so bursts read as continuous scroll instead of chunky jumps. **During an active flood, suppress stays armed, so only `onWheel` (wheel-up) un-pins — scrollbar drag/arrow un-pins only when the flood pauses; this matches "stay stuck until the user manually scrolls up."** **Don't re-enable `followOutput`, don't add another bespoke one-shot scroll correction, and don't split `stickToBottom` back into multiple mechanisms** (pitfall #68). A story-window smooth-scroll feature existed v0.6.8–v0.6.11 and was **removed in v0.6.12** — marginal, a magnet for false bug reports. **Don't add `useEffect`-driven scroll logic** (or re-add smooth scroll) without reading GameWindow.tsx and DESIGN.md §23. Room-state updates funnel through the rAF pump (`roomQueueRef`), not direct `setRoomState` — see DESIGN.md §23 and pitfall #20. **As of v0.13.4 two more load-bearing structures sit in this pipeline:** main's `scheduleFlush` coalesces event floods (16ms leading-edge throttle — one renderer batch per frame during bursts, immediate when idle; B172, pitfall #82d), and ALL scrollback appends route through `appendTrimmed()` — hysteresis trimming (grow to `MAX_LINES + TRIM_CHUNK`, ONE cut back to `MAX_LINES`), never a per-batch slice to the exact cap (B171, pitfall #81 — that per-batch trim was the years-long "text hops after a while").

### Command-send pipeline (the dual of the game-text pipeline)
How a command reaches the game — traced end-to-end in the v0.14.1 validation pass, recorded so it isn't re-derived. **Boundary:** renderer → `window.api.sendCommand(sessionId, cmd)` → preload `ipcRenderer.send(SEND_COMMAND)` → main `ipcMain.on(SEND_COMMAND)` → `getSession(sessionId)` (**silently `return`s if it misses** — the failure point that makes a wrong sessionId look like a dead send) → `s.connection.send(cmd)` → Lich mode `LichConnection.socket.write(cmd + '\r\n')` / direct mode `gameSocket.write(cmd + '\r\n')` (the `\r\n` is what lets Lich process `;commands` as a complete line). **All ~10 renderer entry points** (typed bar, macros, aliases, repeat-macro tokens, triggers, Genie/Lich map walks, room-exit buttons, in-text command links, Lich-dash run) funnel through three GameWindow functions — `dispatchUserText` (typed/alias/token), `sendCommandSequence` (macro + alias batches, with `delayMs`), and `sendCommand` (map/exit/in-text-link/trigger via `triggerCallbacks`) — and **every one MUST send via `sessionIdRef.current`, never a captured `session.sessionId`** (pitfall #86: a tab Reconnect swaps the id without remounting, so a held closure goes stale and main drops the command). Quick Send is the exception: it targets specific characters from the live main-pushed `roster` (`entry.sessionId`), not the active session. **The renderer-side echo (`setLines` `>cmd`) is SEPARATE from the send** — so *"a command echoes but the game never responds and no `>` prompt returns, while typed commands still work"* is the canonical signature of a send-side bug (stale id, or a dropped/edited-out `window.api.sendCommand` call). **As of v0.14.5 all THREE funnels also `logToSession` the `>cmd` echo** (`dispatchUserText` and `sendCommandSequence` always did; the canonical `sendCommand` was the gap — map walks / exit clicks / in-text links / trigger commands echoed on screen but never reached the Session Log). Log↔screen parity is the invariant: any new send path that echoes must also log (or do both via the canonical funnels). **The INVERSE signature — *the game responds but no `>cmd` echoes* — means a send path wired to a RAW `window.api.sendCommand` that skips the `setLines` echo** (B199, Sekmeht: trigger `command` actions did exactly this — `triggerCallbacks.sendCommand` was a raw send, so a trigger that sent `smile` showed only the game's reply). The fix is to route such a path through the canonical echoing `sendCommand` useCallback (echo `>cmd` + send) — for `triggerCallbacks`, via a `sendCommandRef` latest-closure ref because `sendCommand` is defined LATER in the component than the `triggerCallbacks` useMemo. When adding ANY new command path, send through the echoing `sendCommand` (or `dispatchUserText`/`sendCommandSequence`), NOT a bare `window.api.sendCommand`, unless a no-echo send is genuinely intended. The pure resolution core that decides WHICH strings get sent (`resolveMacro`/`resolveAlias`/`parseCursorMarker`/`matchKeyCombo`/`interpolate`/`getMacroToken`) is regression-covered by `tmp-cmd-harness` (see the testing note above); the component send call itself is not (pitfall #86 — re-read the body). **Command history is persisted per character as of v0.15.2 (F57):** [commandHistory.ts](src/renderer/commandHistory.ts) load/save on the `commandHistory` scopedKey (≤200 entries, try/catch'd write — background telemetry, never toasts; rides `state:` → YAML, deliberately NOT in `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` — the automationStats precedent), the ↑-from-live-line draft is stashed in `historyDraftRef` and restored at index −1, and Esc clears the bar (layered under the slash palette's Esc — palette dismiss first, clear second). The push POLICY (which paths push — pitfall #31) is unchanged. Two one-time per-character macro seeds live side by side in GameWindow: `seededRepeatMacros` (v0.8.3, repeat tokens) and `seededNumpadMovement` (v0.15.2, F56 — the Frostbite-default movement pad); both skip already-bound keys and never resurrect deletions. The command input's first-session placeholder (F58) is gated on the initial history load being empty. **Two more v0.15.2 input-layer behaviors (DESIGN §38.6/38.7):** typed lines split on `;` (F59 — `splitTypedCommands` in [macros.ts](src/renderer/macros.ts), harness-covered: a line whose first non-space char is `;` is a LICH command returned VERBATIM — never split a `;line`; `\;` escapes; each part runs the full alias/echo/send/log tail; QuickSend deliberately does not split), and printable keys typed while focus is elsewhere FOCUS the command bar (F60 — end of the global keydown handler; guards: no modifier chords, not in a text field/select/contentEditable, `!anyModalOpenRef.current`, `!e.isComposing`, `!e.defaultPrevented`; always-on by design, no setting). Ctrl+F opens the in-scrollback search (F49, [ScrollbackSearch.tsx](src/renderer/components/ScrollbackSearch.tsx)) — its jumps UN-PIN then `scrollToIndex`, never a new scroll mechanism (pitfall #68).

### Slash commands & toasts (DESIGN §37, Phase 1 v0.14.5, Phases 2–3 v0.14.6)
A `/`-leading line in the command bar is a **CLIENT command** — it executes locally and NEVER reaches the game. Intercepted at the top of `dispatchUserText` ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)), after the history push (↑ recalls), before alias resolution; unknown commands **fail closed** with a hint (a typo can't leak to DR); `//text` escapes to send a literal `/text`. **[slashCommands.ts](src/renderer/slashCommands.ts) is a declarative REGISTRY (the §35 capturer-registry philosophy)** — `SLASH_COMMANDS` entries (noun + aliases + verb + positional args + `key=value` options + flags + description + example + executor) drive the parser, the palette, AND `/help` from one source; **adding a command = one entry, never an if-chain**. Executors receive a `SlashContext` built in GameWindow's `runSlashLine` whose apply functions do exactly what a panel save does (`saveX` → `setX` → `saveProfile()`), and rule creation goes through the `newX()` factories — so a slash-created rule is byte-compatible with an editor-created one (`allGroups: true`, quota-safe saves). Result lines echo as `internal-system` client text + log to `[sys]`. The **palette** ([SlashPalette.tsx](src/renderer/components/SlashPalette.tsx)) mounts only while the input holds a slash line: command-list mode (↑/↓ select, **Tab/click completes, Enter ALWAYS submits as typed** — don't make Enter complete) → argument-hint mode (signature + live validation via `parseSlash` + a live highlight style preview). It's **portaled** (works when the command bar lives in a floating window, §33) at z 130, sized off `var(--game-font-size)` directly (pitfall #45b), and forwards keys via a `useImperativeHandle` ref called FIRST in `handleCommandKey`. **Scope: the main command bar only — QuickSend deliberately does NOT interpret `/`** (it targets other characters' sessions; a client command there is ambiguous). Syntax rules when extending: noun-first, ONE positional sugar per command (highlight's color, contact's template), everything else `key=value`, flags bare. **Colors resolve via [colors.ts](src/renderer/colors.ts)** (curated 16 > user customs (`/colors add`, `SharedProfile.customColors`) > the ~148 standard web names (Genie's vocabulary) > `#hex`) — **resolve-at-entry: rules/themes store HEX**, palette edits never retro-update; editors' free-text color fields resolve names via `normalizeColorInput` **on BLUR only** (on-change hijacks longer names) and the Theme Editor commits on blur/Enter (theme vars always store hex). A noun may have BOTH a bare form and verbs (`findCommand`: verb wins, bare falls back — the `/colors` shape). **When a noun has a bare form AND verbs, the palette must NOT commit to the bare form on `noun ` — else the verbs never list or Tab-complete (v0.16.0 `/ai` bug).** `resolveCommand` ([SlashPalette.tsx](src/renderer/components/SlashPalette.tsx)) skips the bare (verb `''`) prefix for any noun in `NOUNS_WITH_VERBS`, so `/ai ` / `/colors ` STAY in list mode and their verbs (on/off/catchup, add/remove/list) rank + Tab-complete exactly like a verb-only noun (`/trigger`). The parser's `findCommand` still RUNS the bare form on Enter (`/ai`→status is unchanged); only the palette's *commit-to-arg-hint* is suppressed. This is why a bare+verbs noun must NOT also define a redundant `status`-style verb that duplicates the bare output (two identical rows) — give status to the bare form only. Both such nouns today (`ai`, `colors`) have a NO-ARG bare form, so suppressing the bare commit never hides an argument hint; if you ever add a bare+verbs noun whose bare form takes ARGS, this rule would swallow its arg-hint and needs revisiting. **Completion is RANKED** (`scoreEntry` in SlashPalette: exact part 100 > verb prefix 80 > noun prefix 60 > verb substring 30 > noun substring 20 > description 10; best-first stable sort, selection resets to top on every edit) — Tab completes what the user was typing, never registry order; noun-prefix TIES fall to registry position (bare `/t` → `/template add`; `/ts` is deterministic via the exact alias). **A required arg is required NON-EMPTY** unless its spec sets `allowEmpty` (only `/sub add`'s replacement — `""` = delete the text); without that check `/highlight add ""` mints a dead empty-pattern rule. When adding list-style verbs, pass `listRules`' `where` param if the rules live outside the Automations panel (contacts → Contacts panel). **Phase 2 (v0.14.6):** `/alias` (expansion splits on `;`), the `/trigger` quick-form (`"pattern" do "command"` — the `do` is optional sugar; fills `newTrigger`'s built-in command action; gates/multi-action stay editor-only BY DESIGN, don't grow the quick-form into the full editor), and **`edit` verbs on all five rule nouns** via `SlashContext.openRuleEditor(tab, id)` → GameWindow's `slashOpenRule` state → AutomationsPanel `*OpenId` props → each panel's `openRuleId` find-and-select effect (the TriggersPanel pattern — replicate it verbatim for any new panel; MacrosPanel's is `openAliasId` + `initialTab='aliases'`). The palette takes an optional **`live: SlashLiveData` prop** (template/mode/group/stream/theme names) for value-completion chips — extend THAT prop for new live completions; never import character state into the registry (it stays pure). **/help is TWO views:** bare = one plain-language row per NOUN from the `NOUN_HELP` blurb map (**new noun ⇒ add its blurb line**; a missing noun falls back to the entry description) + a syntax primer; `/help <noun> [verb]` = signatures with every arg/option HINT spelled out — hints are user-facing documentation, keep them current (Principle #11). **Result lines can be RICH** (`SlashLine = string | {rich:[{text,color}]}` — `/colors` renders each name in its color; GameWindow maps `color` → `TextSegment.fg`, `slashLineText()` for the log). **Record lookups on user tokens use the `hasColor`-style `hasOwnProperty.call` guard** — a bare `NAMED_COLORS[t]` walks the prototype chain and `"constructor"` resolves to a FUNCTION (a real shipped-then-caught bug). Slash-added aliases/triggers arm immediately (aliasesRef mirror; `useTriggerEngine(triggers, …)`). **Phase 3 (client control — `/mode`, `/group`, `/panel`, `/theme`, `/log search`, `/clear`):** these executors drive UI STATE, so the integration lives in GameWindow's `SlashContext` implementations, with the registry entries as dumb matchers — keep that split. Load-bearing details: `/panel` MUST branch on `layoutMode` (pitfall #79 — `slashOpenPanel`/`slashClosePanel` generalize `toggleFreeDebugWindow`'s shape in free mode, `addToZone(id,'bottom')`/`removeTab` in panels mode) and matches stream names case-insensitively but opens the CANONICAL id (Principle #5); `/theme` resolves id-FIRST then display name (two built-ins share "Classic", pitfall #35 — a shared name that isn't an id errors with the ids); `/mode`/`/group` ride `useGroups()` so rule gating updates through `activeGroupStates` automatically; `/clear` = the context menu's `clearLines`, deliberately no confirm. **Contacts/templates are in the registry too** (`/contact add "Bob" Friends` updates an existing contact rather than erroring; template names must EXIST — no silent minting; `/template remove` mirrors ContactsPanel.deleteTemplate, leaving members' `templateId` dangling): contact applies MUST use the pitfall-#36 blessed path (`saveContacts` + `setContacts` together), which the `SlashContext` built in `runSlashLine` does — don't hand a future executor a raw contacts write. **Toasts (§37.6):** `showToast()` in [toasts.ts](src/renderer/toasts.ts) (no-dep, CustomEvent) → [ToastHost.tsx](src/renderer/components/ToastHost.tsx) mounted once per window in App. Use toasts for app-level/background notices (quota failures, transfer results); use in-flow `internal-system` lines for command feedback. Never `window.alert` from the renderer (it freezes the whole window mid-play; `safeSetItem`'s quota warning is the precedent conversion).

### Profile system (DESIGN.md §20)
YAML files in `app.getPath('userData')/profiles/` — `%APPDATA%\lichborne\profiles\` in production (lowercase — `app.getName()` reads the package.json `name` field, NOT `build.productName`). `ensureProfilesDir()` in [profiles.ts](src/main/profiles.ts) is the canonical accessor. Two-stage migration (NSIS `preInit` + runtime fallback) rescues pre-v0.6.4 install-dir profiles.

- **Per-character setting** — write to `scopedKey(character, 'myThing')` and call `saveProfile()`. The dynamic `state:` pipeline picks it up automatically. No type changes needed.
- **Shared setting** — must be added to `SharedProfile` type + `buildSharedProfile` + `importSharedProfile`. (v0.15.2 additions: `lastSessionCharacters` — the F62 "Reconnect Last" roster snapshot, written non-empty-only by the primary window; and the four F37 `shared*` global-rule lists, which bridge the `lichborne._global.*` localStorage keys — see the Automations global-rules bullet.)
- **Schema versioning** — both files declare `profileVersion`. Migrations registered in `profile-migrations.ts` by SOURCE version. Adding optional fields is NOT a breaking change. Future-version YAMLs are skipped (preserved on disk).
- **Backups** — timestamped `{name}.yaml.{ISO-ish}.bak`, rolling retention of 5.

### Profile Transfer (F38, v0.10.0)
Platform-wide character setup Export/Import. As of v0.10.0 this is the **single Lichborne↔Lichborne path** — it superseded the old Automations export (that Export button was removed, and the ImportWizard's "Lichborne" source card was removed; the Automations panel's Import button is now legacy-client only, "Import from another client…" — see the Import wizard section). Launcher top-bar **"Transfer"** button → one modal, Export / Import tabs ([ProfileTransferModal.tsx](src/renderer/components/ProfileTransferModal.tsx), core logic in [profileTransfer.ts](src/renderer/profileTransfer.ts)). Export picks ANY source character (reads its YAML `state`, works disconnected) and writes a `.lb.yaml` bundle into a new **`Exports/` folder** (sibling of `profiles/`, `getExportsDir`/`ensureExportsDir` in [profiles.ts](src/main/profiles.ts)). Import lists files from `Exports/` (+ Browse… dialog defaulting there) and fans out to multiple already-added characters via checkboxes. Files: `profile-transfer:*` IPC in [main.ts](src/main/main.ts).

- **A Transfer category needs THREE registrations, not one: the `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` entry, a slot in `applyProfileImport`'s `order` array, AND a switch case** — a category with only the entry exports fine and shows as a checkbox but silently applies NOTHING on import (the v0.14.0 Experiences category shipped exactly that; caught + fixed v0.14.6 while adding the Named Colors category). **Shared-data categories** (Theme's `myThemes`, Named Colors' `customColors`) are target-character-independent — they merge into the SHARED stores and rely on the modal's post-import `_shared.yaml` flush; don't route them through the per-character `store`.
- **What transfers is an explicit allowlist** — `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` in [profileTransfer.ts](src/renderer/profileTransfer.ts). Ten categories grouping exact `state` suffixes: Display & Accessibility (`settings` minus `panelFontSizes`), Panel Layout (zone added-flags / tabs / activeIds / heights / `panelWidth` / `panelFontSizes`), Panel View Preferences (`mapViewMode`, `lichMapScale`, `streamTimestamps`, `scriptPalette`, exp prefs), Theme (top-level `theme` + shared custom theme), and Highlights / Triggers / Macros / Aliases / Groups & Modes / Contacts. **Deliberately excluded**: `seededRepeatMacros` / `seededNumpadMovement` / `mainTopMigrated` (internal one-time flags), `discoveredStreams` (ephemeral), `commandHistory` (character history, the `automationStats` precedent), `activeGroupStates` / `activeModeId` (only on Replace). **When you add a new per-character setting, decide if it belongs in a category here and add it** — settings default to NOT transferred until listed (safe default; a forgotten key is a papercut, never a target-breaker).
- **Non-destructive by construction** — import writes ONLY into the target's `state` map (per-key) + top-level `theme`. Identity/launcher top-level fields (`account`, `character`, `game`, `useLich`, `hidden`, `favorite`, `guild`, `circle`, `notes`, `profileVersion`) are never in `state`, so they're structurally unreachable.
- **Active vs inactive targets** — see pitfall #56. Inactive → YAML read-merge-write. Active (focused OR backgrounded session) → write localStorage working copy + remount the session via App's per-session reload nonce. **LB** is the project's short branding abbreviation (used in the `.lb.yaml` extension).

### Map system (DESIGN.md §19)
Two views: **Lich Map** (Lich image tiles) and **Genie Maps** (Genie XML-driven graph). Genie XML is the spatial source of truth for the graph view — coordinates come directly from the hand-curated XML files; no auto-layout, no BFS placement, no zone stitching. One zone visible at a time, picked by the dropdown or auto-switched when the player's room title matches a room in another loaded zone.

**Two prior approaches have been deleted; do not reintroduce.** The per-zone Genie Graph (`MapGraphView.tsx`, deleted v0.6.3) tried to render zones individually with the old augmentation matcher. The Lich-native BFS view (`LichGraphView.tsx` + `lichLayout.ts`, deleted v0.6.6) tried to make every Lich room renderable by inferring layout from `wayto` cardinals — but Genie's hand-curated coords and Lich's directional walks disagree in dense clusters, producing "type west, marker goes north" misrenders.

**Rendering matches Genie's `MapForm.cs` exactly.** 8×8 node rects are CENTERED on the XML position because Genie's `ConvertPoint(pos, 4)` SUBTRACTS the offset (MapForm.cs:187–193). Arc endpoints go through the XML position directly. Labels at `(pos + 1, pos + 1)` matching `DrawString(r.X + 1, r.Y + 1)`. Getting any of this wrong visibly misaligns label clusters; verify against the reference source instead of guessing.

**Arcs render in two passes** for dense-cluster legibility: under-pass at full opacity (drawn before nodes; lines disappear into rect fills inside clusters) + over-pass at 0.35 opacity drawn on top (faint trace across rects so you can follow a line all the way to its endpoint). Each pass collapses N arcs into 3 `<path>` elements (one per cardinal/climb/go category) via concatenated `M x,y L x,y` segments; same data, render twice, ~6 SVG elements total.

**Cross-zone stubs** are 1-room boundary markers with `note="MapXX_Name.xml"`. `isStubNode(n)` detects `.xml` in note aliases. Title lookup MUST prefer non-stub matches (otherwise the marker in zone A wins over the real room in zone B) — and it merges `byTitle ∪ byNormalized` *before* the non-stub filter, so a `byTitle`-only stub can't trap the match when the real room is reachable through the normalized form (B78).

**Ambiguous-title disambiguation — the Genie matcher (v0.7.0; exits + inline-desc capture + pure-resolver rewrite v0.11.7 — see pitfall #70 for the full story).** Same-titled rooms (a Barrows zone has 40+ "Whistling Wood, Barrows" nodes; the Crossing has 7 "Moonstone Street") are resolved by a **module-level PURE function `resolveGenieRoom(pool, normDesc, liveExits, prev, sourceFileToZoneId, staleCount)`** ([GenieMapView.tsx](src/renderer/components/panels/GenieMapView.tsx)), driven from a SINGLE effect that owns the breadcrumb (`prevLocationRef`) and the cross-zone hold counter (`staleCountRef`). **It is NOT a `useMemo`** — the old impure memo mutated those refs as it computed and double-counted under React StrictMode (dev), so it was rewritten; `pool` (the title-matched candidate list) stays a pure memo, but the stateful resolve lives in the effect (`currentLocation` is `useState`). This mirrors how GenieMaps' own client matches (NAME + EXIT-SET + DESCRIPTION — `Node.Compare`/`CardinalCount`, NodeList.cs). Resolution ladder: (1) single candidate; (2) **description-EXACT** unique; (3) **exit-set EQUALITY** unique; (4) **description-SUBSTRING** unique (≥24 chars, B148/B150); (5) **graph adjacency** over the FULL pool — the candidate joined by a Genie arc to `prev` (the last resolved room), preferring an exit-matched neighbour; (5b) cross-zone stub adjacency; (6) **exit-aware conservative cross-zone hold** (B110) — commits to the new-zone guess when it's exit-corroborated OR `prev`'s exits no longer match the live exits, else holds `prev` (3-strike escape); (7) file order last resort. **Two signals carry it:** the inline `<preset id='roomDesc'>` description is now captured into `roomState.desc` every look/move (pitfall #70) so the desc tiers actually fire, and the **exit set** (always-fresh, the game sends the compass every room) tracks the marker *while running* when DR hasn't re-sent a description. **Exits are ADDITIVE — never a pre-filter that removes candidates before adjacency** (that excludes the correct neighbour when Genie exit data is imperfect → marker strands; this was the v0.11.7 regression). The Lich Map's `findRoom` ([mapTypes.ts](src/renderer/components/panels/mapTypes.ts)) carries the same exact-then-substring desc logic (B150) and benefits from the inline-desc capture too. **The two maps differ in their PRIMARY signal:** the Lich Map matches by **room id first** (`lichDb.get(roomId)`, exact/robust — the parser reads the Simu room-id-flag `[Title] (id)` format, pitfall #65) and falls to title+desc when the id is absent; the Genie Map has **no room ids in its data**, so it is **title + description + exits** (exits make it track reliably while running, not "always degrading"). Matching is per-session/state-driven (MapPanel gets each GameWindow's own `roomState.{title,desc,exits,roomId}`, gated on the per-character `showMapOverlay`, NOT `isActive`) so it tracks for active AND backgrounded characters; only the camera/layout is active-gated (pitfall #24).

**Click model (v0.6.8): left-click pins, right-click walks.** Left-click a regular room → toggles a pinned gold BFS path (no walking). Left-click a stub → switches the displayed zone to its target XML. Right-click anything → walks (BFS in-zone, `sendWalkPath`). The map only auto-switches zones when the player's `roomTitle` actually lands in the new zone — never on walk completion (the game can block any command; racing the map ahead strands the user).

**Camera follow-the-player** uses `useLayoutEffect`, not `useEffect`, so the transform update lands in the same paint frame as the indicator's new world position. Default ON; manual pan/zoom turns it off; the ◆ button re-enables. Always-center model (not margin-snap). The follow effect gates on `followNode` — the *same* `visibleById.get(...)` lookup the indicator uses — so "marker visible" and "camera following" can't desync.

**Smooth camera motion.** Pan group is positioned with the CSS `transform` *property* (not the SVG attribute) so `.genie-pan-smooth` can `transition` it (`150ms linear` — linear, not ease-out, because a follow camera re-targets every step and ease-out's velocity reset pulses visibly). `snapTransform` (delta > 600px or > 20% scale vs last-painted transform) drops the transition for big jumps so zone switches / ◆ / fit cut instantly. The indicator carries the *same* transition + snap flag so it stays screen-centred during walks instead of bouncing. Gated on the `mapAnimations` setting (default ON): pan group + indicator only get `.genie-pan-smooth` when `!isDragging && mapAnimations`. (v0.6.8–v0.6.11 gated this on a separate `smoothScroll` setting; v0.6.12 removed that and folded the map glide under `mapAnimations`.)

**Current/selected/hover/hover-path/pinned-path indicators are hoisted OUT of `nodeRects`** as single overlay elements. Pre-hoist, walking re-built the entire `nodeRects` JSX every step. The current-room indicator is a sonar locator: two `genie-here-ping` expanding rings + the solid `INDICATOR_R` ring; the pings are exempt from the animation-pause via a higher-specificity rule.

**Per-color effect system (v0.6.7).** Every COLOR_LEGEND category has its own visual signature (heartbeat for Healer, coin glint for Shop, ripples for Water, leaves for Lumberjacking, dirt for Mining + Trailhead, vortex/drift/rise sparkles for the magical 4, etc.). The structure is uniform — adding a new effect is a 4-step pattern: (1) declare a `*_COLORS` set or extend `MOTE_EFFECTS`, (2) add a memo at the appropriate place in the component that builds the SVG elements per visible-node match, (3) add a CSS keyframe in `map-panel.css`, (4) render the memo at the correct layer in the SVG tree. Stub `↗` glyph always wins over category glyphs (cross-zone identity > resource category). `getMoteContrastColor(hex)` picks mote fills based on room luminance (light bg → dark motes, dark bg → light motes). `normalizeNodeColor()` in `parseGenieZone` converts CSS color names (`"Blue"`, `"Red"`, etc.) to canonical hex so downstream effect lookups don't silently miss rooms.

**Animation pause — two freeze classes (v0.6.7, extended v0.6.9).** The pan group `<g>` carries ONE of two mutually-exclusive freeze classes, both cascading `animation-play-state: paused` to descendants:
- `genie-pan-dragging` — *transient* freeze when `isDragging || inMotion`. `isDragging` flips on mousedown/up; `inMotion` flips true on any `currentLocation` change and resets a `MOTION_QUIET_MS = 800` timer. The locator sonar ping is **exempt** (`.genie-pan-dragging .genie-here-ping` keeps it running) — you still want to see yourself mid-walk.
- `genie-anim-off` — *permanent* freeze when `settings.mapAnimations` is off (default ON). **No ping exemption** — "off" stops the ping too.
The className picks one or the other (`!mapAnimations ? 'genie-anim-off' : (isDragging||inMotion) ? 'genie-pan-dragging' : ''`) so the ping-pause and ping-exemption rules never collide.

**Category effects are OMITTED (not paused) and CAPPED (v0.7.0).** Two layers of defense, both because SVG CSS animations are expensive — each animated element forces Recalculate Style every frame and is a compositor-layer candidate:
- *Omitted during motion.* `animation-play-state: paused` stops an animation advancing but leaves the element layer-promoted — profiling during travel showed residual Layerize ~21% even with effects "frozen". So the 10 animated per-category effect groups (sparkles, heartbeats, coin glints, ripples, bubbles, caution/implode rings, leaf/dirt falls, XP rises) render only when `showEffects = mapAnimations && !isDragging && !inMotion`. During travel/pan/off they're not in the DOM at all. They re-mount once the player has been still for `MOTION_QUIET_MS` (1500ms — long enough that normal sub-second running cadence never re-mounts mid-run; a short window would tear them up and down every step).
- *Capped to the nearest N rooms.* Idle in a dense zone (the Crossing) all effects on was ~29% Recalculate Style. The effect memos iterate `nearbyNodes`, not `visibleNodes` — `EFFECT_CAP` (30) rooms nearest the player (or zone-centre when viewing a zone you're not in), or the stable `EMPTY_NODES` ref when `!showEffects`. So at most ~30 rooms animate regardless of zone density, and the effect memos don't recompute during travel (dep is the unchanging `EMPTY_NODES`). **`auras` deliberately still uses `visibleNodes`** — they're static (no animation, no per-frame cost) and they ARE the colour map.

The freeze classes still cover what *stays* rendered (the sonar ping, the static/fire auras). Node **hover** is likewise suppressed during motion (`onNodeHoverEnter` checks `inMotionRef`) — the map scrolling under a stationary cursor otherwise fires a storm of pointer enter/leave → re-renders.

**`mapAnimations` setting (v0.6.9; sole map-motion switch as of v0.6.12).** `mapAnimations` (default ON) is the single toggle for ALL Genie map motion — the per-color category effects AND the camera glide. Off → `genie-anim-off` freezes effects and the glide is disabled (camera snaps). Per-character `AppSettings` field, persists via the dynamic profile `state:` pipeline, threads `GameWindow → PanelFrame → MapPanel → GenieMapView` (the `autoLinkUrls` path). (v0.6.9 also had a `smoothScroll` setting; removed v0.6.12 with the story-window smooth scroll.)

**Genie parse cache (v0.6.7).** First-time parse of a 122-XML maps folder takes several seconds (DOMParser is synchronous and chunky). `genie-cache:load` / `genie-cache:save` IPC handlers in `main.ts` serialize the parsed `Map<zoneId, GenieZone>` to `userData/genie-cache.json`. Subsequent launches verify a fingerprint (sorted `filename:mtimeMs:size`) against current folder state and skip re-parsing if it matches — load drops from seconds to ~50ms. Version field (`GENIE_CACHE_VERSION`) lets us invalidate every user's cache when the GenieZone shape changes without manual cleanup. Cache write is fire-and-forget after parse.

Files: [MapPanel.tsx](src/renderer/components/panels/MapPanel.tsx), [MapImageView.tsx](src/renderer/components/panels/MapImageView.tsx), [GenieMapView.tsx](src/renderer/components/panels/GenieMapView.tsx), [mapTypes.ts](src/renderer/components/panels/mapTypes.ts).

### Theme system (DESIGN.md §6)
~150 CSS custom properties in `themes.ts`. `darkBase` is the canonical full set; every other theme is a partial override merged over `darkBase` in `applyTheme` / `applyCustomTheme`. Theme Editor (`ThemeEditor.tsx`) uses a `TABS` declarative schema — new variables surface there (it exposes ONLY the general vars, not specialty ones like `--map-*`). **The structural automap colors (`--map-bg/chrome-bg/text/text-muted/border/border-subtle/btn-bg/btn-border/select-bg/node-fill/node-stroke/dot`) are NOT per-theme — they live in `MAP_STRUCTURAL_CASCADE` (one block wired to the general palette: `--map-bg`→`var(--bg-app)`, `--map-text`→`var(--text-secondary)`, …) which is spread into `darkBase` AND re-applied LAST in both `applyTheme`/`applyCustomTheme`, so the map always follows App Background / Game Text / borders on every theme and live-updates in the editor (B161). Only the SEMANTIC map cues stay per-theme: `--map-arc-*` (directional path lines), `--map-current-color` (the "you-are-here" marker), `--map-select-color`. Don't pin a structural `--map-*` in a theme — it's inert (the force-apply overrides it); see pitfall #75.**

### Automations, groups, modes (DESIGN.md §8)
Highlights, triggers, macros, aliases, contact templates, **and mutes** share a `groupIds: string[]` + `allGroups: boolean` shape. `isRuleActive(rule, activeGroups)` gates them. New rule types should follow this pattern and default to `allGroups: true`.

- **Global cross-character rules (F37, v0.15.2 — DESIGN §39).** Highlights/triggers/macros/aliases/**mutes/substitutes** (all six rule types; mutes/subs joined at Sekmeht's ask, same release) can also live in a GLOBAL store that applies to every character: the **virtual `_global` character scope** (`GLOBAL_RULES_SCOPE` + `asGlobalRules` in [characterScope.ts](src/renderer/characterScope.ts)). The rule stores/panels work on it UNCHANGED (they only see `scopedKey`); the disk bridge is **`_shared.yaml`** (`SharedProfile.sharedHighlights/Triggers/Macros/Aliases`, raw-key read/write in profile.ts), NOT a character YAML. GameWindow merges globals AFTER the character's lists at each engine input (**character-first** — ties/key/prefix conflicts resolve to the character's rule), normalized **always-active** (groups are per-character; the editors take a `hideGroups` prop in Global scope). Live sync = `lichborne:global-rules-changed` custom event (same window) + `storage` events on the `lichborne._global.` prefix (cross-window). The AutomationsPanel header's "This Character | All Characters" switch re-points a `CharacterProvider` at `_global`; the analytics prune counts global ids as live (fires record under each character). **When adding a rule-consuming feature, decide whether it reads the merged list (engines do) or the character list (editors/saves do) — merged arrays are DERIVED, never saved.** Global contacts are deliberately NOT built (presence tracking mutates contacts at runtime — a shared store races across windows; needs its own design). No slash `global` flag yet (recorded, §39.5). **F63 (same release, DESIGN §39.6–39.7):** each of the four editors has an **"Applies to" scope-MOVE control** (rendered only when AutomationsPanel passes `onMoveScope` — the storage stays two stores, the toggle is a deliberate move; content-identical targets → source removed + toast, never a duplicate); rule content-identity lives in [ruleIdentity.ts](src/renderer/ruleIdentity.ts) — **ONE definition shared by the move, Transfer's append-dedup, and Transfer's global-awareness; change identity semantics there, nowhere else.** Transfer has a merge-only "Global Rules" shared category (`globalRules` — runs FIRST among rule categories so the per-character global-dup filter sees the merged store), and all six per-character rule categories skip incoming rules already present in the destination's global store (both merge modes). **The header scope switch renders on EVERY Automations tab** — greyed + tooltip on Groups (the only non-capable tab) — so header buttons never shift position between tabs (Sekmeht's disabled-in-place-beats-disappearing call; apply it to future header controls).

- **Automation Analytics — usage stats + health, off by default (v0.14.4, DESIGN §36).** A self-tuning layer over the user's OWN native automations (display/config — not a Lich concern). One **app-wide master toggle** (`SharedProfile.automationAnalytics`, mirrors `bulkConnectSeparateWindows` — localStorage working copy `lichborne.automationAnalytics` + a same-window `lichborne:analytics-changed` custom event the GameWindow's `analyticsEnabledRef` listens for, because a cross-window `storage` event never fires in the writing window). **Two layers:** (a) **static health** — pure analyzers in [automationHealth.ts](src/renderer/automationHealth.ts) (`analyzeHighlights/Triggers/Macros/Aliases/Mutes/Substitutes` → broken / duplicate / no-op / **key-or-name conflict**), reusing the existing `buildXRegex` so "broken" means exactly "won't compile"; (b) **runtime usage** — per-rule fire counts + lastFired in [automationStats.ts](src/renderer/automationStats.ts) (`recordFire`, in-memory cache + 800ms debounced flush, per-character `scopedKey('automationStats')` → rides `state.*` into the profile YAML for free, **excluded from Profile Transfer** as character history). **Storage is bounded — two rules.** The flush is **try/catch'd, NOT `safeSetItem`** (background telemetry must never throw or alert the user — a quota-failed stats write just skips; the live cache keeps the count). And the only unbounded vector — `recordFire` keys by `ruleId` and never deletes an entry, so a DELETED rule's stats would linger forever (worse on re-imports, which mint new nanoid ids) — is closed by **`pruneStats(character, liveIds)`**, called from AutomationsPanel's mount when analytics is on: it drops every stats entry whose id isn't in the union of all six current rule lists, so the map is bounded by the live rule count (Sekmeht: "I don't want this to bloat anywhere"). The map is ONE flat id→stat record across all six types, which is why the prune needs the union of all six `loadX(character)` id sets, not one panel's. **Reset + prune persist to YAML, not just localStorage.** `resetStats` writes an empty map and `pruneStats` shrinks it in localStorage — but YAML is the truth that re-seeds localStorage on next connect (`importCharacterProfile` copies every `state` key back), so a clear that never reached YAML would re-appear next launch. Both therefore trigger the panel's `onSaved` (→ scheduled profile save, flushed on shutdown): `useRuleAnalytics(…, onSaved)`'s `reset` calls it after `resetStats`; AutomationsPanel calls it when `pruneStats` returns `>0`. The stats flush is `try/catch'd` not `safeSetItem` (background telemetry never alerts/throws). **The runtime hooks ride EXISTING per-line work (pitfall #82) — gated on `analyticsEnabledRef.current`:** triggers piggyback `triggerCallbacks.onFire` (already per-rule); highlights ride the Debug fire-scan (`logHighlightFiresRef` gate widened to `showDebug || analytics`); mutes/subs report via an optional `onFired(ruleId)` added to `applyMutesToSegments`/`applySubstitutesToSegments`; macros/aliases count at resolve time (`resolveMacro`/`resolveAlias` now return `ruleId`). **OFF → zero added cost.** UI: shared [AutomationAnalytics.tsx](src/renderer/components/AutomationAnalytics.tsx) (`useRuleAnalytics` hook + `RuleBadges` per-row + `AnalyticsReview` banner) — the master toggle is in the AutomationsPanel header, each sub-panel wraps its body in an `.aa-host` column with a **full-width** Review banner above the list (NOT in the ~210px sidebar — it was unreadable there), the Review is **collapsible per-category** (each issue type a `<details>`, capped at 200 rendered entries — a real ruleset has 1000s of duplicates), jump links call the panel's real `selectRule`/`selectAlias`/`selectMacro` (NOT bare `setSelectedId` — the detail pane renders off the `draft` that the selector sets), and the **"Remove duplicate copies"** bulk action (keep one of each set) lives in the Duplicate section. `useRuleAnalytics` live-refreshes every 2s while open (recordFire MUTATES the cached stats object in place, so the panel needs a periodic re-read or counts never update / Reset looks dead). **When adding a new rule type, add an `analyzeX` + thread the runtime hook; keep all six in sync.**

- **Mutes & Substitutes — two display-layer rule types (DESIGN.md §31, v0.12.0).** **Two separate Automations tabs** ("Mutes" → [MutePanel.tsx](src/renderer/components/MutePanel.tsx), "Substitutes" → [SubstitutesPanel.tsx](src/renderer/components/SubstitutesPanel.tsx); Sekmeht chose separate top-level tabs over one nested "Text Modification" tab) that act on incoming main-window game text. Both are **native, NOT delegated to Lich `textsubs.lic`** (display concern; must work without Lich per Principle #2; portable via Profile Transfer; clean import target). Same shape as highlights (`scopedKey('mutes')` / `scopedKey('substitutes')`, ride the `state.*` map, **no profile-shape change**); compiled+group-gated into `activeMutesRef`/`activeSubsRef`; applied by **GameWindow's `applyTextMods` — mute → substitute → (highlight at render)** — DISPLAY ONLY (the Session Log captured the raw line per-event upstream, so neither loses history). **Stream scope = GLOBAL by default** (the pass runs over `newMain` AND every `newStream[key]` buffer; Sekmeht's call = Genie's global model), with an **optional per-rule `stream` restrict** (Frostbite's `target`): a rule applies everywhere unless `rule.stream` is set, then only to that stream (`!rule.stream || rule.stream === streamId`). The editors' **"Apply to"** dropdown (`STREAM_OPTIONS` in mutes.ts) sets it; we do NOT auto-skip Thoughts (unlike Genie). **On IMPORT, substitutes come in GLOBAL** (no per-rule stream — "substitute wherever the text shows up", the Genie model; Sekmeht 2026-06-08); the per-rule restrict exists for users who want it, but nothing auto-scopes on import. (An earlier experiment scoped Frostbite's `target` to streams and special-cased an `exp` pseudo-stream so mind-state subs could fire on the skill readout — **all reverted**: see the mind-state note in the import bullet for why those are unsupported instead.) Transferable via **separate `mutes` + `substitutes` categories** in `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES`. **Right-click menu** ([ContextMenu.tsx](src/renderer/components/ContextMenu.tsx) now supports **nested submenus** — hover-expand, viewport-flipping + the root-menu viewport clamp): the game-window menu groups display-changing actions under **`Modify Text ▸`** (Highlight / Mute / Substitute, each ×"word"/"this line") and automation under **`Trigger ▸`**, then Show in Log / Clear — four short root rows instead of ten flat ones (Sekmeht's framing: "modify the text" vs "build something from the text").
