  - **Mute** (renamed "Gag/Ignore" — friendlier) removes matching text, with a **`scope` like highlights**: `line` (default — drop the whole line, the typical gag) or `match` (strip only the matched text — e.g. mute a name without nuking the room you're in). `applyMutesToSegments` ([mutes.ts](src/renderer/mutes.ts), global regex): `line`→`null` (drop TextLine), `match`→`replace(re,'')` per-segment **+ tidies the whitespace gap** (collapse double-space, drop space-before-punct, trim seams) so `…healer Quentin.`→`…healer.`. **Right-click** (like Highlight/Trigger): `Mute "word"` (new `match` mute) / `Mute this line` (new `line` mute) → `openMuteEditor` → `mutePrefill` → AutomationsPanel `mutes` tab opens an unsaved draft.
  - **Substitute** rewrites matched text → `replacement` (native JS `$N`/`$&` capture refs). `applySubstitutesToSegments` ([substitutes.ts](src/renderer/substitutes.ts)), per-segment, after mutes/before highlights. Game-state vars NOT interpolated (capture groups only — what the source clients use). **Right-click** `Substitute "word"` / `Substitute this line` → `openSubstituteEditor` → `substitutePrefill` → Substitutes tab opens an unsaved draft (empty replacement to fill in).
  - **Import** (the count-only "belongs in Lich" notices are gone; terminology: **Mute = Wrayth `<ignores>` = Genie `gags.cfg` = Frostbite `ignores.ini`**; **Substitute = Genie `substitutes.cfg` = Frostbite `substitutes.ini`**, Wrayth has none): Mutes from all three (Genie `#gag`/`#ignore`, Frostbite `[ignore]`, Wrayth `<h>` inside `<ignores>`); Substitutes from Genie `#sub`/`#subs`/`#substitute` (regex, `$N` kept) and Frostbite `[substitution]` (regex, `\N`/`\0`→`$N`/`$&`, via `unescapeQtRegex` — NOT `unescapeQtIniValue`, whose punctuation-collapse would mangle regex escapes like `\(`). Each gets its own preview tab. **Imported substitutes are GLOBAL** (no stream scope — Genie model). **EXCEPTION: Frostbite `target=Experience` subs are flagged `unsupported`** (shown greyed in the preview with a note, NOT imported by default): these are the mind-state numbering rules (`(clear)`→` 0 $1`, `(very rapt)`→` 31 $1`, …) for Frostbite's dedicated Experience WINDOW. Lichborne shows the skill readout in the **main window already space-aligned**, so substituting a variable-width number (1-digit `0` vs 2-digit `31`) into it **breaks the table's column alignment** — and the patterns are bare words (`(clear)` has no boundary) so applying them globally also mauls normal prose. Flagging unsupported (detected by `target === 'Experience'` in `parseSubstitutes`) was Sekmeht's call after we tried & **reverted** an `exp`-pseudo-stream approach (storm-gray/frostbite: 89 subs → 54 ready + 35 unsupported). The precise `target=Main` damage/protection subs (lookahead-anchored, `poor → poor (2/27)`) import normally as global and fire fine. **Frostbite array sections iterate actual indices, not `size=N`** (stale-size, pitfall #73). Imported rules **persist exactly like highlights** — `saveMutes`/`saveSubstitutes` are byte-identical to `saveHighlights`, and the wizard's `onSaved` chains to GameWindow's `setMutes`/`setSubstitutes` reload + `scheduleProfileSave` → YAML. **Each AutomationsPanel tab panel loads its rule list once on mount (`useState(() => loadX(character))`), so after an import it would show STALE/empty until a tab switch remounts it** — fixed by an `importNonce` in [AutomationsPanel.tsx](src/renderer/components/AutomationsPanel.tsx) that bumps on the wizard's `onSaved` and is part of every tab panel's `key`, forcing a remount+reload on import ONLY (a panel's own edits don't bump it, so editing never resets its UI). **The key MUST be tab-unique (`` key={`${panelType}-${importNonce}`} ``), NOT a bare `importNonce`:** Macros and Aliases are the SAME component (`MacrosPanel`, differing only by `initialTab`, which `useState` reads once on mount), so a shared `key={importNonce}` let React reuse the one instance across those two tabs and the Macros tab rendered Alias content. Any new AutomationsPanel tab needs `` key={`<type>-${importNonce}`} `` too.

- **Highlight overlap resolution = SPECIFICITY + per-property compositing (v0.11.3, the Profanity model).** In [renderSegmentFull.tsx](src/renderer/utils/renderSegmentFull.tsx): contacts still beat highlights (B116); among match-scope highlights covering a run, each visual property (text color / background / bold / glow) is taken INDEPENDENTLY from the **smallest (most-specific) covering highlight that sets it** — so a word-highlight's color punches through a broad phrase highlight while the phrase's background still shows, and a bold-only/bg-only highlight layers onto another's fg. Equal-length ties go to the first-encountered (top-of-list) highlight (deterministic, unlike Profanity's arbitrary unstable sort). **This replaced v0.11.2's "first/top-of-list wins, all-or-nothing" model** after the cross-client research below (Sekmeht's call: specificity is more dynamic and doesn't force users to manage list order at scale). Consequences: the `HighlightRule.priority` field stays **vestigial**, and there is **deliberately NO reorder UI** in HighlightsPanel — a v0.11.2 ▲/▼ reorder control was added then **removed in v0.11.3** because list order no longer determines precedence (it would falsely imply a priority mechanism; specificity does the work, and ties fall to first-in-array silently). Line-scope highlights use a separate path (`getLineHighlightStyle`, first-match) but are NOT just a container tint: **a line-scope highlight's TEXT COLOR must override preset/fg segment colors** (B200, Cherisse — otherwise a "Line — entire line is styled" highlight is invisible on thoughts/speech/lnet/substituted lines, because `[data-preset]` colors the segment and a child's explicit color beats the container's inherited one). The line color is threaded down as an `overrideColor` param to `renderSegment`/`renderSegmentFull` (applied at the 2 line-render sites — `TextLineRow`, which covers the main window + all stream panels, and `RoomPanel`); the non-match runs render it inline (beating the no-`!important` `[data-preset]` CSS), keeping the preset's bg/italic + bold/links; match-scope runs still punch through with their own color; contacts keep their template color (B116). bg-only line highlights leave text colors alone (only `color` is threaded). If you change the property-resolution, keep the merge `key` in sync (adjacent runs merge only when the composite key matches).
- **Highlight overlap resolution across front-ends (research, v0.11.3 — TheTargonian's question "the higher in the list wins? is that how Genie does it?").** There is **no single convention**; the four DR/GS front-ends use three different models, along TWO axes. *Axis 1 — what decides precedence:* **Wrayth & Frostbite = list position, BOTTOM wins** (last/lowest in the list supersedes; Frostbite verified in [highlighter.cpp](file:///c:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/gui/text/highlight/highlighter.cpp) — it walks the list top→bottom inserting nested HTML `<span>`s, so the innermost/last color wins; user-reorderable). **Genie = pattern text, sorted** (its `HighlightList`/`HighlightRegExpList` are `SortedList`s keyed by the pattern string — [Globals.cs](file:///c:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Lists/Globals.cs), applied in [ComponentRichTextBox.cs](file:///c:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Forms/Components/ComponentRichTextBox.cs) via `SelectionColor=`; last-applied in sorted order wins, NOT user-orderable). **Profanity = specificity, smallest match wins** ([highlight_processor.rb](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/highlight_processor.rb): per segment, `color_list.sort_by { |h| h[:end]-h[:start] }` then takes the first non-nil — smallest/most-specific range wins; ties arbitrary via Ruby's unstable sort; NOT user-orderable). **Lichborne v0.11.2 was list position, TOP wins** (the outlier direction). *Axis 2 — all-or-nothing vs per-property compositing:* Profanity, Frostbite, and Genie all resolve **fg / bg / underline INDEPENDENTLY** (a small fg-only highlight punches its color through a broad bg-only highlight; the two compose — red text on the broad highlight's yellow bg). v0.11.2 Lichborne was the only all-or-nothing one. **DECISION (v0.11.3): Lichborne adopted Profanity's model — specificity (smallest match wins) + per-property compositing** (the bullet above is the live behavior). Rationale: it's the most dynamic, handles overlaps well WITHOUT forcing users to maintain a precedence order (which Sekmeht judged unmanageable at scale). We diverge from Profanity in ONE detail: equal-length ties are deterministic (first/top-of-list) rather than arbitrary. We did NOT adopt Wrayth/Frostbite bottom-wins or Genie pattern-sort.
- **Built-in variable catalog (v0.11.2 expansion).** Trigger/macro/alias `$var` interpolation resolves from `buildVars` ([useTriggerEngine.ts](src/renderer/hooks/useTriggerEngine.ts)) and `buildMacroVars` ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)) — these MUST stay in sync, and the editor display lists (`INTERPOLATABLE_VARS` in [triggers.ts](src/renderer/triggers.ts), `MACRO_VARS`/`ALIAS_VARS` in [macros.ts](src/renderer/macros.ts)) MUST be updated when you add one. Current set: regex groups (`$0/$match`, numbered `$1..`, **named** `(?<who>…)→$who`), `$line`, `$characterName`, `$date`/`$time`/`$timestamp`, vitals (`$health/$mana/$stamina/$spirit/$concentration`), `$rt`, `$ct`/`$casttime`, `$stance`, `$spell`/`$preparedspell`, `$left`/`$right`, `$room`/`$roomname`, `$roomid`, `$exits`, and indicator booleans (`$bleeding/$poisoned/$diseased/$stunned/$webbed/$joined/$hidden/$invisible/$dead`). Sources are live per-session state (`triggerCtxRef`), so adding one = thread the value into `TriggerGameState` + the GameWindow event handler that populates `triggerCtxRef` + both var-builders + the display lists. Unknown `$foo` interpolates to the literal `$foo` (working-as-intended). No profile-shape change — these are read-only resolution sources.

### Login & character-selection flow (v0.8.0, DESIGN.md §13.6)
Empty state and "+" tab open `Launcher.tsx` + `AddCharacterWizard.tsx`, not `LoginScreen.tsx` (kept only as type-host for `SessionInfo`). `LichSetupFields.tsx` is the single source of truth for Lich path/port/frontend editing — its render sites are `LichSetupDialog.tsx` (shared by the Launcher's ⚙ button **and** the Settings panel as of v0.9.2 — Settings launches the dialog via an "Open Lich Setup…" button rather than embedding the fields) and the legacy `LoginScreen`. All wrap it in `.login-form` for CSS scoping. The XML-stream-mode dropdown is labeled **"Lich Frontend"** (v0.9.2) — Lich's own term: each `--stormfront`/`--wizard`/`--avalon`/`--frostbite`/`--genie` flag sets `$frontend` in Lich's `argv_options.rb`. The stored field is still `lichMode`; only the label changed.

- **Launcher rendering rules** are documented in DESIGN.md §13.6. Key invariants: Favorites is always-open; per-account sections default collapsed but **single-account is always expanded** and **freshly-added accounts auto-expand once** (wizard writes the account name to `lichborne.launcher.expandedAccounts` before `onCompleted` bumps `refreshKey`, and Launcher's refresh effect re-reads it).
- **AddCharacterWizard is account-driven, not character-driven** (v0.8.0). Step 1 collects account/password/game; step 2 runs `eaccessFetchCharacters` (mode-agnostic SimuCo auth, no Lich needed) and bulk-writes one stub `CharacterProfile` per checked discovered character. Existing profiles are listed but disabled. No connection happens in the wizard — tiles appear, user clicks Connect when ready.
- **Per-tile state is launcher-owned and writes immediately** via small read-modify-write helpers (`setCharacterFavorite`, `setCharacterGame`, `setCharacterUseLich`, `setCharacterHidden`, `patchCharacterProfile` for the notes editor). Never go through the GameWindow's debounced `scheduleProfileSave` for these — that's a different ownership track (see Pitfall #26 below).
- **Bulk Connect** ([BulkConnectPicker.tsx](src/renderer/components/BulkConnectPicker.tsx) + `runBulkConnect` in App.tsx) runs sequential per-account connects. DR's one-character-per-account rule forces this; sequential is also the simpler error-isolation model.
- **Same-account conflict** raises a confirmation modal (Cancel / Disconnect-and-continue) instead of refusing. The disconnect uses the awaitable `disconnect-await` IPC; the conflicting tab stays in the bar in disconnected state.
- **Shutdown** uses `gracefulDisconnect({ quickClose: true })` which calls `socket.end()` (guaranteed flush of QUIT) + force-close without waiting for server ack. ~300ms total regardless of session count. In-tab Disconnect and the conflict-modal auto-disconnect keep the full 5s ack-wait — they need the account slot confirmed released for the next action.

### Top chrome: app-bar, native menu & the menu-action bridge (v0.10.0, top-chrome redesign)
A tester-driven space-reclaim pass (TheTargonian, F39): Lichborne was showing ~3 fewer lines of game text than Frostbite because of stacked full-width chrome rows. Two reclaims shipped, plus a menu build-out.

- **Unified app-bar** ([AppBar.tsx](src/renderer/components/AppBar.tsx)) — one **app-level** row (rendered by AppShell when `!isEmpty`, replacing the old bare `CharacterTabBar` row) holding the **Lichborne brand + a connection status dot** (from the active session's `useSessions().status.connected`), the **character tabs** (composes `CharacterTabBar`), the **action buttons** (Debug/Logs/Panels/Maps/Contacts/Automations/Lich/Theme/Settings), and **Disconnect/Login**. The per-session `game-toolbar` that used to live inside every GameWindow is **gone** — that's the reclaimed row. This realizes DESIGN.md §13.3's original single-row intent (which had drifted to two rows). CSS in [app-bar.css](src/renderer/styles/app-bar.css); button/brand classes are shared from `game.css` (globally available in the bundle).
- **The menu-action / session-action bridge** is how app-level UI drives the **active** session. Native menu clicks (main process) → `menu-action` IPC → preload `onMenuAction` → `App`'s subscriber, which **splits**: session actions (`isSessionAction`, [src/shared/menuActions.ts](src/shared/menuActions.ts)) re-dispatch as a `lichborne:session-action` **DOM event**; app actions (login-character, bulk-connect, profile-export/import, quick-send, close/next/prev-character, check-updates) run in App via a latest-closure ref (so they see live `sessions`/`activeId`). The **app-bar buttons skip the IPC** and dispatch the DOM event directly (they're already in the renderer). The **active** GameWindow handles `lichborne:session-action` via a latest-closure ref (pitfall #31 pattern) guarded on `isActiveRef` — every mounted GameWindow hears it, only the active one acts. Each case mirrors what the old toolbar button did. Adding a new app-bar/menu action = add the string to `SESSION_ACTIONS`/`APP_ACTIONS` + a case in GameWindow's `runSessionActionRef` (session) or App's `runAppActionRef` (app).
- **ModeSwitcher moved to the Icon Bar** (its `trailing` slot) — it reads `useGroups()`, and `GroupsProvider` is **per-session inside GameWindow** (pitfall #6 isolation), so it can't live in the app-level bar. See pitfall #57. Its portal dropdown right-aligns / flips up / clamps to the viewport (it now sits at the row's right edge, possibly a bottom Icon Bar).
- **Native menu** ([main.ts](src/main/main.ts) `setupMenu`) is the full tree **File · Edit · View · Tools · Lich · Window · Help**; Lichborne items are click-only (hotkey policy in Operational guardrails). The Window menu also hosts the **decouple** items (Move Character to New Window / to Main Window, v0.11.0). `refreshMenuState()` scopes every Window-menu item to the **FOCUSED window's** owned-tab count (re-run from `sendStatus`/`createSession`/`destroySession` AND `win.on('focus')`): Next/Previous + Move-to-New need 2+ tabs in that window, Close needs 1+, Move-to-Main only enables in a secondary (decoupled) window — NOT global counts (that mis-shows items as enabled in separate-window mode). Disconnect/Login on the app-bar is driven by the active session's `connected` flag (`handleLoginActive` in App does destroy+remove+open-picker).
- **Compact vitals** (opt-in, `settings.compactVitals`) — dense half-height strip with acronym labels (DESIGN.md §5.1).
- **Done in v0.10.0 deferred-polish:** **(a)** per-button **active-state glow** — `SessionStatus` gained a `panel*` flag for EVERY toggle button (`panelDebug/panelLogs/panelMap/panelLich/panelManager/panelAutomations/panelSettings/panelContacts/panelTheme`, pushed by a GameWindow `updateStatus` effect), and AppBar applies the matching `btn-*--active` for the **active** session, so every panel/overlay button glows while its panel is open (inline ones + the four in the More menu; the ⋯ button glows when a hidden one is open). The `btn-*--active` styles for the buttons game.css didn't already cover (Panels/Automations/Settings) live in [app-bar.css](src/renderer/styles/app-bar.css). **(b)** a static **"More ⋯" dropdown** in AppBar holding the less-used buttons (Debug/Logs/Contacts/Theme) — inline buttons are Panels·Maps·Automations·Lich·Settings — so the bar stays usable on narrow windows with no width-measurement. **v0.13.4 (B178) extends this into a degradation ladder:** window `minWidth` is now **480** (users tile multiple windows), and em-based container-query tiers on `.app-bar` hide the wordmark + compact the buttons (≤ 71em), then fold the five inline buttons into the ⋯ menu (≤ 58em) via always-rendered CSS-gated twins (`app-bar-collapsible` / `app-bar-more-item--overflow`) — Disconnect/Login never collapses. The thresholds are em (container queries resolve em against the bar's game-font anchor) so they track the font setting; don't convert them to px media queries. **`container-type` makes the bar a STACKING CONTEXT** (layout containment), which buried the More dropdown under the game area (B179) — the bar carries `position: relative; z-index: 70` (content/WindowLayer ≤ 60, overlays ≥ 100) to lift its whole context; don't portal the menu instead (the `--overflow` items are gated by the bar's own `@container` query and a portal breaks descendance), and audit popovers any time you make an element a query container. **(c)** the vestigial GameWindow `status`/`scriptPalette` state was pruned (AppBar derives connection state from `useSessions`).
- **Still deferred:** Phase 3 (logo into the brand slot — Sekmeht parked it) and the **script palette** as a real future feature (its dead stub was removed, so build it fresh when wanted).

### Import wizard (DESIGN.md §15)
Wrayth XML / Genie .cfg / Frostbite .ini parse into a neutral `ImportCandidate` intermediate, then `mapper.ts` converts to native rules with `allGroups: true` and blank names. Per-client quirks under `src/renderer/import/`. Substitutions counted but not imported (F12). **Wrayth coverage was completed in v0.11.1 (B146, Thanator's real export):** highlights live in `<strings>` (NOT `<highlights>` — that block doesn't exist in Wrayth; the old parser silently imported zero), so `parseStrings` reads them as match-scope highlights colored via the `<palette>` (`@NN`→hex through `resolveWraythColor`). `<names>` → contacts AND per-color **contact templates** named `colorNN` (by palette index, stamped on `ImportHighlight.templateName`; the wizard's contacts-apply find-or-creates the template by name and assigns `templateId`). `<presets>` → `themeVars` via `parsePresets` (bold/speech/whisper/thought/roomName/command/link → CSS preset vars; `watching`/`selectedLink` skipped; `"skin"`/empty bg → none) feeding the existing "Imported from {source}" custom-theme path. Macros import from **all 10 sets** (was set 0 only) with cross-set key collisions flagged `partial` + an apply-time first-wins key dedup in `doImport` (Lichborne has one keybinding set). `<ignores>`(gags)/`<vars>` are count-only notes. Two layout/dedup traps fixed in the same pass — see pitfall #61. **Frostbite coverage was completed in v0.11.9 (B159, Rakkor's real `highlights.ini`):** highlights live in `[TextHighlight]` keyed `N\value`/`N\color`/`N\bgColor`/`N\options`/`N\alert`/`N\alertValue`/`N\timer`/`N\group`. Colours are Qt `@Variant(...)` QColor blobs (spec byte at index 4 must be `1`=RGB; channels are 16-bit, take the high byte; spec `0`=invalid=no bg). The **`options` field is a 5-bit QBitArray** whose meaning is taken verbatim from Frostbite's `highlighter.cpp`: bit0=entire-row (→ `scope:'line'`), bit1=partial-words (set→`phrase` substring, clear→`text` word-boundary), bit2=starting-with (whole-line submodifier, no LB equivalent), bit3=match-groups (per-capture-group colouring → flagged `partial`), bit4=case-insensitive (deliberately **ignored** — imports forced case-insensitive, Sekmeht's call). **`|` in a value is alternation** — `buildPattern` splits and emits a `regex` (each alt regex-escaped, wrapped `\b…\b` unless partial-match) so `A|B|C` matches; passing it as literal `text` matched nothing (the pre-v0.11.9 silent failure on ~15 of Rakkor's entries). Values are unescaped in **two layers** — Qt INI (`\\`→`\`) THEN QRegExp punctuation-escapes (`\'`→`'`), because a Frostbite value is a QRegExp pattern: `Redeemer\\'s` → (Qt) `Redeemer\'s` → (QRegExp) `Redeemer's` (a single-pass unescaper leaves the stray `\` and the regex then hunts a literal backslash — caught only by the end-to-end match test, not the parse). Highlights dedup on full visual identity (pitfall #61a). `[GeneralHighlight]` (roomname/speech/whisper/thought/script → preset theme vars) and `[AlertHighlight]` (health/bleeding/death → "belongs in Lich" count) are **keyed by role/alert NAME with NO `size=` key** — both prior parsers used a numeric `size`-indexed loop and silently returned nothing; fixed to iterate the named keys. Frostbite **groups** (Critters/Combat/Travel/…) stay informational (`sourceClass`), NOT recreated as LB groups (Sekmeht's call) — **EXCEPT `group=Names`** (v0.12.0): a `[TextHighlight]` with `group=Names` is a player name, routed to `result.names` (Contacts) instead of highlights, each with a per-colour `templateName` (`color<HEX>` — hex-derived since Frostbite has no Wrayth-style palette index). `parseHighlights` returns `{ highlights, names }`; the wizard's **source-agnostic** contacts-apply (`ensureTemplate(n.templateName, n.textColor)`) creates one template per colour and assigns each contact's `templateId` — identical to the Wrayth `<names>` and **Genie `names.cfg`** (`#name {#hex} {Name}` → `parseNames`, v0.12.1) paths. **All three clients** import player names as Contacts with per-colour templates (`color<HEX>`; Wrayth prefers its palette index `colorNN`). (Rakkor's Frostbite file: 151 names → 9 templates; Genie names.cfg: 96 → 7. Genie's `parseNames` now also stamps `templateName` + dedups by name — before v0.12.1 it produced contacts with NO template.) Timers (`timer`/`timerValue`/`timerAction`) aren't imported (no LB timer feature) → flagged `partial`. The colour/options decode shares `parseQtEscapes` ([colorUtils.ts](src/renderer/import/colorUtils.ts)) — see pitfall #72 for the single-digit-hex bug this rework surfaced. The wizard's highlight preview renders each pattern in its real fg/bg on a fixed dark game-like chip (`.iw-hl-preview`) + text/bg swatches — shared by all three legacy importers. **`macros.ini`** (`[keypad]`/`[alt]`/`[ctrl]`/`[function]`, keyed by Qt modifier+key integer codes decoded in `normalizeFrostbiteKey`) parses via the **shared `parseImportedMacroAction`** ([macroAction.ts](src/renderer/import/macroAction.ts)) — the SINGLE macro-action parser used by **all three** legacy clients (Frostbite, Wrayth, Genie) so they import macros identically. It has **two split modes**: a **send-token** model (Frostbite `sendToken: /\$[ns]/gi` from `macrothread.cpp` — BOTH `$n`/`$s` send, `$s` adds a sequence pause we don't model, + `stripOuterQuotes`; Wrayth `sendToken: /\\r/g` + `cleanSegment` to drop the leading `\x`) where a token sends the preceding command and a TRAILING no-token command is type-and-wait (gets `@` appended at the end); and a **separator** model (Genie `separator: /;/g` + `cleanSegment` dropping leading `\x`/trailing `\r`) where every command AUTO-SENDS and nothing is appended — a command is type-and-wait only if it already has an `@`. In BOTH modes a command with `@` is a cursor (the runtime `parseCursorMarker` drops the cursor where the `@` is, incl. **mid-string** — `take @ from my backpack` / Genie `first @` → cursor in the gap), so `@` is NEVER flagged "move to a Lich alias" (the pre-v0.11.9 mistake — fixed for Frostbite/Wrayth, then Genie). **Segments are NOT trimmed** so an intentional trailing space survives and positions the cursor (`advance ` → `advance @`; trimming gave `advance@` → "advancesword"). `allBuiltin` is reported so every client surfaces a nothing-but-built-ins macro as `unsupported` instead of silently dropping it; Genie additionally filters `#`-prefixed internal scripting (`isGenieInternal`, e.g. `#if`/`#put`/`#class`) so a `#if`-conditional macro reduces to `unsupported`. Do NOT re-add a per-client copy; change macro-import behavior in the one helper so the clients can't drift. **Genie count-only notices fixed (v0.11.9):** Genie writes the SHORT command forms, so `parseGenieFiles` counts `#sub`/`#var`/`#gag`|`#ignore` prefixes (covering `#subs`→substitutes, `#var`→variables, etc.) — matching only the long `#substitute`/`#variable` reported 0 on real Genie configs and silently suppressed the "belongs in Lich" notices. (Genie **classes** → Lichborne groups remains an unbuilt opportunity: the 4th `{class}` arg on highlights/triggers is still informational-only `sourceClass`.) **Genie highlight/trigger PATTERN handling (v0.11.9 bug-check fixes):** Genie's `/pattern/`, `/pattern/i` wrapping marks an EXPLICIT regex regardless of the declared type (`stripGenieSlashWrap`, matching Globals.cs:1007-1019 — strip leading `/`, trailing `/i`→case-insensitive or `/`); without it a slash-wrapped pattern imported with the slashes baked in as literal text and **never matched** (`/The taipan…/i`). And **`beginswith`** highlights (Genie's `HighlightBeginsWithList`, "line STARTS WITH") are imported as a `^`-anchored regex (`'^' + escapeRegex(pattern)`, line scope), NOT a plain substring — the old `phrase` mapping over-matched (fired on the pattern appearing anywhere in the line). Highlight type → mode/scope otherwise: `regexp`→regex/match, `line`→phrase/line, `string`→text/match, `beginswith`→regex/line. Triggers are always regex (also slash-stripped). **Known minor gaps (accepted):** `string` (6) maps to word-boundary `text` vs Genie's raw substring; the `;` command separator is hardcoded (Genie's `separatorchar` is configurable but defaults to `;`). **Trigger sound actions (v0.11.9):** the `sound` `TriggerAction` supports BOTH a `soundFile` (a real WAV/audio path — the engine plays it via `playWavFile`, taking priority) and a `soundPreset` (one of 4 built-ins). `mapTrigger` ([mapper.ts](src/renderer/import/mapper.ts)) preserves a **real audio file** verbatim as `soundFile` (`isAudioFile`: a path separator or audio extension) and only falls back to a `soundPreset` (`mapSoundPreset`) for a built-in sound NAME (Genie's `#play MiniFanfare1`). A sound NEVER makes a trigger `partial` — it's a supported action (uniform with how Frostbite imports highlight sounds as `ready`); a library-name fallback gets an informational note (a tooltip on the `ready` badge), a real file gets none. Don't re-add the old "preset only" mapping that discarded WAV paths, or the sound-→partial downgrade. **`general.ini`**: `[GameWindow]/[DockWindow]/[Commandline] background`→`--bg-app`, `[GameWindow] fontColor`→`--text-primary` (the story-window text colour), `[QuickButton]`→ a surfaced count (no LB command-button feature → "recreate as macros/aliases"). **`substitutes.ini`** (`[substitution]`, regex find/replace) **NOW imports natively** (v0.12.0 — superseded the old "count-only → use textsubs.lic" stance) → `SubstituteRule`s, GLOBAL scope; the `target=Experience` mind-state numbering subs are flagged `unsupported` (see the Mutes & Substitutes bullet's import note). **The wizard is legacy-client only as of v0.10.0** — the "Lichborne" source card (F29 self-import) was removed and Lichborne→Lichborne moves through the platform-wide **Transfer** feature instead (the Automations panel's Export button was removed too; its Import button is now labeled "Import from another client…"). The `parseLichborneYaml` parser ([lichborne.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/lichborne.ts)) and the `nativeRules`/`nativeLayout`/`nativeGroups`/… apply branches in [ImportWizard.tsx](src/renderer/components/ImportWizard.tsx) are now unreferenced (the legacy parsers never populate those fields); left in place as harmless dead code rather than ripped out. `'lichborne'` stays in the `ImportSource` union so the residual `source === 'lichborne'` guards compile.

### Session Log (DESIGN.md §28, shipped v0.7.0)
Per-character daily plain-text logs. **Capture** happens in `GameWindow.onGameEvent` → `logToSession()` → `session-log:append` IPC → buffered per-character writer in [sessionLog.ts](src/main/sessionLog.ts). Files: `{userData}/Logs/{Character}/{Character}_YYYY-MM-DD.log`, line format `[HH:MM:SS][stream] text` (the date is in the filename; parsers also accept the legacy `[YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS.mmm]` form). Buffered (1s / 100-record flush, force-flush at 5000); `flushAllSessionLogs()` runs on graceful close next to `backupAllProfiles()`.

- **Config is app-wide, NOT per-character.** All Session Log preferences (capture gates, retention, compression, raw-size cap, the Recent-tail filter, the Export-builder format prefs) live in one `SessionLogSettings` object — [sessionLogSettings.ts](src/renderer/sessionLogSettings.ts), stored in `_shared.yaml` via `SharedProfile.sessionLog`. `logToSession` calls `loadSessionLogSettings()` fresh per batch (it's a tiny localStorage read — no stale-closure ref needed, and a Settings change applies instantly to every open character). The capture config also rides along in `SessionLogAppendPayload` (`retentionDays`/`compress`/`maxRawMB`) so main can run maintenance without its own copy. Both the SettingsPanel section and the modal read-modify-write the shared object so neither clobbers the other's fields.
- **What's skipped:** `raw`, room sub-streams (`ROOM_STREAMS`), blank lines — state, not history. Stream IDs `cmd`/`sys`/`main` are the capture-category keys; everything else counts as "streams".
- **Size management (v0.7.0):** closed (non-today) day-files are gzip-compressed to `.log.gz` (~85-90% smaller) by background `maintain()` — runs at session start + day-rollover, gated by `sessionLogCompress`. All readers route through `readLogFile()` (gunzips transparently) and `resolveDayFile()`. Two retention limits: `pruneOldLogs` (age, `.log` + `.log.gz`) and `enforceRawSizeCap` (caps *uncompressed* `.log` bytes only — never `.gz`, never today's file). If you change the line format or add a maintenance limit, keep both parsers (`LINE_RE` in the modal, `EXPORT_LINE_RE` in main) accepting the legacy form.
- **UI:** [SessionLogModal.tsx](src/renderer/components/SessionLogModal.tsx) — one modal, three views (Recent Tail + Quick Search + Export), opened by the toolbar **Logs** button or right-click → "Show in Log" (which opens straight into Search). Tail is paginated (`PAGE`/`JUMP_RADIUS`); never loads a whole day. The Recent-tail filter (`filterHidden`/`filterDedup`) and the Export format prefs persist in the app-wide `SessionLogSettings`, not per-character.
- **Export builder ("Create Log File"):** the renderer gathers a `SessionLogExportSpec` (date range, stream layers, include-timestamps/tags, dedup, summary, split-per-stream, target) and main does all the reading/filtering/formatting/writing in `session-log:build-export`. Big data never crosses IPC — only the spec and a small `SessionLogExportResult`. `target: 'file'` runs a save (or folder, when `splitPerStream`) dialog; `'clipboard'` writes combined text via Electron `clipboard`.
- **Read IPC:** `session-log:list-days`, `read-day` (tail + `beforeLine` pagination), `list-streams` (single day, or a range when `toDate` is passed), `search` (returns `SessionLogSearchHit` with `lineNo`/`total` for jump-to-tail), `build-export`, `disk-usage`, `open-folder`. All read handlers flush the character's buffer first so reads reflect the live session.

### AI features — BYOK, capability-routed (DESIGN §10, shipped v0.16.0)
**Three guardrails, all load-bearing (DESIGN §32):** (1) AI **advises / composes / summarizes / decorates and NEVER issues game commands** — the single rule that keeps every AI feature inside Simutronics' scripting policy and Principle #1; (2) **BYOK, opt-in, privacy-disclosed** — nothing leaves the machine unless a feature is enabled AND its one-time consent gate accepted; (3) **AI ENHANCES, never GATES** — every feature has a working non-AI baseline (for Catch Me Up the baseline is the scrollback + Session Log: the player can read what they missed themselves; the AI just summarizes it).

- **The adapter is CAPABILITY-routed, not provider-routed** ([src/main/ai/](src/main/ai/)) — the correction to the old §10 "one OpenAI key does everything" assumption. **Claude has no image generation and no embeddings endpoint**, so `text` / `embeddings` / `image` are three independently-BYOK capabilities. v0.16.0 implements **text (Claude)** only; `embed()`/`generateImage()` are **declared but throw a clear "capability not configured"** so the image (G9/AI9) and RAG (AI3/AI6/AI10) tracks slot in later with no redesign — a feature reaching a dark capability must **degrade with a message, never crash**.
- **Keys live in main's `safeStorage` (`ai-keys.json`, the `passwords.json` pattern) and NEVER cross IPC** — only a "is a key present" boolean does ([aiKeys.ts](src/main/ai/aiKeys.ts)). All AI calls run in MAIN, never the renderer (keeps the key off every game-text path; a renderer `fetch` to the provider would be CSP-blocked anyway).
- **The Claude client is a ~100-line raw-`fetch` SSE reader** ([claudeProvider.ts](src/main/ai/claudeProvider.ts)), **deliberately NOT `@anthropic-ai/sdk`** — zero new npm packages (v0.15.0 packaging hygiene: `dependencies` = true runtime externals only) and it matches this codebase's hand-rolled-parser ethos. Don't "upgrade" it to the SDK without a reason.
- **Config split:** the **secret key** → `safeStorage`. The **non-secret config** (master enable, model tier, per-feature consent flags) → [aiConfig.ts](src/renderer/aiConfig.ts) (`lichborne.ai` working copy) → `SharedProfile.ai` → `_shared.yaml`. Deliberately NOT in `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` (machine-local — the `automationStats` precedent). Default model **Haiku 4.5** (cheap, the workhorse); Sonnet 5 / Opus 4.8 selectable.
- - **Log-backed Catch Me Up (v0.17.1, Sekmeht — reverses the v0.16.x screen-only decision above).** `/ai catchup 2.5h` now reads THIS CHARACTER's session log from `[now − 2.5h, now]` instead of only the screen buffer — fixing the "I did a 2.5h catchup but it only returned recent items" report (the screen buffer is bounded by `MAX_LINES`, so it can't reach past a few thousand lines). **Why it works now when the v0.16.x log build was reverted for scale:** the whole pipeline runs in MAIN (`buildCatchupDigest` in [sessionLog.ts](src/main/sessionLog.ts)) and returns a COMPACT digest — never raw rows over IPC (a year is ~29M lines). It walks **day by day, yielding between days** (`setImmediate`) so a long window can't block main and freeze every session, and pushes PROGRESS on `session-log:catchup-progress` for every phase (reading day N/M → deduping → extracting → summarizing) so the UI shows "Working on it…". **The model analyses EVERYTHING (Sekmeht), not a sample:** the payload is the FULL deduped log body (up to the tier's `maxChars`) + a fact-sheet of EXACT whole-window tallies as anchors. **DEDUP is what makes "everything" affordable** — grinding's repetition collapses, so a realistic window's UNIQUE content is a fraction of its raw size; if the deduped body still overflows the biggest tier, the most-recent fits and the tallies still cover the whole period (main trims, header says so). **Six TIME-SCOPED tiers** (`CATCHUP_TIERS` in GameWindow: recent ≤45m → session → extended → day → period → historical ≤1y) each carry their own prompt guidance (narrative at 30m, retrospective at 1y), `maxTokens`, and `maxChars` (45k→240k). **Extractors are EMPHASIS, verified against real log lines Sekmeht supplied** — ranks (`You've gained a new rank in …`), combat damage taken (`lands a light hit (1/23) to your chest` → attacker + part + severity — the severity ladder is the **VERIFIED 22-level GM-Kodius scale** `light hit`→`apocalyptic strike`, which **alternates `hit` and `strike`**, so the damage regex MUST match both (`(?:hit|strike)`) or every *strike*-level hit silently drops — a real bug shipped-then-fixed with a made-up `moderate`/`severe` ladder; attackers are counted ONLY on damage lines, never on arrivals/misses), deaths (`Your death cry echoes…`), directed speech (say/whisper/`<to you>` telepathy), work orders (`You hand X your logbook … N Dokoras in return`), and banking with Lich's VERIFIED coin ratios (plat=10000…copper=1, from `drbanking.rb`) → real net money flow. **THREE load-bearing rules for any future extractor:** (1) **tally counts BEFORE dedup** — two identical rank/hit lines are two REAL events; deduping first silently halves them. (2) **NEVER invent DR game math** (coin ratios, xp curves) — mine it from Lich's `drinfomon` (`drbanking`/`drexpmonitor`/`drstats`, each with SPEC files = verified inputs) or omit the category. (3) The `DRExpMonitor: Skill(+N)` line is the **mindstate/learning-rate ticker, NOT ranks** — counting it as ranks inflates the number wildly (nearly shipped exactly that); ranks come from the game's own message, and the ticker is filtered out as churn. **Per-character** (each GameWindow passes its own `session.character`; progress is `requestId`-filtered — pitfall #6). **Fallback (the safeguard, "AI enhances never gates"):** if session logging is OFF or the log read throws, it degrades to the screen buffer and SAYS SO in the header (`session log off, screen only`); the header also reports real coverage (`log reaches back 40m`, `N repeats collapsed`, `analysed the most recent portion`). **NOT YET DONE / KNOWN GAPS:** never run against a live game (all verification is pattern-level against pasted lines); banking currently keys on the `DRBanking:` SCRIPT line, not the game-native `The clerk slides a small metal box…` messages Lich parses (script-independent — a documented port); no injury-message extractor; docs/live-test/pattern-registry-port are the next pass. **`CATCHUP_MAX_MINUTES` (slashCommands.ts) is the executor's window ceiling — raised 24h → 1 YEAR in the same change**, because the tiers/pipeline supporting a year is USELESS if the executor still rejects `7d` before running (it did — a leftover screen-only guard one function away from the tier code). **Lesson: when you widen a feature's range, trace the WHOLE command path — the `parseDuration` unit, the tier table, AND the executor's cap + its error text + the arg hint (Principle #11) — not just the piece you're editing.** Keep `CATCHUP_MAX_MINUTES` aligned with the largest `CATCHUP_TIERS` window.
- **Catch Me Up (AI4) — the window is ALWAYS a TIME RANGE `[from, now]`, from exactly TWO sources: (1) an explicit duration (`/ai catchup 27m` — `parseDuration` ([slashCommands.ts](src/renderer/slashCommands.ts)) takes `27m`/`90`/`2h`/`2.5h`/`1.5h`/`1h30m` AND unit suffixes `m`/`h`/`d`/`mo`/`y` — `2mo`=2 months, `1y`=1 year; `mo` MUST be alternated before `m` or `2mo` reads as 2 minutes), else (2) the default 30m.** The header ALWAYS states which was used — the feature must never be a black box. **Two auto-window mechanisms were BOTH removed — do NOT reintroduce either:** a *silent idle-detector* (watched keypress gaps, made `/ai catchup` behave differently based on state the user couldn't see — Sekmeht: *"I don't understand what data /ai catchup looks at"*), and a **`/afk` toggle** (marked an explicit away-span; removed as not-worth-it, Sekmeht 2026-07-14: *"it's on the player to know how to catch up"* — the duration argument covers it). If you wandered off, the answer is `/ai catchup 2h`, not a mode or a heuristic.
- **GATHERING IS AN INVARIANT — read main + EVERY OPEN STREAM PANEL, never `lines` alone.** A **watched** stream (thoughts/deaths/arrivals) routes to `streamLines` and **never reaches `lines`** — `STREAM_FALLBACK` only spills a stream into main when *nobody is watching it*. Gathering from `lines` alone made the summary blind to exactly the conversation a returning player cares about, and it got **WORSE the better the user's panel layout was** (that inversion is how the bug was found). `collectHistory()` merges both, **timestamp-merged + source-tagged** (`[thoughts] Rakkor says …`), skipping our own `internal-system` chatter, the `lbAI` stream, and `CATCHUP_SKIP_STREAMS` (state readouts that clear+rewrite — `exp`/`inv`/`activespells`/`moonwindow`/… — which would feed the model a stale TABLE instead of events). **Any future AI feature that reads "what happened" must gather this way.**
- **⚠️ SUPERSEDED v0.17.1 — Catch Me Up NOW READS THE SESSION LOG (per-character), tier-scoped. The screen-only scope described in THIS bullet was the v0.16.0–v0.17.0 behaviour; see the "Log-backed Catch Me Up (v0.17.1)" bullet below for the current architecture. The history here is kept because its LESSON still governs: the FIRST log attempt (v0.16.x) failed on SCALE, and the v0.17.1 build only works because it solves scale differently (extract-then-summarize + dedup + per-tier budget), NOT by dumping raw log text with filters. Read the rest of this bullet as "why the naive version was reverted", not "why it can't read the log".** SCOPE (historical) — Catch Me Up summarizes WHAT IS ON YOUR SCREEN. It does NOT read the session log. Purpose, in Sekmeht's words (2026-07-14): *"I walked away, I came back — what did I miss in the last 20 minutes?"* Source is `collectHistory()` (live scrollback + open stream panels), filtered to the window. **A log-reading build was written, tester-shipped, and REVERTED** — it worked, but log scale (a busy character logs **80k lines/day**: 49k `main` + 38k `inv` + 17k `spells`) forced in priority tiers, a verbatim block, realm-ticker gating, NPC-vendor filters and template collapsing, and it *still* produced walls of vendor chatter. None of that is needed for the few thousand on-screen lines (already bounded by `MAX_LINES`). **LOG ANALYSIS IS A DIFFERENT FEATURE** (DESIGN §10.4) — do NOT merge it back in. The transferable lesson: **the scale of the input decides the architecture** — the same feature over 3k screen lines and 80k logged lines is two different features. Groundwork left behind: the `session-log:read-window` IPC (filters a time range in MAIN; **never bound a TIME window with a LINE count** — pitfall #92).
- **`[sys]` never enters the prompt — INVARIANT.** That's where we log our OWN output (slash results, **prior summaries**); feeding it back makes the model summarize its own summaries. `collectHistory` enforces it by skipping `internal-system`-led lines and the `lbAI` stream.
- **`gatherWindow` dedups on TEXT ALONE, not (stream, text) — deliberate.** DR double-emits speech (pitfall #49: once inside the pushStream block, once to main), so with a conversation/whispers panel OPEN the two copies land under **different streams** at the same timestamp. A stream-aware dedup misses that and feeds the model every spoken line twice.
- **The budget is CHARACTERS, not lines** (screen path: `CATCHUP_MAX_CHARS` 40k; log path: per-tier `maxChars` 45k–240k — chars ≈ tokens/4). A flat tail is fine on the SCREEN path precisely because the source is the screen buffer, not a log; the LOG path sends the full deduped body (main-trimmed to the tier budget, most-recent kept) plus the exact tallies. The header says so honestly when it can't fit everything. **Naming the character in the prompt** (`catchupSystem(character)`) is the highest value-per-token line in it — the first version said "the player" and made the model *guess* which name in raw game text was them.
- **`lbAI` is the AI OUTPUT STREAM** (`AI_STREAM` in aiConfig.ts) — a first-class named stream seeded into `discoveredStreams`, so it's always addable in Panel Manager / `/panel open lbai`. **DECIDED default (Sekmeht, 2026-07-14): output goes to the MAIN game window; when an `lbAI` panel is open (`watchedStreamsRef.has(AI_STREAM)`) it routes THERE instead.** Making `lbAI` the DEFAULT was considered and DECLINED — the summary should land where the player is looking; `lbAI` is the opt-in "keep it out of my scroll" surface. Routing is decided ONCE per run and the streaming updates follow it. Never emitted by the game → **no `STREAM_FALLBACK` entry**. **Every future AI feature routes its output through `lbAI`.** The two main-window-path edges (live line trimmable in a 2000+-line flood; per-token full-`lines` re-map, pitfall #82) are accepted-low-severity — opening the `lbAI` panel fixes both. **Its display label is `lbAI` (not the mangled `LbAI`):** client-seeded streams have no game title, so `streamLabel(id, title?)` (aiConfig.ts) special-cases `AI_STREAM` and is used at every tab/add-menu label site (makeCustomTab, both add-menus, slashPanelTab, addToZone) — a game title still wins, else capitalize-id as before (behavior-preserving for non-AI streams).
- **Rendering:** the summary is ONE live line, updated per delta, with TWO segments — a quiet `internal-system` **header** and the body on the **`ai` preset**. **`ai` follows the GAME TEXT color** (`color-mix(in srgb, var(--accent) 25%, var(--text-primary))` in panels.css), NOT `--text-dim` — AI output is *content the user reads*, not a throwaway notice like "Connection closed." (Sekmeht: *"it's dark grey when I have white text"*). It ends with a **trailing `\n`** for separation from the next paragraph — **never a separate spacer row**, which picks up its own empty `[HH:MM]` when timestamps are on. Errors stay on `internal-system` (a notice, not content).
- **Slash surface:** `/ai` (bare status · on · off · key · catchup · stop). It's a **bare+verbs noun**, so it depends on the `NOUNS_WITH_VERBS` palette rule (see the slash section) — without it the verbs never list or Tab-complete. `/ai key` deliberately does NOT accept a key inline (it would land in command history and the palette); it points at Settings. (A `/afk` command existed briefly and was removed — see the window-source bullet above.)
- **Error handling — SSE `error` frames MUST be surfaced.** `claudeProvider.handleFrame` THROWS on an Anthropic `error` frame (e.g. `overloaded_error`/529 arriving AFTER `message_start`) so it propagates out of `claudeChatStream` → main's try/catch → the renderer's error line. Without that branch a mid-stream failure hit no case, was ignored, and the caller's `onDone` fired with a partial/empty summary and NO error (tokens still counted). A pre-stream failure is already handled by the `!res.ok` check. Any future SSE consumer must handle the `error` frame, not just the deltas.
- **When adding an AI feature:** route output through `lbAI` (main-default, lbAI-if-open); gather via `collectHistory()` (never `lines` alone); add a consent key to `aiConfig.consent` + a disclosure modal that discloses BOTH the data sent AND that it's billed to the user's own key; call the adapter, never an SDK; give it a `/ai <verb>` + `NOUN_HELP` line; pre-check the key so consent isn't shown for an unfireable request; and **build its non-AI baseline first**.

### Windowed Panels / Free Layout (DESIGN.md §33, shipped v0.13.0)
A per-character toggle (`layoutMode: 'panels' | 'free'`, scopedKey) between **Static Panels** (the docked 4-zone skeleton) and **Windowed Panels** (free-floating windows). **Terminology:** *Static Panels* = docked; *Windowed Panels* = floating; *streams* are the content placed inside either — those are the user-facing terms. Internal code keeps the older name "Free Layout" (`freeLayout.ts`, `fl-*` CSS, `freeWindows`/`layoutMode`/`freeLayoutLocked`); don't bulk-rename.

**Direction (Sekmeht, 2026-06-11): Windowed Panels is the end state — Static Panels WILL be discontinued** (stage 1: flip the default to `'free'` for new characters; stage 2: remove Static entirely with a one-time `buildWindowsFromCurrentLayout` conversion so no layout is lost — neither stage scheduled yet; full plan in DESIGN §33). Operational consequences NOW: don't build static-only features; until stage 2, every new feature must still work in BOTH modes (the pitfall-#79 per-mode aggregation pattern is the interim cost — those branches collapse when Static goes away); prefer designs that get simpler without the zone skeleton; and treat the zone scopedKeys as future legacy state to MIGRATE at stage 2, never silently delete (Principles #3/#8).

- **Model:** in free mode GameWindow renders a pointer-through `WindowLayer` ([WindowLayer.tsx](src/renderer/components/WindowLayer.tsx)) of `FloatingWindow`s ([FloatingWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/FloatingWindow.tsx)) INSTEAD of the skeleton (the skeleton's chrome strips / main-top zone / right column are gated on `layoutMode === 'panels'`). Each `FloatWindow` ([freeLayout.ts](src/renderer/freeLayout.ts)) has a **fractional** rect (0..1 of the game area, so windows scale on OS-window resize / §13.9 decouple), `z`, `showTitle`, and a `kind`: `panel` (a PanelFrame on `sharedFrameProps`) or decoupled chrome — `main` (the extracted `textAreaNode`), `command` (`commandBarNode`), `vitals`, `icon`. Persisted via the scopedKeys above → YAML (Principle #1; carried by Profile Transfer's Panel Layout category).
- **Conversion = CASCADE, NOT measure-and-mint.** Switching to windowed (or "Rebuild from panels") runs `buildWindowsFromCurrentLayout` — clean default SIZE per surface at a staggered position (only chrome HEIGHTS are measured). The pixel-for-pixel "pop your exact layout free" approach was tried and **abandoned**: titled windows are bigger than edge-to-edge panels strips, so it always overlapped / "scaled weirdly" (esp. the bottom command bar constricting everything). Don't revive it.
- **Snapping** (§33.5): magnetic edge + window-to-window on drag AND resize; live guide lines; **Alt** disables; arrow-keys nudge the focused window. Snap targets measured LIVE from the DOM (`getSnapTargets`).
- **Add/lock UI lives in the Panel Manager**, NOT floating on the overlay (a floating button had no good home): an **Add Window** section (unlimited new panels + re-add any missing singleton so a closed bar can't be lost) and a **Lock windows** toggle (`freeLayoutLocked` → drag/resize/nudge become no-ops, handles hidden, and the grip's dash drag-mark hidden too — F44 v0.13.2; the 11px grip strip itself stays so geometry doesn't shift on lock toggle; tab drag-reorder is also disabled while locked — F46 v0.13.5, PanelFrame's `reorderTabs` prop: windowed passes `!freeLayoutLocked`, static zones pass `true`; reorder flows through the normal `onTabsChange` path so persistence is the existing one in both modes). The static-panel **zone manager is hidden in free mode** (windows aren't bound to zones).
- **Chrome windows (command/vitals/icon) are FIXED-height** (deterministic), resizable both axes, bar centered in the body. **Never auto-height, and never auto-*hug* either** — see pitfall #74 (the deterministic-height rule) and pitfall #93 (a measure→persist auto-hug was tried in v0.17.0 and REVERTED — it corrupted saved heights + clipped the vitals bar).
- **Window chrome (title bar / grip) — the v0.17.0 polish + its invariants ([free-layout.css](src/renderer/styles/free-layout.css)).** The `.fl-titlebar` (name shown) and `.fl-grip` (name hidden) are a slim ~8px header; **their heights MUST stay matched** (both derive from `1.4em × 0.5em` / `0.7em`) or showing/hiding the name jumps the header (the bug: a shrunken titlebar was thinner than the grip). Title text needs box > glyph height to centre (too tight → reads top-aligned). The **top resize handle is 4px** (was 6px) so the slim header keeps a drag-to-move zone below it — and because that handle is a FIXED 4px while the header is em-scaled, both `.fl-titlebar` and `.fl-grip` carry a **`min-height: 9px` floor** (kept EQUAL) so the move band stays grabbable at the minimum game font (8px, where the em height would be ~5.6px). The **T (hide-name) button is a chevron `⌃`**, and both controls (collapse/close) are **hidden until window hover/focus** (`.fl-window:hover`/`--focused .fl-tb-btn`) — quiet by default. Visuals are a soft top-lighter **gradient + hairline** (not a hard grey block) with a 1px inset **accent focus line**, all `color-mix` (theme-safe, eyeballed light — Principle #4). When touching the header, keep titlebar==grip height and re-verify the show/hide toggle + drag both work.
- **Cross-feature invariants (verified in the v0.13.0 sweep — hold these when touching windowed mode):** (1) **Adding streams in windowed mode goes through the per-window PanelFrame `+`** (it lists discovered + builtin + custom streams), NOT the Panel Manager's Available-Streams list (that's hidden in free mode) — so don't assume the zone-add path is reachable. (2) **All scroll-resnap paths are `scrollRef`-based** (`stickToBottom`), and `scrollRef` is set by the Virtuoso `scrollerRef` whether the main text renders in the skeleton or a `kind:'main'` window — so replay/tab-show/font-change/resize resnap cover free mode automatically; keep it that way (don't gate resnap on `layoutMode`). (3) **Modals/overlays must out-z the `WindowLayer` (z-index 60)** — the Panel Manager / Settings / Maps / context menus all do (portaled or higher z); a new overlay under z 60 would hide behind floating windows. **Corollary (B166): a DOCKED strip (a flex child of the shell, like the Debug strip) can never work in free mode** — the layer is absolute inset-0 over the whole shell, so the strip renders UNDER the windows; don't reserve a layer inset for it either (tried, replaced). The pattern is to open such surfaces AS a floating window in free mode: the Debug button toggles a panel window seeded with the `debug` tab (`toggleFreeDebugWindow`), the strip renders only in panels mode, and collection is presence-based (`debugOpen` memo, the pitfall-#76 `lichScriptsOpen` shape) so the window ✕ / tab ✕ turn telemetry off with no extra bookkeeping. The collection effect also keys on `session.sessionId` so a reconnect-in-place (pitfall #69) re-arms main's `debugPanelOpen` raw-XML gate. (4) Session-log capture, highlights/contacts/triggers, and the map all work unchanged because windows host the *same* PanelFrame content as zones — only the container changed. **(B193 caveat) That "same content" guarantee only holds for props that ride `sharedFrameProps`** — a callback wired ONLY to a panel's docked panels-mode strip (the Debug panel's `onGotoFireRule`, which drives the Fires-tab "Edit" button) is absent from the PanelFrame-hosted copy, so it silently degrades (greyed button) in a floating window or a zone tab. When a panel is hosted BOTH as a docked strip and via PanelFrame, every prop/callback the strip gets must also be in `sharedFrameProps` → PanelFrame → `renderPanel`, or the PanelFrame copy is missing it. (5) **Every "which tabs are visible/watched" aggregation must branch on `layoutMode`** — the zone arrays are deliberately-preserved STALE state in free mode (they restore the layout on switch-back); aggregating them in free mode caused B167 (unread dots never cleared) and B168 (stream fallback double-routing/blocking). Current per-mode sites: `lichScriptsOpen`, `debugOpen`, `activeIdsRef`, `watchedStreamsRef` — mirror them for any new per-tab feature (full write-up: pitfall #79). (6) **The WindowLayer's ResizeObserver IGNORES 0×0 measurements** (B174 — a hidden character tab is display:none = 0×0; letting it through unmounted every floating window on every tab switch). The `size > 0` render gate means "never measured yet," nothing more — don't re-introduce a 0×0 bail (pitfall #83). **Known minor edges (not bugs):** "Reset Panels" (PM header) resets the *static* zone layout even in windowed mode (no visible effect there — the windowed reset is "Rebuild from panels"); closing the Game/Command window leaves no main text/input until re-added via **Add Window** (recoverable by design).

### Lichborne Experiences (DESIGN.md §34 — SHIPPED v0.14.0: scaffold + Living Tableau [Beta])
The §32 G-series/X-series ("graphics for text players": Combat HUD, Wound Paper-Doll, Tactical Radar, Living Tableau, …) ship as **Lichborne Experiences** — a new first-class layout object: registered graphical **floating surfaces** over the game layout, hosted by the v0.13.0 `FloatingWindow` engine via a new `ExperienceLayer` rendered in BOTH layout modes (the Maps overlay is the shipped precedent). **The panel/stream system stays byte-identical**: Experiences have their own registry (`experiences.ts`), own id space (never in `discoveredStreams` or tab arrays — stream-collision-safe by construction), own scopedKey persistence (rides `state:` → YAML, no profile-shape change) + a `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` category, and an app-bar **"Experiences"** shelf. `map`/`exp`/`lichScripts` stay panels forever. **Two models were explicitly REJECTED — don't re-propose them** (full reasoning in §34.2): per-panel "Interactive Mode" view toggles (Simu splits combat text between the combat stream and main, so the combat window is optional equipment; the HUD reads parsed *state*, not stream text) and "Interactive Streams" as a new panel category (wrong chrome for instruments; pointless namespace bookkeeping). A third draft — the "v2" panel→Experience conversion/dual-hosting revision — was **deliberately discarded** (2026-06-12), but its **DUAL-HOSTING half was SUPERSEDED and SHIPPED v0.15.1 at Sekmeht's fresh explicit ask** (screen estate): every PanelFrame `+` menu offers Experiences below a separator with an [e] badge; hosted tabs are `type: 'experience'` with namespaced `exp:<id>` ids (NEVER bare — §34.1 collision safety; NOT in ALL_PANEL_TYPES), rendered by the same `renderExperienceContent` builder via `renderExperienceTab` on sharedFrameProps (B193), sharing the floating instance's ⚙ prefs — **and hosting their OWN ⚙ in the F31 view-controls corner as of v0.15.2** (`getExperienceHidden`/`onToggleExperienceOption` on sharedFrameProps; find-or-create mints a CLOSED instance as the prefs record for tab-only experiences — one `hidden` map, window and tab can never disagree), taking the panel's F31 A+/A− via an inline `--game-font-size` re-map, counted into the §35.6 scene gate by the pitfall-#79 per-mode `expTabIds` aggregation, and EXCLUDED from `watchedStreamsRef`. **The panel→Experience CONVERSION half stays discarded** — `map`/`exp`/`lichScripts` remain panels forever (full split: §34.2 item 3). First Experience: **Living Tableau (X1, "Gather Mode")** — decided 2026-06-12, superseding the Combat-HUD-first call. **G1 (Combat HUD) is now a combat FACET of X1, NOT a separate Experience** (2026-07-16, Sekmeht — full decision + risks in DESIGN §32.1's G1 entry): its instruments render as auto-revealing `ExperienceDef.options` LAYERS on the Tableau's scene (readiness ring / range gauge / threat+condition drawn ON the creature figures — the SceneParser already tracks `cast-creatures`), which subsumes a hard Social⇄Combat mode toggle (all combat layers off = today's pure social Tableau; social off + combat on = a combat cockpit rendered on the scene). The `CombatParser` work is unchanged and co-locates in the same Experience. Watch at spec time: visual-grammar collision (tactical layers must take hierarchy when combat is live), combat-flood perf under the §35.6 gate, and G1 now riding X1's Beta stability. NOT a §34.2 rejected model (those rejected giving *panels* interactive modes; this layers onto an *Experience*). **G1 combat facet — Phase 1 BUILT (v0.16.1, 2026-07-17) — the cockpit renders AROUND the player avatar, NOT on the creature figures (Sekmeht refinement: "the combat flavor should sit around the player's bubble").** On the Tableau: **readiness RINGS** hug the avatar (three cooldown sweeps inner→outer — Roundtime / Cast / Aim, each in its command-bar timer colour `var(--rt/ct/aim-end)`, only while that timer runs; a `CombatRings` SVG); a **danger pulse** on the avatar for wound conditions; **threat/engaged flare** on creature figures (v0.17.0/B220 — driven ONLY by ASSESS, which knows who's at melee; the old BLANKET `inCombat`→flare-every-creature marker was RETIRED because it flagged harmless NPCs that wandered in mid-fight, and no non-assess signal can tell friend from foe); and a **gauge panel UNDER the figure** ([TableauExperience.tsx](src/renderer/components/experiences/TableauExperience.tsx) + [experiences.css](src/renderer/styles/experiences.css)) with **BAL / POS bipolar gauges** (a red→yellow→green spectrum track + a fixed **0/neutral tick** + a moving value needle; balance is anchored at **"solidly" = 0 baseline**, green above / red below) and an **RNG** row (M/P/R cells, threatened band lit). All gate on the `readiness`/`threat`/`danger`/`position` ⚙ options; gauges FADE with combat (v0.17.0: hold through the 8s `inCombat` sticky, then fade out via asymmetric CSS — quick in, slow out; NOT the old persistent-HUD "leave them on"), timers/rings only while live. The state (`rtExpires/ctExpires/aimExpires/stance/hands/position/balance/range/assess`) rides ONE `useMemo`'d `experienceCombat` object through the single `renderExperienceContent` props source (pitfall #82c — a fresh literal each render would defeat the memo'd Tableau). **THREE gotchas this build cost:** (a) **a scene root that hosts A−/A+ zoom MUST anchor `font-size: var(--game-font-size)`** — `.tableau-scene` lacked it, so the em-based figures/gauges never scaled and "the +/- buttons did nothing" (the moons-scene had it; B211). A−/A+ is effectively a whole-scene ZOOM (element-scaling, fit-to-window, crisp) — the right model for a graphical Experience; a transform camera-zoom (crop-in) is for large navigable spaces like the map. (b) **The scene is a flex column: a fixed-height `.tableau-header` (title+desc, desc line-clamped) + a `.tableau-stage` (flex:1, holds EVERY figure + bubble, `sceneRef` measures it).** Header/stage separation stops figures rendering over the title at close zoom, and the FIXED header height stops figures hopping when description length changes. (c) Combat position/balance/range are parsed by **mirroring Lich's verified regexes VERBATIM** (combatExtract, DESIGN §32.1) — `DRStats` is NOT front-end-readable (in-memory Ruby `@@` vars, no client push; verified), so we run Lich's exact parse in the FE (identical value, live, works direct-SGE). **ASSESS (combat arena, layout B) — BUILT (v0.16.1):** `parseAssessLine` ([combatExtract.ts](src/shared/combatExtract.ts)) MIRRORS Lich's `parse_assess_line` VERBATIM (xmlparser.rb #1413) → typed per-creature records (relation facing/flank/behind/advancing + range + status + id). GameWindow accumulates the `assess` stream per block (`clearStream 'assess'` resets `assessAccumRef`; each line's creature id is scraped from its `<d cmd='look #id'>` segment `cmd`; routing untouched — assess text still flows to its own stream, never main), snapshots to `assessCast` + `assessAt`, threads into `ExperienceCombatState`. **The snapshot is guarded on a NON-EMPTY accumulator** (`batchAssessTouched && assessAccumRef.current.length > 0`): DR emits `clearStream 'assess'` THEN the lines, and at the 16ms flush coalescing (B172) they almost always land in one batch — but a block straddling a flush boundary would apply the just-cleared empty accum and flicker the arena blank for a frame. A completed assess always carries ≥1 entity (the self line), so the guard never suppresses a real update; a genuinely-empty assess (left combat) ages out via the 30s TTL instead. Same clear-then-lines batch-boundary shape applies to any future stream-repaint accumulator — guard the snapshot on non-empty. The Tableau renders id'd creatures with a relation tag + range chip + targeting-number badge, **your target ringed gold** (from the self row's `target`), **melee = engaged** (red glow — the honest "who's attacking", all-melee-attack, no faked per-attack attribution), **reeling** (stunned/imbalanced) dimmed, **click a creature → `face #id`** via the new `onCommand` prop (user action, echoes+logs, NOT automation — like map-walk buttons); ages out after `ASSESS_TTL_MS` (30s — assess is on-demand/script-driven). **v0.17.0 lifecycle fix:** the arena RECONCILES against the live creature cast — assess is a snapshot, so a killed/decayed creature would linger as "engaged"; reconcile by **name-count** vs the SceneParser's dead-aware cast (`normAssessName` normalizes article/case both sides; safe fallback to the raw snapshot if a name-mismatch would blank it), and render the cast's **dead creatures as ✕ corpses** in a row above the tactical row until they DECAY out (they don't vanish on death — Sekmeht). **v0.17.0 layout:** the scene font **fits the container** (width-dominant `fitScale` off the measured stage — a wide-short panel tab was fitting to ~6px "way too tiny"; height only a gentle floor), the **BAL/POS/RNG gauge panel is pinned to the stage BOTTOM** (not hung under the self, so it can't clip in a short tab), the **self figure clamps up clear of the gauge panel** in a short stage (measured gauge height), and the **self renders above seated figures** (z-index) so an overlap reads as depth. **The assess snapshot is ROOM-SCOPED** (B219): it has no inherent room binding (on-demand, cleared only by `clearStream 'assess'`), so an effect drops it on any room-identity change (title OR nav id, pitfall #46) — else retreating drags the old room's creatures into the new one (the name-mismatch fallback surfaces the stale snapshot when the new room has creatures). **Any future per-room SNAPSHOT state must clear on room change the same way** — the live cast auto-updates (B121 sub-stream clear), but a snapshot doesn't. **INVARIANTS from the assess design:** the **id is identity, the NUMBER is a reusable targeting slot** (a dead creature's slot recycles — corpus 2026-07-17: slot #1 went 48407408→48430408; key figures on id); **combat narration is ANONYMOUS** (attacks/closes/advances carry NO creature id — only assess/look/face do — so per-attack→figure attribution is impossible; don't fake it); creatures have POSITIVE ids, PCs NEGATIVE (`pc`). Corpus: `corpus/2026-07-17-assess-lavadrakes.xml` (gitignored). Verified by a focused bundle harness against the real captures + Lich's spec cases. The `CombatParser`'s range/facing/target is now partially realized through assess; the memory backlog's "Tactical Radar" idea is this same data if we ever want a top-down view. X1's Phase 1 kernel (cast + stable seating + procedural avatars + Say bubbles + focus-the-speaker) needs the NEW **`SceneParser`** (name pinned 2026-06-12; G1's later range/target/facing sibling = `CombatParser`) — typed speaker/channel/arrival *scene events* (speech/emotes/arrivals are only styled text lines today, no typed "who said what" exists). **The SceneParser is a CAPTURER REGISTRY (DESIGN §35, Sekmeht's design rule):** every scene event = one registry entry with `gate` (cheap substring pre-check, pitfall #82a) + `match` + `provenance` + `status: verified|unverified` — never a hardcoded if-chain; patterns are mined from existing parsers (Lich `drinfomon` drdefs.rb = the cast-extraction rules; Frostbite xmlparserthread.cpp = the channel/stream routing) and corpus capture (`corpus/`, gitignored) VALIDATES them (replay the real bundled code against captures, flip to verified, fix GAPs). **Phases 1+2 are BUILT (2026-06-12):** [sceneCapturers.ts](src/main/parser/sceneCapturers.ts) (registry; only `verified` capturers run live), [SceneParser.ts](src/main/parser/SceneParser.ts) (cast + arrive/depart diffing per-session, transition-suppressed so our own moves never mass-fire), [sceneExtract.ts](src/shared/sceneExtract.ts) (Lich-rule extraction), `scene-cast` snapshotted for replay (pitfall #60b); the Tableau is a pure view over the typed cast — don't re-add renderer-side text parsing. **Speech (say/ask/exclaim, yell, whisper, thought) is VERIFIED against the real captured session `Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/support/mock.xml`** (the B165 corpus) — harness `tmp-scene-harness/run.mjs` (~115 cases) replays verbatim corpus lines. **The harness is MACHINE-LOCAL, deliberately gitignored under `tmp-*/`** (Sekmeht 2026-06-12: it embeds verbatim corpus lines with real player names — same privacy stance as `corpus/`); it is NOT in the repo or git history — if it's missing, rebuild it from §35.4's recipe (bundle the REAL parsers via esbuild, feed corpus lines, assert events) rather than hunting for it; key facts: speaker+verb ride INSIDE the preset with the quote outside, yells are `<b>`-wrapped (no preset), whispers alias into `conversation`, thoughts have 3 shapes (one rides the TALK stream), DR double-emits to main (deduped by home-stream gating), and DR reuses speech/thought presets for STAT TABLES — the verb shape, never the preset, is the signal. Bubbles are replay-gated (#60a); thoughts render as wisps, NEVER a seated body (§32.2). **v0.17.0: the wisps live in a quiet BOTTOM-LEFT "thought log"** (was top-right, where they obscured the scene — Sekmeht): `.tableau-wisps` anchored `bottom/left`, `flex-direction: column` so the array (oldest→newest) puts the NEWEST at the fixed bottom spot and older ones stack UP + recede (`nth-last-child` opacity fade, `transition: opacity` for a smooth age-up). Bottom-LEFT clears the centre avatar, the bottom-centre gauges, AND the right-edge A−/A+/⚙ controls; `max-width: 42%` keeps it short of centre. **PERF CONTRACT (§35.6, v0.14.0 — INVARIANT): all scene work is OFF until the session has an open Experience** — `parser.sceneCapturersEnabled` (default false) gates the per-line capturer call, `SceneParser.setActive(false)` silences ALL emission (cast still silently tracked so activation backfills via `snapshotCast()` — never inject a LOOK), toggled by GameWindow's `scene-active-toggle` effect (re-arms on sessionId change, pitfall #69); don't add scene work outside this gate. Movement/stealth/emote/logon capturers + conversation gravity (§35.7: chattiness circle, directed-speech `target` pulls pairs together) all shipped 2026-06-12, every shape corpus-verified; procedural avatars are the permanent no-AI baseline (AI backdrop/portrait tier is Phase 3, behind the `AIProvider` adapter). **Per-window view controls (v0.14.7):** every Experience window hosts hover-quiet A−/A+ (per-instance `fontSize` override, applied by shadowing `--game-font-size` on the window subtree) and a ⚙ popover of content-layer checkboxes driven by `ExperienceDef.options` — a new Experience declares its option list in the registry and gates on the `hidden` prop at its single prop entry point (filtered arrays MUST be useMemo'd — effects key on their identities); both persist as optional `ExperienceInstance` fields (old saves load unchanged, ride YAML + Transfer for free). No slash command by design (the window is the surface — recorded §34.6). Phased plan in §34.9; checklist + guardrails in §34.7–34.8. **Experience #2 — Moons [Beta] (v0.15.1, §34.9 item 3; renamed from "Weather & Moons" — id stays `moons`; the [e] badge in the + menu AND tab strip distinguishes it from moonwatch's "Moons" STREAM, and experience-tab labels resolve LIVE from the registry so renames reach already-placed tabs):** a sky-dial instrument over the community **moonwatch.lic** stream — the proof an Experience can ride a Lich script's feed. `parseMoonLine` (accepts the script's NEGATIVE overdue timers `[x]-(-2)` — a digit-only regex made moons vanish pre-rise) + orbital constants + `computeSunPhase` + the sun-prose regexes (mirrored VERBATIM from the script's own detection) live in [experiences.ts](src/renderer/experiences.ts); GameWindow parses `moonWindow` lines at the generic stream branch (read-only id match — routing/discovery untouched, the stream stays addable as a plain panel = the text equivalent; reports MERGE into state, never replace — a moon can't vanish) and catches sunrise/sunset in the main branch behind a pitfall-#82a substring pre-gate. **Sun anchors come from three sources, priority-ordered:** locally-observed prose transitions (exact, provenance-flagged) > the **dr-scripts Firebase** (`moon_data_v2.json` — the same public feed moonwatch polls; `moons:fetch-sun-data` in main, 10-min cache — Lichborne's ONLY direct community-feed read, remove-by-one-gate if ever unwanted) > a lich.db3 `UserVars.sun` synth (≈-flagged, only after the fetch fails; reading it exposed + fixed the pitfall-#91 Marshal link bug). Day/night therefore works direct-SGE (Principle #2; the moon feed itself degrades to an empty state teaching `;moonwatch window`). The footer always shows data age — the feed is crowd-sourced; stale must never read as live. Rendering: viewBox width tracks the measured aspect (0×0-guarded, pitfall #83) — its width CEILING is a **degenerate-measurement guard only** (5000; B204: the original 1100 triggered on ordinary maximized panels, and `xMidYMax meet` then letterboxed the SVG ground/ridges apart from the full-width HTML sky layers — the "sky fills, ground inset" split is the diagnostic signature of a mixed HTML+SVG surface whose viewBox clamp is too low; size any such clamp so normal use can never hit it); SVG text sizes via `calc(var(--game-font-size) * k)` (CSS px = SVG user units — tracks A−/A+, the B201 map-LABEL approach); sky = elevation-blended gradient layers + horizon silhouette + rise/set rings, ALL motion gated on `!settings.epilepsySafe` AND its ⚙ layer. **⚙ options are ONE PER VISUAL LAYER and accurate about exactly what each hides** (The Sun / Living sky / Countdowns / Names / Horizon / Effects — the original combined "Sun & sky" conflated hiding the sun with flattening the backdrop; Sekmeht's split, 2026-07-08; `sunPhase` computes regardless of the sun toggle because the SKY needs it) — apply the same one-option-per-layer rule to future Experiences. **Moons stay STREAM-driven by moonwatch — a Firebase moon fallback was proposed and DECLINED; don't re-add it without a fresh ask** (only the sun reads the feed). **Tier 1 + Tier 2 SHIPPED v0.17.0 (Sekmeht) — do NOT call any of this "Almanac"** (Simutronics' later, separate feature; the term is banned in code/UI/docs — it's the "Moons" experience, full stop): **(Tier 1) a time-of-day WORD on the sky** (DAY/NIGHT/DAWN/DUSK, `skyPhaseLabel` off the SAME sun elevation the gradient uses so it can never disagree; centered just above the horizon, clear of the moons/sun that rise & set at the left/right ends; follows the ⚙ "Living sky" layer — and once TIME is captured the fine Elanthian **daypart** is appended in parens (`calendar.timeOfDay`), e.g. `Night (late evening)`, so it moved OFF the footer date line, which now reads month · year · season). **(Tier 2) weather + the Elanthian calendar, both from COMMAND PULLS** (DR exposes NEITHER passively — verified via drinfomon/DRStats/Vars/XML: the ONLY sources are the `WEATHER` and `TIME` commands; **no community script stores them** — `almanac.lic` is a skill grinder, unrelated). **Weather** (`WEATHER_GLANCE_RE` in experiences.ts): the glance marker — BOTH `You glance up at the sky.` (outdoors) AND `You glance outside.` (indoors w/ window/door) — is followed on the NEXT main line by the weather prose, captured + shown VERBATIM. This is PASSIVE (any natural sky-glance updates the chip). The enclosed refusal `That's a bit hard to do while inside.` is a GENERIC refusal (never matched passively) → read as "indoors" ONLY inside a ⟳ sync. **Calendar** (`parseTimeLine`): parsed ONLY from a ⟳ sync's TIME reply (line 3's `It is currently X and it is Y` isn't unique enough to trust from room prose) — day-of-YEAR (0-indexed "N days since the Victory") → day-of-MONTH via [src/shared/elanthianTime.ts](src/shared/elanthianTime.ts) (`dayOfMonth`, months are a uniform 40 days) so it reads `4 Ka'len the Sea Drake · 457 A.V. · winter · evening`; season/daypart verbatim from TIME line 3. **THE ⟳ IS SILENT (Sekmeht — "don't want players to see the command go through"):** it sends `TIME` + `WEATHER` via RAW `window.api.sendCommand` (NOT the echoing one — pitfall #53's silent-send pattern, no `>time`/`>weather` echo) and their replies are CONSUMED — never shown, logged, or fed to triggers. Suppression is **per-REPLY-BLOCK, NOT a time window** (`silentSyncRef {time,weather,at}` armed by the click) so a `TIME`/`WEATHER` **you type yourself always shows** — the crucial fix (an 8s window ate typed commands). Each flag clears at its reply block's **LAST line** (weather = the desc/refusal; TIME = L4 roisaen/Anlas) IN-LOOP, **NOT post-batch** — a post-batch clear dropped TIME's month/season/daypart when its 4 lines split across flush boundaries (the "Day 44 · 457 A.V." with no month bug); block-end clearing is batch-agnostic, `at`+`SKY_SYNC_WINDOW_MS` backstop a reply that never completes. Suppression is computed at the TOP of the main `stream-text` case (before the log push) via `suppressSync`, which gates the log record AND the `newMain` push AND processLine/highlights; capture happens regardless. **LAYOUT: a HEADER strip + a FOOTER strip** (`.moons-header` / `.moons-footer`, both full-width bands, siblings in the `.moons-scene` flex column) — the **header** holds "what's happening in the sky now" (**sky phase · moons · weather**), the **footer** holds the **Elanthian date**; a ⟳ ends BOTH strips (header + footer — the footer one alone was easy to miss, Sekmeht; same silent TIME+WEATHER pull, same tooltip). Each strip's row is **centered** inline-flow (`.moons-foot-row` under `text-align:center`, so a long weather sentence wraps) with consistent `KEY value age` segments (`.moons-foot-key/v/age`) divided by a faint `|` bar. (Iterated HARD — don't re-litigate: footer-only run-on → too-tall 4-row grid → 2-row footer → a floating top pill (rejected "weird") → these two strips.) **CONTRAST is SKY-ADAPTIVE, not fixed** — a `sceneInk` IIFE lerps three things off sky brightness (`wDay`): the text `color` (dark by day → light by night), a `--moons-halo` (OPPOSITE lightness, an SVG `paint-order:stroke` behind the scene text so names/chips/the DAY word read on ANY sky — day was the weak case, dark ink on a bright sky), and a `--moons-band` (OPPOSITE the text, so the strips are a frosted-LIGHT band by day behind dark ink / a DARK band by night behind light ink — a fixed dark tint was low-contrast by day). Scene text fades via `fill-opacity` (NOT element opacity) so the halo stays solid.
