The ONE themeable cue is the arc guide (`--moons-guide` → `var(--accent)` in darkBase, blended toward the sky-ink) — everything else in the scene (sky gradients, moon lore colors, shadow landscape) is FIXED realistic/lore data, the Principle #4 exception like the map's baked tiles. **Weather-effect sky animations + season icons (v0.17.0):** `detectWeather(prose)` regexes the captured weather line into `WeatherFx` flags (snow/rain/clouds/fog/wind/storm/clear/heavy — `\b`-anchored keyword sets; **`gale` is WIND not storm**; storm ⇒ rain+heavy+clouds; any precip ⇒ clouds) driving CSS-keyframed SVG layers over the sky: drifting clouds behind the bodies, wind-slanted snow/rain, a horizon fog gradient, an occasional storm lightning flash. Particle arrays are DETERMINISTIC (index-hashed, no `Math.random`); motion gated by the ⚙ "Weather effects" layer AND `epilepsySafe`; the SVG helpers are module-hoisted (pitfall #4, no hooks). A **season icon** (❄️/🌱/🌻/🍂) prefixes the season on the date line; indoors the weather line shows a **⌂** glyph + "sky not visible — step outside". **`wx` is a PLAIN const (NOT a hook), placed after `if (!moons) return`** — a `useMemo` there changed the hook count when moon data arrived → Rules-of-Hooks mount crash (blank screen after login). Three ⚙ layers ("Weather", "Weather effects", "Calendar"). **No slash command (§34.6 — the window/⚙ is the surface).** **Living-sky visual pass (v0.17.0, full detail in DESIGN §34.9):** the day glow is **sun-centric** (a userSpace `lb-sunglow` radial follows the sun's arc position — warm-white at noon, gold near the horizon, NONE below it so night stays night; the base day/zenith gradients were flattened so the horizon no longer dominates); **F69 sun-lit moons** shade each up-moon from the sun's on-screen direction (per-moon dynamic `radialGradient` + `MoonStyle.tones`, sun-tint via `color-mix` applied through **`style` NOT the SVG attribute** — color-mix is unreliable as an SVG presentation attribute); **F67/F68** ambient (twinkling stars, shooting star, winter aurora, summer fireflies) gate on the ⚙ Effects layer + `!epilepsySafe` via `anim` AND need `calendar.season`; **F70** winter snow + the sun glow are STATIC (always on when data supports). The **`Moons feature backlog` F64–F73** (F67–F70 shipped, F64–F66/F71–F73 planned) is enumerated in DESIGN §34.9. **General gotcha worth keeping: `color-mix()` works as a CSS *property* (via `style`) but is unreliable as an SVG *attribute* (`stop-color=`/`fill=`) — route dynamic color-mix through `style`.** **Bug-checked (comprehensive, 2026-07-20) — no blocking bugs; residuals all minor:** TIME line 4 (skill-dependent fine clock) is consumed-not-parsed via `roisaen`/`Anlas` tokens (an exotic low-skill variant could leak a line); within `SKY_SYNC_WINDOW_MS` (8s) of a ⟳ whose reply is DROPPED/slow, a MANUALLY-typed TIME/WEATHER can be over-suppressed (the 8s backstop for a slow reply is required; needs a dropped cmd + you redundantly typing it). `silentSyncRef`/`awaitingWeatherRef` are RESET on a reconnect-in-place (pitfall #69) so a mid-sync/mid-glance flag can't carry over and mis-capture the new connection's first line; the orphaned-`>` risk (pitfall #88) is handled by the existing prompt-collapse (suppressed lines never enter `newMain`). **elanthianTime.ts is the platform-wide Elanthian date/time reference** (units, month names, seasons, 7-year cycle, dayparts, `dayOfMonth`/`monthIndex`) — reuse it for any future Earth↔Elanthia conversion; see [[elanthian-time-reference]]. **Living landscape below the horizon (v0.17.0, Sekmeht — "I like nature"):** the ground band hosts a persistent, data-free NATURE scene (`MoonsLandscape`, a module-hoisted no-hooks sub-component like `MoonsClouds`/`MoonsPrecip`) — a distant forest edge, mid + large foreground trees (mixed pine + round), a winding **stream** flowing into a reflective **lake** — gated by a new ⚙ **"Trees & water"** option (id `landscape`, default on; the id is stable so an earlier "Village & landscape" save carries over — the village was the first draft, REPLACED by nature at Sekmeht's ask; don't reintroduce buildings without a fresh ask). **PERSPECTIVE is the core model:** every element's size scales with its baseline y (`persp(baseY)` 0.5 near the horizon → ~1.45 near the bottom), distant pieces fade toward a pale haze (atmospheric perspective), and everything LIGHTENS by day / DARKENS at night via a `landNight` factor derived from `sunElev` (works with NO TIME check, like `groundShade`). Colours lerp through **`mixHex(a,b,t)`** (a module-level hex-lerp — the Principle #4 realistic-colour exception; use it, NOT color-mix-as-SVG-attribute, pitfall). **Daytime contrast (the trees/lake read as objects, not ground):** saturated foliage vs a desaturated neutral ground, a dark **edge outline** on every canopy/tier, **contact shadows** under trees, and a **dark rim** on the lake. **Sun-DIRECTIONAL shadows (`shadow()`):** cast along the SAME radial fan as the crepuscular rays — from the sun's horizon point `(sun.x, horizonY)` THROUGH the object base, so a shadow points straight down (6 o'clock) under the sun, angles to ~4–5 o'clock toward the far side, lengthens as the sun sinks, and (because `baseY − horizonY` grows with depth) near-horizon objects cast flatter shadows than foreground ones; a rotated ellipse renders the angle; dusk/night falls back to a soft ambient blob. **Lake REFLECTIONS:** shimmering vertical columns for the sun (by day) + the LIT moons (Yavash/Xibar) where they pass above the pool (clipped to the lake's height at that x, no clipPath); **Katamba is excluded** (emits no light) and reflections are **skipped when the lake is iced** (winter). **SEASONAL dressing** rides the EXISTING ⚙ "Seasonal touches" toggle (`landSeason` = 'none' unless that's on AND the season is known): a per-season foliage palette (`SEASON_CFG`) + winter snow-caps on trees & an **iced-over lake/stream**, spring **blossoms**, summer lushness (+ the existing fireflies), and autumn recolour + **falling leaves** (a `LEAVES` particle array + `.moons-leaf` keyframe, gated on `anim`/epilepsy-safe like snow/rain). **Moon-body colour/glow corrections (v0.17.0):** Katamba = soot-black disc + **grey** rim + an **ominous MIASMATIC dark-violet glow** (`#2a123f`) that darkens a bright day sky AND reads as a shadowy purple on a dark one — it HOLDS at full through day+dusk and fades only into true night (`clamp01((sunElev+0.35)/0.3)`); **a pure-black glow was tried and is INVISIBLE on a dark sky (black only darkens) — a "shadow" glow that must read at night has to be a coloured haze, not black** (the lesson). Yavash = ruby/crimson (glow `#e01430`); Xibar = vivid ice-blue disc + a darker **blue** rim (`#88bce6`) + a **silvery-white** glow (`#dbe9f5` — no atmosphere, so the halo is ice-field shine). `MoonStyle` gained optional **`glowStrength`** (>1 = more intense) + **`glowR`** (halo radius × disc r); overlapping bodies paint in **`MOON_DEPTH` z-order** (furthest→closest: Sun, Yavash, Katamba, Xibar — the disc passes sort by it). Pill dot colours mirror the corrected hues. All new gradients (`water`, the moon glows) are per-instance via `gref`/`uid` (pitfall #95). **Sky-motion + night-sky polish (v0.17.0, Sekmeht):** the scene's `setTick` interval was dropped **30s → 2s** so the bodies AND everything derived from the sun's position — shadows, crepuscular rays, lake reflections — advance together in sub-pixel steps (smooth + in-sync), instead of a jerky 30s redraw; a CSS-transition ("glide") on the disc `cx`/`cy` was tried first and REVERTED because it smoothed the discs ONLY, desyncing them from the recomputed shadows/rays (the correct fix is one smoothly-advancing clock, not per-element transitions). **Star field**: grew from 9 to **70 deterministic stars**, each with a brightness `b` and a `reveal` threshold — bright stars show at dusk, fainter ones reveal the closer it gets to **true midnight** (a "light-pollution-clearing" effect) via a new **`nightDepth = clamp01(-sunElev)`** that PEAKS at midnight (unlike `wNight`, which saturates just past dusk); per-star `opacity = clamp01((nightDepth − reveal)/0.28) * b`, culled when invisible; the twinkle animation moved to **`fill-opacity`** so it multiplies with (rather than overrides) the per-star reveal opacity. **Shooting stars**: from ONE fixed rare streak to **6 scattered across the sky** (varied x/y, one down-left, staggered timing via inline CSS custom props `--sx/--sy/--ex/--ey/--dur`), still gated on `anim && isNight && clearSky` (clouds correctly hide them). **FX draw order** was reorganized to: sky + stars (background) → bodies → ground/landscape → **day/night FX (shooting stars, fireflies, leaves) in the FOREGROUND** → **weather FX (clouds, then precip/fog) FRONTMOST** (Sekmeht). **TDZ lesson (a real startup crash this session):** a module-level `const` array built at import time (`STARS = Array.from(...)`) called `clamp01`, a `const` arrow declared LATER in the file → temporal-dead-zone `ReferenceError` at load, "nothing renders." Build + tsc pass (valid code, runtime-only) — same blind spot as a deleted side-effecting statement. **Rule: a module-level array/object built at load must only call HOISTED `function`s (like `mixHex`) or `const`s declared ABOVE it — never a later `const` arrow; inline the helper if in doubt.**

---

## Sibling clients — feature reference (Genie · Frostbite · Profanity)

How the three popular DR/GS front-ends implement the features Lichborne also has — read from their source (`C:\temp\Genie4-Dev`, `C:\temp\Frostbite-Dev`, `C:\temp\Profanity\ProfanityFE`). Captured so we have grounded context when a tester asks "how does X do this?" or we're deciding Lichborne's approach. **The big axis is HOW MUCH the front-end does itself vs delegates to Lich:** Genie = everything native (Lich optional); Frostbite = lots native + its own Ruby scripting; **Profanity = thin presentation layer, ALL automation/scripting/mapping is Lich** (the model closest to Lichborne's stated philosophy). Lichborne sits between Profanity and Frostbite: a GUI config layer that implements *some* front-end automation (highlights/triggers/macros/aliases) for users who don't write Lich scripts, while pushing the heavy automation to Lich.

### The three at a glance
- **Genie** — C#/.NET, WinForms GUI. **Full-featured do-everything client**, Lich optional. One config panel per feature ([Forms/ConfigPanels/](file:///c:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Forms/ConfigPanels/) — `UCHighlightStrings/UCTriggers/UCAliases/UCSubs/UCIgnore/UCMacros/UCVariables/UCClasses/UCNames/UCPreset/UCWindows`). Its OWN scripting language (`.cmd` scripts + ~100 `#commands`, variables, `#if/#math/#goto`, classes) — [Core/Command.cs](file:///c:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Core/Command.cs) (the `#command` catalog is pitfall #48). Own StormFront XML parser ([Core/Game.cs](file:///c:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Core/Game.cs)). Genie also owns the **map XML format Lichborne's Genie view reads**.
- **Frostbite** — C++/Qt GUI. **Full GUI client + its own RUBY scripting** (scripts run as an external `QProcess`, talking back over TCP via `scriptapiserver`/`scriptstreamserver`; [gui/script.cpp](file:///c:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/gui/script.cpp), [scripts/lib/](file:///c:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/scripts/lib/) `ruby_goto.rb` etc. — a Lich-like Ruby model embedded in the client). Has a Lich integration dir ([gui/lich/](file:///c:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/gui/lich/)) AND its own SGE login (eauth/connectwizard), like Lichborne. Genie-format maps ([gui/maps/](file:///c:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/gui/maps/)).
- **Profanity (ProfanityFE)** — **Ruby, curses TUI, NO GUI, Lich-forward.** Connects to a *port* (`--port=8000`, i.e. Lich's port) — it has **no own login; Lich does connection/login**. It implements ONLY presentation/config: highlights, gags, key macros, stream→window routing, colors, layouts. It has **NO native triggers, aliases, general substitutes, variables, scripting, or mapping** — every bit of that is **Lich's job** (Lich scripts, `;alias`, vars, `;go2`/mapper). Clean Ruby lib ([lib/](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/) — `highlight_processor.rb`, `gag_patterns.rb`, `xml_tokenizer.rb`, `game_text_processor.rb`, `window_manager.rb`) + a hand-edited XML settings file, hot-reloaded with `.reload`. **This is the purest expression of Lichborne's "display & configuration layer over Lich" stance — when in doubt about whether to build automation in the client, Profanity is the "delegate to Lich" reference point.**

### Per-feature
- **Highlights.** *Genie:* three lists (string / line-begins-with / regex), stored as `SortedList`s keyed by the pattern text, applied to a RichTextBox via `SelectionColor`/`SelectionBackColor` — **per-property, last-in-(alphabetical)-order wins, NOT user-orderable.** *Frostbite:* HTML — wraps matches in nested `<span>`s walking the list top→bottom, so the **innermost/bottom-of-list color wins per-property**; a highlight can also carry **alert (sound) + timer actions** (so a Frostbite highlight doubles as a trigger). *Profanity:* `<highlight fg bg ul>regex` applied after XML strip; **specificity — smallest match wins — per-property** ([highlight_processor.rb](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/highlight_processor.rb)). *Lichborne (v0.11.3):* adopted **Profanity's model** (specificity + per-property compositing) — see the Automations note above for the full write-up + why.
- **Triggers.** *Genie:* dedicated `UCTriggers` — regex line → run command(s)/script, gated by classes. *Frostbite:* **no separate trigger system** — uses highlights-with-actions (sound/timer) for simple cases and Ruby scripts for real logic. *Profanity:* **none — Lich does triggers.** *Lichborne:* native trigger engine (WHEN→THEN, gates, cooldown, variable-watch) — richer than Genie's, the one place we're more "client-automation" than the Profanity ideal (deliberate: GUI users want triggers without scripting).
- **Macros / key bindings.** All three map a key → a "typed" string with a **cursor marker + escapes**. *Genie & Wrayth:* `@` = cursor, `\x` = clear, `\r`-less = wait. *Profanity:* `<key macro='...'>` with `\r` (send), `\x` (clear), `\@` (literal @), `@` (cursor), `\?` (backfill) + a rich **action** set (cursor/word-edit/kill-ring/window/tab/history) bound separately from macros. Lichborne already implements the `@`/`\@` cursor convention (pitfall #51); the kill-ring/word-edit actions are a Profanity idea we don't have.
- **Aliases.** *Genie:* `UCAliases` (`#alias`), `$1/$rest` args. *Frostbite:* via scripts/macros. *Profanity:* **none — Lich `;alias`.** *Lichborne:* native aliases with `$1/$rest`.
- **Gags (suppress lines).** *Genie:* `UCIgnore` (`#ignore`/`#gag`). *Frostbite:* `gui/text/alter/ignoresettings` (an "ignore" tab in its alter subsystem). *Profanity:* `<gag>` (all text) + `<combat_gag>` (combat stream only), regex, dropped before routing ([gag_patterns.rb](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/gag_patterns.rb)). *Lichborne:* **SHIPPED v0.12.0 as "Mutes"** (DESIGN §31; the Automations "Mutes & Substitutes" note above) — global by default with an optional per-rule stream restrict (a superset of Profanity's general/combat split), `line` or `match` scope, imported from all three legacy clients.
- **Substitutes (rewrite displayed text).** *Genie:* `UCSubs` (`#sub`/`#substitute`). *Frostbite:* `gui/text/alter/substitutionsettings` + `alter` (recolor/replace). *Profanity:* only a narrow **`perc-transform`** (rewrites spell-window text) — general subs are Lich's job. *Lichborne:* **SHIPPED v0.12.0 as "Substitutes"** (DESIGN §31) — native display-layer rewrite with `$N` capture refs, global by default, imported from Genie/Frostbite (Frostbite `target=Experience` mind-state rules flagged unsupported).
- **Variables.** *Genie:* `UCVariables` — user `$vars` + built-in game vars, used in scripts/triggers/macros. *Frostbite:* script/shared-data vars. *Profanity:* **none — Lich `Vars`.** *Lichborne:* built-in game-state vars (v0.11.3 catalog) + trigger-set vars; we deliberately do NOT persist a Lich-style var store (that's Lich).
- **Groups / classes / modes.** *Genie:* `UCClasses` — named on/off "classes" that gate highlights/triggers/aliases/macros. This is **exactly Lichborne's groups+modes** (DESIGN.md §8). Frostbite/Profanity have no direct equivalent.
- **Mapping.** *Genie:* its own map editor + the XML map format (Lichborne's Genie view consumes it). *Frostbite:* Genie-format maps in `gui/maps`. *Profanity:* **none — Lich's mapper/`;go2`** (it just shows a room window). Lichborne does both a Lich-image map and a Genie-XML map (DESIGN.md §19).
- **Scripting.** *Genie:* its OWN interpreted language (`.cmd` + `#commands`). *Frostbite:* **Ruby** subprocess + TCP API (Lich-like). *Profanity:* **none native — Lich Ruby scripts** are the whole scripting story. *Lichborne:* none native, and per Principle (display layer, not Lich-replacement) we **surface Lich scripts** rather than ship a script engine — the Profanity stance (see DESIGN.md §30 Lich-integration opportunities).
- **Parsers.** All four parse the same StormFront/SGE XML stream. *Genie:* `Core/Game.cs`. *Frostbite:* `gui/xml`. *Profanity:* a streaming tokenizer ([xml_tokenizer.rb](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/xml_tokenizer.rb) + `tag_handlers.rb` + `game_text_processor.rb`). *Lichborne:* `StormFrontParser` (stateful tokenizer, DESIGN.md §-game-text-pipeline). Useful when DR sends an oddly-shaped tag: cross-check how Profanity's `tag_handlers.rb` (closest in spirit — also Lich-fed) treats it.

### Takeaways for Lichborne
1. **Profanity is the philosophical north star** — when deciding whether a feature belongs in the client or in Lich, "Profanity delegates this to Lich" is a strong signal to surface-not-rebuild (esp. scripting, mapping/go2, persistent vars).
2. **Highlights specificity + per-property compositing (Profanity) beat list-order** for UX at scale — already adopted (v0.11.3).
3. **Gags and substitutes shipped in v0.12.0** (Mutes & Substitutes, DESIGN §31) — built native (display concern, must work without Lich), with Genie's global-scope model + an optional per-rule stream restrict, closing the former gap vs all three siblings.
4. **Frostbite proves a GUI client can host Ruby scripting** via a subprocess+TCP API — relevant if we ever want richer script *integration* (but our stance is surface Lich's, not host our own).
5. **Macro kill-ring / word-edit actions** (Profanity) are a low-cost input-ergonomics win we lack.

---

## Pitfalls (read before touching adjacent code)

> **Adding a new pitfall — read this first.** Pitfalls are numbered sequentially and the numbers ARE referenced from other comments / commit messages / docs (e.g. "see CLAUDE.md pitfall #33"). When adding a new one, **find the highest-numbered existing pitfall and add the new one AFTER it, with the next number** — do NOT insert before an existing pitfall or renumber an existing one. The natural editing instinct (using Edit with an existing pitfall as the anchor `old_string` and putting the new content first in `new_string`) puts the new pitfall in the wrong position; the correct anchor is the `---` separator at the END of the pitfalls list, with the new pitfall inserted between the last existing pitfall and that separator. Sekmeht caught me making this exact mistake three times across v0.8.7 and v0.8.8 (B121, B124, B126) — each time renumbering an older pitfall instead of just appending. The fix path when caught: revert the renumbered older pitfall to its original number, then append the new one at the end. The numbering is `1, 2, 3, ..., 31, 33, ...` (32 has been missing for ages; don't try to fix the gap, it's referenced from elsewhere by its current number).

1. **`app.getName()` returns `name`, not `productName`.** userData is `%APPDATA%\lichborne\` (lowercase). The `productName: "Lichborne"` under `build:` only affects installer / Start menu display. Mixing the cases caused a v0.6.4 hotfix to silently no-op.
2. **electron-builder NSIS `customInit` runs AFTER the previous uninstaller.** Use `preInit` and read the previous install location from `HKCU\Software\${UNINSTALL_APP_KEY}` (`$INSTDIR` isn't set that early).
3. **NEVER put user data inside the install directory.** NSIS `RMDir /r $INSTDIR` on every upgrade. Pre-v0.6.4 lost everyone's profiles this way.
4. **`StormFrontParser` is stateful and lives for the session lifetime.** Reset on new login. Stream-mode state can bleed across `<prompt>` boundaries.
5. **Scroll pinning fights you if you add naive useEffect logic.** Read GameWindow.tsx + DESIGN.md §23 before adding any programmatic scroll.
6. **Stream IDs are case-sensitive everywhere except `NEVER_DISCOVER`.** Lowercasing them anywhere will break Lich scripts. See B34.
7. **`lichPort` is the Lich front-end port, not an SGE shard port.** Don't look it up from a per-game table at credential build-time (v0.6.3 bug).
8. **`setState` in a mousemove handler must be gated on a hover sentinel** or you re-render on every pixel. See `GenieMapView.tsx` `onMouseMove` (gates on `dragRef.current`).
9. **Genie node rects are CENTERED on the XML position, not top-left anchored.** `ConvertPoint(pos, 4 * scale)` SUBTRACTS the offset (MapForm.cs:187–193). Anchoring top-left shifts every node 4px down-right and misaligns label clusters. Verify against Genie source for any map-rendering math change.
10. **`pointer-events: none` on the SVG pan group breaks click-to-walk.** `isDragging` flips true on mousedown BEFORE click fires — toggling `pointer-events` on the parent at that point makes the click target the SVG root, not the inner node `<g>`. Gate hover at the React layer (check `dragRef.current` in the hover handler) instead.
11. **Use `useLayoutEffect` for camera-follow.** The map's follow-the-player effect must update the transform in the same paint frame as the indicator's new world position. Plain `useEffect` produces a 1-frame "indicator at new spot, camera still old" flash at high walk rates.
12. **`useRef(initialValue)` initialized to a meaningful prop is a footgun.** The "did this change since last render" pattern requires `useRef(null)` (or whatever sentinel ≠ the first real value) so the first non-null render is treated as a change. See `lastLocationRef` in GenieMapView for the cautionary tale.
13. **Genie XML colors can be CSS color names, not just hex.** Some maps use `color="Blue"`, `"Red"`, `"Aqua"`, `"Lime"`, `"White"`. SVG `fill` accepts both, but `COLOR_LEGEND` and every effect lookup keys by hex. `normalizeNodeColor()` in `parseGenieZone` converts these to canonical hex at parse time so downstream code sees a single form. If a new room mysteriously has no aura or animation, check whether its color attribute is a named color we don't normalize.
14. **`opacity` SVG attribute conflicts with CSS animation on `opacity`.** Per SVG2 spec CSS wins, but having both set creates ambiguity that browsers can handle inconsistently. When applying an animated class to an SVG element, omit the `opacity` attribute (set to `undefined`) so CSS owns it cleanly. See the aura render's `opacityAttr` ternary.
15. **`indicator.id` is case-normalized to lowercase by the parser** (`raw.replace(/^Icon/i, '').toLowerCase()`) for the typed-flag checks AND the generic event payload. Renderer keys (`indicators.poisoned`, `indicators.bleeding`, etc.) are lowercase. Don't switch on `IconBLEEDING` directly downstream — match the lowercase form.
16. **If you change the `GenieZone` / `GenieNode` / `GenieArc` shape, bump `GENIE_CACHE_VERSION`** in `main.ts`. The parse cache stores the entire serialized zone graph; a shape change without a version bump means old caches deserialize into wrongly-shaped objects and produce silent runtime errors deep in the renderer. The version bump invalidates every user's cache on next launch with no manual cleanup.
17. **Map animations pause via the parent `<g>`'s class, not per-element.** `.genie-pan-dragging *` cascades `animation-play-state: paused` to all descendants. Don't add `pointer-events: none` to that group when toggling drag/motion — it would shift the click target off the inner node `<g>` and silently break click-to-walk (the mousedown sets the class before click fires).
18. **The map pan group and the current-room indicator must transition in LOCKSTEP.** Both carry `.genie-pan-smooth` (same `150ms linear`) and share the `snapTransform` flag. The indicator lives inside the pan group, so its screen position is `pan ∘ indicator`; if only the pan transitions while the indicator's world position jumps instantly, the halo bounces off-centre every walk step. Matched transitions make the interpolations cancel. Don't change one easing/duration without the other.
19. **No inline `height: 100%` on the `GenieMapView` outer wrap.** It's a flex child (`.map-canvas-wrap` → `flex: 1; min-height: 0`). An inline `height: 100%` overrides flex sizing and, evaluated against the parent's full height before the parent subtracts its own toolbar, pushes the MapPanel's view-selector toolbar off-screen at narrow window heights. Keep it `display: flex; flex-direction: column; minHeight: 0` and let CSS own the height.
20. **Room-state updates go through the rAF pump, not direct `setRoomState`.** Fast running emits multiple `room-title` events per frame; React 18 auto-batches them so only the last room survives and the map skips rooms. `roomQueueRef` + a `requestAnimationFrame` loop apply one per frame (cap 8). Don't bypass it — **except when `document.hidden`** (minimized/backgrounded), where the pump drains synchronously because rAF is throttled and would otherwise freeze room state (pitfall #71).
21. **`Home`/`End` are native (command-box cursor) when the command input is focused.** Only `Ctrl+Home`/`Ctrl+End` and the focus-elsewhere case scroll the story window. `PageUp`/`PageDown` always scroll. Testers expect text-editing keys to edit text (B77). Don't re-claim plain `Home`/`End` for scrolling.
22. **`LichBridge.interceptLine` suppression is poll-aware — don't make it match on output format alone.** The auto-poll's `;listall` response is consumed (hidden) so it doesn't spam the game window, but a player-typed `;list`/`;listall` produces the same format. `LichBridge.pollScriptList()` arms a 4s window; `interceptLine` consumes a matching line only while armed, otherwise lets it through (B79). Route the auto-poll through `pollScriptList()`, never `injector.pollScriptList()` directly.
23. **Never put CSS `contain` on `.text-line` / `.text-line-wrap` (the react-virtuoso rows).** Layout containment isolates each row from Virtuoso's own item-measurement / scroll-offset bookkeeping, so the scroll position can't be held stable when the list updates while the user is scrolled up — what they're reading gets dragged off-screen (B84). It was a v0.6.8 per-row perf hint, removed v0.6.12. The CSS carries DO-NOT-RE-ADD comments.
24. **An inactive character's GameWindow is `display:none` — its DOM measures 0×0.** Every inactive tab stays mounted and keeps processing game events (room titles, etc.), but `clientWidth`/`clientHeight`/`getBoundingClientRect` all read **0** until the tab is shown. Any layout-dependent logic must (a) guard against 0 dimensions so it doesn't write garbage (`centerOnCurrent`, `fitToView`, the follow `useLayoutEffect` all bail on `!w||!h`), and (b) re-run when the tab becomes visible again — GenieMapView uses a `ResizeObserver` on the SVG to recenter the camera on the 0→size transition. Without (b), a character that travels while its tab is hidden tabs back with the camera stranded rooms away. This is the canonical multi-character map pitfall: hidden ≠ unmounted, but hidden = unmeasurable.
25. **`LoginCredentials` must carry per-shard fields; main has no other source for which DragonRealms shard a connect is for.** Lich and SGE both need to know the shard (DR/DRX/DRT/DRF) — Lich because the launch flags (`--dragonrealms` vs `--test --dragonrealms` vs `--platinum --dragonrealms` vs `--fallen`) decide which front-end port it opens, SGE because the gameCode third arg to `authenticate()` decides which character list / login key it returns. Before v0.8.0, `LoginCredentials` had no `game` field, `App.tsx#runConnect` used the *global* `adv.lichPort` instead of the per-character port, `LichConnection.launch` hardcoded `'--dragonrealms'`, and `ConnectionManager` never passed gameCode to SGE — a 4-layer chain (B95) where DRT/DRX/DRF characters silently routed to DR at every layer. Rule now: every per-shard connection parameter rides in `LoginCredentials` — `game`, `lichArguments`, and `lichPort` (derived per-character from the canonical `GAMES` table in [lichSettings.ts](src/renderer/lichSettings.ts) via `gameOptionByCode()`, NOT taken from the global advanced settings). When adding a new shard or a new per-shard parameter, update both `LoginCredentials` and `GAMES`; don't keep a duplicate table in main.
26. **`CharacterProfile` has two ownership tracks; the GameWindow's debounced save must NOT clobber launcher-owned fields.** GameWindow owns `theme` + `state` (the dynamic localStorage-mirror map). Launcher owns `game`, `useLich`, `hidden`, `favorite`, `guild`, `circle`, `notes` — all written via the small read-modify-write helpers in [Launcher.tsx](src/renderer/components/Launcher.tsx) (`setCharacterFavorite`, `setCharacterHidden`, etc.) directly via `window.api.writeCharacterProfile`. Before v0.8.0, `exportCharacterProfile` ([profile.ts](src/renderer/profile.ts)) called `buildCharacterProfile` and wrote the result verbatim — which only knew the GameWindow's fields. Every debounced save from an active GameWindow (firing 2.5s after any per-character settings change) silently stripped favorite/hidden/notes/guild/circle AND reverted game/useLich to the stale session.* values, un-favoriting connected characters and bouncing back launcher-side pill changes (B97). `exportCharacterProfile` now does a **read-merge-write**: spread `built` first, then override launcher-owned fields from the existing YAML so they persist. When adding a new launcher-owned profile field: (a) add it to the `CharacterProfile` type as optional; (b) add it to the merge in `exportCharacterProfile`; (c) write it via a launcher helper, not through any GameWindow path. Don't try to extend `buildCharacterProfile` to know about launcher fields — they're authored from a different surface and the GameWindow doesn't have authoritative values for them.
27. **`discoveredStreams` must never contain a builtin `PanelType` id.** A "discovered" stream is one the game emits via `stream-declare` / `stream-push` events; the renderer adds it to the `discoveredStreams` array so the Panel Manager can surface it as a Custom row in Available Streams. But every builtin PanelType (`combat`, `room`, `exp`, `thoughts`, …) is ALSO offered as a built-in row from `ALL_PANEL_TYPES`. If the same id appears in both lists, PanelManager shows the stream twice — once as a builtin (correctly hidden after add via the `openTypes` filter) and once as a "custom" discovered row (the old `availableCustom` filter only checked `openCustomIds`, and a builtin tab has `type: 'combat'`, not `'custom'`, so the discovered row never hid). Clicking the second row added a duplicate tab with the same id (B100, combat). Root fix is at the discovery filter in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx): reject any id matching an entry in `ALL_PANEL_TYPES` in addition to the hand-curated `NEVER_DISCOVER` list — adding a new builtin PanelType is then automatically covered, no `NEVER_DISCOVER` bookkeeping needed. PanelManager's `availableCustom` filter also defensively excludes builtin-type ids and ids matching an open builtin tab, so a stale discoveredStreams from an older session can't reintroduce the duplicate. **When adding a new builtin PanelType, you don't need to touch `NEVER_DISCOVER`** — only add aliases the server might use (e.g. `experience` → `exp`) if any.
28. **Never call `navigator.clipboard.writeText` from the renderer. Always use `window.api.writeClipboard`.** The renderer's `setPermissionRequestHandler` / `setPermissionCheckHandler` (set up originally for the font picker's `queryLocalFonts`) refuse `navigator.clipboard.writeText` silently — Electron's internal permission name doesn't match a whitelist and the call returns a swallowed promise rejection. No error, no log, nothing reaches the system clipboard. This was B18 (auto-copy) in v0.1.9 and re-bit us as B102 (Debug Copy All) in v0.8.2 because DebugPanel was the one site that never got migrated. The fix every time is the same: route through `window.api.writeClipboard` → `write-clipboard` IPC → main's `clipboard.writeText` (which has no permission guard). When adding any new "copy to clipboard" UI, use the IPC channel from the start. Grep `navigator.clipboard` periodically — if a hit is in renderer code, it's a bug.
29. **Highlight / trigger regexes are compiled with `/g`; loops using `regex.exec()` must `lastIndex++` after a zero-width match.** Highlights compile via `new RegExp(...source, rule.caseSensitive ? 'g' : 'gi')` in [highlights.ts](src/renderer/highlights.ts). When walking matches with `while ((m = regex.exec(text)) !== null)`, a zero-width match (e.g. user pattern with an empty alternative like `(word1|word2|)`) leaves `lastIndex` at the same position and the loop spins forever. Both the renderer (`renderSegmentFull.tsx`) and the Fires log (`logHighlightFiresRef` in GameWindow) have this guard — copy the pattern when adding any new exec-loop. Also: don't use `regex.test()` if you want "does it match a NON-empty string" — `test()` returns true for empty matches. The Fires log used to use `test()` and logged phantom fires for malformed patterns until B101 (v0.8.2) replaced it with `exec()` + length check.
30. **Don't `encodeURIComponent` the `URL=` param of `https://www.play.net/bounce/redirect.asp`.** play.net's bounce takes the value after `URL=` *literally* — Genie's `FormMain.cs` LinkClicked path does raw string concatenation for exactly this reason. Encoding `://` to `%3A%2F%2F` makes the bounce page hand the browser a malformed destination ("site doesn't exist"). The F23 wrapper in [renderSegment.tsx](src/renderer/utils/renderSegment.tsx) ships intentionally raw (B105). The instinct on review is "URLs in query strings should be encoded" — that's the right instinct in general but wrong for this specific endpoint. Comment in the source explains why; preserve it. If the bounce's behaviour ever changes (it accepts encoded input), test by clicking a real external link, not by reading the resulting string.

31. **`dispatchUserText` is the canonical "process text as if the user typed it" path; don't bypass it with raw `window.api.sendCommand` when you want alias resolution + echo + history + log.** Extracted from `handleCommand` in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx) as part of v0.8.3 F07 (repeat-command macros). The two callers are (a) the command-bar Enter handler — `{ pushToHistory: true, clearInput: true }`, and (b) the macro token expansion site (`{RepeatLast}` / `{RepeatSecondToLast}` / `{ReturnOrRepeatLast}`) — `pushToHistory` and `clearInput` vary by token. Macro tokens are resolved at **fire time**, not interpolation time, because they reference live state (`historyRef.current` and `commandRef.current`) that doesn't fit into the string-substitution `interpolate(template, vars)` shape. The global keydown handler mounts once with empty deps, so it reaches `dispatchUserText` via `dispatchUserTextRef.current` (latest-instance mirror updated in a no-dep `useEffect`) and reaches the live command bar via `commandRef.current` (mirror of the `command` state, updated when state changes). If you add a new flow that programmatically sends user-equivalent input — a hotkey, a context menu "send", a script-driven replay — route it through `dispatchUserText` so it picks up aliases, the command echo, the session log, and the proper history-push policy automatically. `historyRef` push rule: only the bar's normal Enter and `{ReturnOrRepeatLast}` (typed case) push to history — RepeatLast/SecondToLast must NOT push when replaying, otherwise two presses of RepeatLast would re-pin the previous command and break the next RepeatSecondToLast. Two-press idempotence is part of the Stormfront/Wrayth contract testers expect.

33. **Accessibility overlays (high contrast, color blind) live on top of theme vars — never write theme vars without re-applying overlays.** `applySettingsToDOM` in [settings.ts](src/renderer/settings.ts) writes the active character's accessibility overlay vars *after* the theme vars (e.g. deuteranopia rewrites `--vital-health-ok-start` to a teal). The two writes share keys, so any `applyTheme` / `applyCustomTheme` call from any caller would silently erase the overlay if not followed by an overlay re-apply (B114). The fix is a `registerThemeAppliedHook(fn)` export in [themes.ts](src/renderer/themes.ts): `applyTheme` and `applyCustomTheme` call the hook after writing their vars. GameWindow's theme-apply effect registers a callback that closes over the active session's `settings` and re-runs `applySettingsToDOM(settings)` — so theme writes from ThemeEditor live editing, ThemePicker preview paths, and theme switching all get overlays re-applied automatically. Cleanup on effect teardown clears the hook so an unmounting GameWindow doesn't apply the wrong character's overlays after the next mount. Settings.ts can't import themes.ts directly without a circular dep, hence the registration pattern. When adding a new accessibility-style overlay (epilepsy-safe shapes, dyslexia-friendly font, etc.), add it to `applySettingsToDOM` — the hook will re-apply it after every theme write for free. Don't write overlay vars from outside `applySettingsToDOM` or you'll miss the post-theme re-apply path.

34. **Theme vars: panel-specific colors should cascade from the closest general `--*` var via `var(...)` in `darkBase`, not literal hex.** Established by B108 (`--map-bg` → `var(--bg-app)`) and broadened in B112 (8 panel text vars → `var(--text-secondary/muted/dim)`). The Theme Editor only exposes the *general* surface vars (App background, Game text, Labels, Muted text, etc.); custom themes built via the editor never set the specialty vars. With literal hex defaults in `darkBase`, custom themes were stuck with whatever value `darkBase` baked in — Rakkor's "Game Text" black on a light theme left Room / Hands / Exp panels stranded grey. Pattern when adding any new panel-specific text/bg/border var: pick the closest general var that matches the role (body text → `--text-primary` or `--text-muted`; section labels → `--text-secondary` or `--text-dim`; panel bg → `--bg-base`; panel surface bg → `--bg-app`) and default to `var(--general)`. Built-in themes (Parchment, Mist, Ruby, …) that need a distinct color *still* set the specialty var explicitly — `applyTheme` merges over `darkBase`, so an override always wins. Held / active accent colors (`--hand-held-color`, `--spell-active-color`, etc.) are the exception — they ARE the visual cue and should stay specialty-tinted. If you find yourself writing `'--new-thing-color': '#888888'` in `darkBase` and `#888` is also the value of `--text-muted`, that's the smell: write `'var(--text-muted)'` instead. If you find yourself adding a new specialty var to the Theme Editor schema *just so* light-theme users can override it, that's also the smell — make the cascade do the work.

35. **Built-in themes can share a display `name`; persistence + lookup keys on `id` only.** Established in v0.8.6 F35: both `{ id: 'classic', ... }` (dark) and `{ id: 'classic-light', ... }` (light) ship with `name: 'Classic'`. The two rows in the Theme Picker differentiate visually via the swatch dot (`item.swatches[0]` = black for the dark Classic, white for the light one). ThemePicker uses `item.id` for React keys ([ThemePicker.tsx](src/renderer/components/ThemePicker.tsx) `key={item.id}`) so no double-key warning. `initTheme` reads `localStorage.getItem('lichborne.theme')` (a saved id) and resolves via `THEMES.find(t => t.id === savedId)` — the display-name collision is never load-bearing. If a future contributor sees "two Classic" in the catalog and tries to rename one, they'll break the muscle-memory of testers who picked "Classic" expecting the white-bubble light theme. Keep the duplicate display name when the visual differentiation (swatch dot) is the intended affordance. Apply the same pattern when adding any future paired-theme set (e.g. a Slate Light, Mist Dark).

36. **Contact tracking has TWO long-running effects (last-seen + time-spent polling) that BOTH share the same `pendingContactsRef` buffer — every read AND every state-change must respect it.** Established in B119 + F34. The last-seen effect (fires on `roomState.players` change) builds a 2-second debounced buffer in `pendingContactsRef` to batch lastSeen / lastRoom / encounterCount updates. The 60s `timeSpentMs` polling tick reads contacts to add 60s to anyone in the room. Both effects MUST start from `pendingContactsRef.current ?? contactsRef.current` — using `contactsRef.current` alone misses in-flight buffer updates and the next `saveContacts` clobbers them. The buffer also gets cleared whenever `contacts` state changes externally (ContactsPanel save, import, polling-tick flush): a no-deps `useEffect([contacts])` nulls `pendingContactsRef` + `clearTimeout(lastSeenTimerRef)` — without this clearing, an in-flight buffer would write a stale snapshot back to localStorage and wipe whatever the user just added (B119: Rakkor's "save 12th contact, it disappears"). When adding a new contact-tracking effect, always: (a) base on `pendingContactsRef.current ?? contactsRef.current`, (b) write through `saveContacts` + `setContacts` + `scheduleProfileSave` together, (c) trust the B119 cleanup useEffect to drop your buffer when state changes externally. Don't write to `contactsRef.current` directly — it's a downstream mirror, not a source of truth.

37. **Encounter / presence detection needs TWO gates, not one — absence-threshold AND cooldown.** F34's `encounterCount` increments only when a contact is detected AND `(now - lastSeen) > ABSENCE_THRESHOLD_MS` AND `(now - lastEncounterAt) > ENCOUNTER_COOLDOWN_MS`. The absence-threshold (90s, > polling-tick 60s with a margin) gates "they actually LEFT since last seen" — without it, a contact who stays in your room for 10+ minutes ticks the counter every time `room.players` changes (someone else enters / leaves) because the last-encounter timestamp is old. The cooldown (10 min) gates "even if they left, don't double-count a quick exit-then-re-enter." `lastEncounterAt` updates only on actual increments; `lastSeen` updates on every detection. Both timestamps are needed and serve different purposes — don't fold them. When adding any new contact-state-transition feature (e.g. "first seen on day X" badges), think in terms of presence-edge detection rather than just "is this contact here right now," and use the same absence-threshold + cooldown shape so we don't end up with multiple half-correct definitions of "encountered."

38. **`lichborne:open-quick-send` custom DOM event is the canonical way to open QuickSend from anywhere outside AppShell.** Established in F33 v0.8.6. AppShell owns the QuickSend modal state and listens for the event; on receipt it queries the visible `.session-shell:not(.session-shell--hidden) .command-input` for the value and opens QuickSend prefilled — the same DOM read the keyboard handler does for Ctrl+Shift+Enter. Use the event rather than prop-drilling an `onOpenQuickSend` callback through every GameWindow / panel — AppShell is already DOM-aware for this path, and the event keeps the source-of-input logic in one place. If you add a new "send a command somewhere else" entry point (a context menu item, a panel button, etc.), dispatch `document.dispatchEvent(new CustomEvent('lichborne:open-quick-send'))`. Don't dispatch the event with a payload — the event handler's contract is "open with whatever's in the active command bar" and adding payload-based behavior would split that contract.

39. **Panel Manager has two ownership dimensions; don't conflate "slot added" with "slot has streams".** v0.8.1 introduced explicit add/remove of panel locations — the 4 slots (Main-Top, Top-Right, Middle-Right, Bottom-Right) each carry an `*Added` boolean (`mainTopAdded` / `topAdded` / `midAdded` / `bottomAdded`) that controls whether the slot renders in the game window. The slot's `tabs` array controls which streams live in it. The two are independent. An added slot with empty tabs renders an `EmptyPanelSlot` placeholder; a removed slot can still have tabs in the array — *that's not necessarily a bug*. `removePanelZone` clears the tabs when the user explicitly removes, but the **migration default for `mainTopTabs` was `[]` as of v0.8.3** (was `[room, combat]` in v0.8.1–v0.8.2) precisely because the default + `mainTopAdded=false` produced "phantom tabs in an un-added zone" — invisible to the user but visible to any code that aggregates tabs across zones. **Anywhere code aggregates tabs across the four zones, it MUST gate on the `*Added` flag.** Two sites currently do this (both fixed in B106/B107): (a) `watchedStreamsRef` in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx) — used by `STREAM_FALLBACK` routing; without the gate, phantom tabs claim their streams as "watched" and lines like combat / conversations silently buffer instead of falling back to main. (b) `allTabs` in [PanelManager.tsx](src/renderer/components/PanelManager.tsx) — used by `openCustomIds` and `openTypes`; without the gate, phantom tabs hide discovered streams from Available Streams, leaving the user with no path to re-add a stream to a visible slot (this was Legiro's moonwatch / Moons bug). New code that mutates tabs (`addToZone`, `moveTabToZone`) auto-flips the `*Added` flag on as a safety so adding a stream to a removed slot doesn't leave it invisible. Migration defaults when the flag is missing: **Main-Top → false** (new zone, explicit opt-in), other three → **true** (preserve v0.8.0 always-visible). When adding a fifth panel location in the future, follow the same pattern: new `*Added` state + scopedKey persistence + migration default + render-gate in GameWindow + `addPanelZone`/`removePanelZone` handlers + PanelManager UI entry + **audit every cross-zone aggregation site to gate on the new flag**.

40. **`newDiscovered` in GameWindow's event batch must dedupe WITHIN the batch, not just against existing state.** Established in B123 (v0.8.7). The event loop in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx) translates every incoming `stream-declare` AND `stream-push` event into a push to a per-batch `newDiscovered: string[]`. The dedup filter at the `setDiscoveredStreams` site checks `existing.has(id)` (against pre-batch state) but originally did NOT track ids it had already added in the same pass. A Lich script that emits `<streamWindow id='X'/>` immediately followed by `<pushStream id='X'/>` produces both events in a single batch; both push `'X'` into `newDiscovered`; both pass the `existing` check (since `X` isn't in `discoveredStreams` yet); both get appended → array becomes `['X', 'X']`. PanelManager renders one row per array entry, so the user sees two identical "Available Streams" rows; adding either makes `openCustomIds.has('X')` true and filters out BOTH rows (this is also how to recognize the bug — adding "one" of two identical-name rows hiding both is a duplicate-id signature, not a display bug). The fix is a `seenInBatch: Set<string>` local to the filter; first entry in a batch passes and gets recorded, duplicates within the same batch are rejected. When adding a new stream-discovery event type in the future (a hypothetical third tag that should also surface a stream), route it through the same `newDiscovered` push site so the existing dedup catches it for free. If you add a separate write site, replicate the `seenInBatch` pattern. The corresponding parser invariant: `stream-declare` (from `<streamWindow>`) and `stream-push` (from `<pushStream>`) deliberately emit independently — script writers' intent is "make sure the UI knows this stream exists" with multiple safety nets, and stripping one of them at the parser layer would break legitimate scripts. Dedup is the renderer's job.

41. **Room sub-stream stale-clear lives at the parser, not the GameWindow event batch.** Established in B121 (v0.8.7). The Room panel's structured sections (`room`, `room-objects`, `room-players`, `room-creatures`, `room-extra`, `room-exits`) get populated from `<component id='room ...'/>` tags. When DR doesn't re-emit a component for a room transition (common — DR is sparse with re-emits unless `LOOK` forces them), the previous room's data carries over and surfaces as ghost players / objects in the Room panel until a manual `LOOK`. **The wrong place to fix this is GameWindow's event batch loop** (which is where I tried first): track which sub-streams "were seen" in this batch, clear the rest on title change. The fatal failure: IPC batches can split title-change from component updates across multiple batches. A batch carrying only the new title with no component re-emits would falsely "see no players this batch" and wrongly clear data the next batch was about to populate. **The right place is the parser** ([StormFrontParser.ts](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts)). DR's XML protocol orders `<streamWindow>` (which carries the subtitle = room title) BEFORE any `<component id='room ...'/>` for the new room — deterministic, single-batch-or-not. New `lastRoomTitle: string` field on the parser; in the streamWindow handler, when `cleanTitle !== lastRoomTitle` emit `clear-stream` for all six room sub-streams BEFORE the typed `room-title` event. Components that DO arrive then re-populate via their own clear+stream-text flow; sections that DON'T arrive stay correctly empty. The `lastRoomTitle` gate prevents a no-op streamWindow re-emit (same subtitle, DR sends these for non-transition repaints) from clobbering freshly-populated sub-stream data. **B117 compatibility**: the parser's `captureSegments` work for monsterbold lives inside the `<component>` handler which fires AFTER the streamWindow pre-emit clear-streams — bold capture is unaffected. **Downstream beneficiary — contacts tracking**: the F34 encounter / `timeSpentMs` effects iterate `roomState.players`, so before B121 they were ingesting carryover ghost players from the previous room and crediting time-spent against the wrong room. B121's clear at the parser cascades to a clean `roomState.players: []` during the transition gap, so contacts stats are now accurate by construction (no separate fix needed for F34). **Don't move this logic back into GameWindow** — every fix at that layer has to know about batch boundaries, which makes it brittle. The parser sees the raw tag stream and knows the ordering. **Reset on session boundary**: `lastRoomTitle` is cleared in `parser.reset()` alongside other per-session state, so the first room of a new session always triggers clear-streams.

42. **Lichborne-source imports bypass the `ImportCandidate` intermediate; new rule types must update the bypass, not just the intermediate.** Established in B124 (v0.8.7). The import wizard's neutral intermediate at [types.ts](src/renderer/import/types.ts) (`ImportHighlight` / `ImportTrigger` / `ImportMacro` / `ImportAlias`) was designed to model the union of Wrayth / Genie / Frostbite source formats — it does NOT model the full native Lichborne rule shape. `ImportHighlight` has no `bold` / `glow` / `glowColor` / `groupIds` / `allGroups` / `name` / `enabled`; `ImportTrigger` has no `gates` / `oneShot` / `cooldownSeconds` / `watchStream` / nested action ordering / `groupIds` / `allGroups` / `name` / `enabled`; `ImportMacro` / `ImportAlias` are similarly trimmed. When F29 (Lichborne→Lichborne) shipped in v0.8.4, it routed everything through this intermediate, and the mapper at [mapper.ts](src/renderer/import/mapper.ts) hardcoded defaults for every field the intermediate didn't carry — silent data loss on round-trip across every rule type. **The fix shape**: `ImportResult` carries an optional `nativeRules?: { highlights, triggers, macros, aliases }` block (loose `unknown[]` typing to avoid a circular import with the rule modules). The lichborne.ts parser populates it in lockstep with the ImportCandidate arrays, spreading the source rule object and overriding `id: nanoid()` (and for triggers, every nested `TriggerAction.id` regenerates too). [ImportWizard.tsx](src/renderer/components/ImportWizard.tsx)'s `doImport` checks `result.nativeRules` and prefers it over `mapImportResult(...)` output when present; non-Lichborne sources leave it undefined and fall through to the legacy mapper path. **When adding a new rule type** (e.g. a future "scene", "snippet", "schedule"…), the new type needs: (a) full shape in the native rule module with `id` + `name` + `enabled` + `groupIds` + `allGroups` like every existing one; (b) an entry in `LichborneExportFile` and the parser's `nativeRules` block at [lichborne.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/lichborne.ts) that spreads the source and regenerates ids; (c) an apply branch in `doImport` mirroring the existing highlights/triggers/macros/aliases shape — content-based dedup key, append-merge filter, save call. The ImportCandidate intermediate is **only** for surfacing the rule in the wizard preview UI; if you don't need preview support for the new type, you don't need an ImportCandidate at all (just `nativeRules`). The cardinal sin is the reverse — adding the field to ImportCandidate + mapper but forgetting to extend `LichborneExportFile`'s parser shape, which would re-introduce the B124 loss pattern. **Don't trust loaded rules to have default fields** — the runtime stores assume rules saved by Lichborne have all required fields, but a hand-edited YAML or a malformed export could be missing them. Defensive normalization belongs at the `loadHighlights`/`loadTriggers`/etc. layer, not the import boundary; we don't have it today because exports always come from `loadHighlights(character)` which returns runtime-complete shapes. Add it only when a tester actually hits a malformed-import crash.

43. **When the user can manually scroll past where the scroll API thinks the bottom is, the bug is in LAYOUT, not scroll math.** Established in B122 across v0.8.7 → v0.8.8. The half-row clip at font 13+ ate three failed hypotheses before landing on a real fix: (a) v0.8.7 lowered a `totalListHeightChanged` threshold from 2px → 0.5px — didn't help; (b) v0.8.8 first attempt replaced raw `el.scrollTop = el.scrollHeight - el.clientHeight` with `virtuosoRef.current?.scrollToIndex({ align: 'end' })` on the theory Virtuoso's internal accounting differed — didn't help; (c) Sekmeht's diagnostic — "I can manually scroll down ~half a row past where the snap lands" — proved BOTH APIs agreed on the wrong target. When two independent scroll APIs converge on the same position but the DOM has scrollable content past that position, the issue is in CSS / layout, not in the math. The fix that worked: a `components.Footer` on Virtuoso (`<div style={{ height: 14 }} />`, fixed 14px, gated to `settings.fontSize >= 13`) — defensive layout slack that doesn't require knowing why the scroll APIs land short. **General principle**: scroll-snap math problems are usually solvable by adding layout slack rather than by chasing what the math is doing. If you're tempted to write a third hypothesis-based fix to scroll math, stop — add invisible padding below the content instead. Specific to this case: the 14px footer is **gated on font ≥ 13** because at font 12 and below row heights round to clean integer pixels and no clip occurs; the slack would just be empty space below the last row (visible gap above the vitals strip). **Pair fix shipped in same release**: a separate `useEffect([settings.fontSize, settings.lineHeight, settings.largePrint])` re-snaps via `scrollToIndex({ align: 'end' })` ONLY when `pinnedRef.current` was already true — font / line-height / large-print changes reshape every row's height, growing scrollHeight, leaving the previously-pinned scrollTop short of the new bottom. Bail on `!pinnedRef.current` so scrolled-up readers aren't yanked back. rAF before the snap so Virtuoso has a frame to re-measure rows at the new dimensions. The threshold check in `totalListHeightChanged` is left at 0.5 (responsive) but doesn't carry the load — the footer does. **SUPERSEDED (v0.11.4, B153 — Rakkor reported the clip back at font ≥ 13; the footer was REMOVED.)** The real diagnosis (after several wrong turns): at font ≥ 13 the pinned view rests exactly **one line short** of the bottom — the decisive tester clue was "I can always wheel down one notch to reveal it," i.e. the true DOM bottom *is* reachable, the auto-follow just wasn't getting there. Cause: Virtuoso's `followOutput` lands at "last item at viewport bottom" but **under-measures the last row at fractional heights** (a row is `min-height: 1.4em` + `0.15em` wrap padding ≈ 1.55em, non-integer at font ≥ 13), so the last line lands clipped — AND `followOutput` runs *after* the synchronous bottom-correction in `totalListHeightChanged`, overriding it. **Two documented dead ends — do not retry:** *(1)* **integer per-row pixel heights** (`ceil(font × line-height)` on `.text-window .text-line`) — did NOT help; the short-landing is followOutput under-measurement + override, not row-height rounding. *(2)* a **font-scaled `components.Footer`** (slack to scroll into) — once the correction below reached the true bottom, any footer just became a one-line **gap** (last line a row ABOVE the vitals bar instead of flush), and it under/over-shot non-monotonically right around font 13–14 (so the bug looked "font-13-specific" — it was just the footer math crossing over there). **The actual fix: defer the raw bottom scroll into a `requestAnimationFrame`** in `totalListHeightChanged` ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)) — `el.scrollTop = el.scrollHeight - el.clientHeight` inside a rAF runs AFTER `followOutput` and wins, landing at the genuine DOM bottom (DOM `scrollHeight` is immune to Virtuoso's internal under-measurement). Last line sits flush at every font, **no footer, no clip, no gap.** `scrollToBottom` (End key) and the font re-snap do the same rAF raw correction after their `scrollToIndex({align:'end'})`. The re-snap effect also arms `suppressUntilRef` **synchronously before** the rAF (not only inside it), because the relayout on a font change (rows AND the command bar both grow — the command bar scales with `--game-font-size`, pitfall #45) balloons `scrollHeight` while `scrollTop` holds, so `dist` crosses the 40px deadband and `handleVirtuosoScroll` un-pinned BEFORE the rAF ran → the re-snap bailed, the "N new lines" badge appeared, and the view stranded ~1 line up. **Lessons:** (a) when a pinned virtual list rests one line short but the bottom is wheel-reachable, the auto-follow (`followOutput`) is under-measuring and the fix is a DOM-truth `scrollTop = scrollHeight - clientHeight` correction — but it must be DEFERRED to a rAF to win the race against `followOutput`; (b) a "slack footer" only masks a short-landing and turns into a visible gap the moment the scroll actually reaches bottom — fix the scroll, don't pad the content; (c) integer rows are NOT the lever for a followOutput short-landing.

44. **The Room panel must mirror the main scroll's styling for the same content.** Established in B117 (v0.8.5, monsterbold creatures), reinforced in v0.8.8 (line-mode highlights for treasures). DR's `<component id='room players'/>` / `room objs` / `room creatures` / `room extra` sections are the exact same content that appears in the main scroll's "You also see ...", "Also here: ...", and (for desc) the room paragraph. Anything that styles that content in the main scroll — server-pushed bold/color, user contact name highlights, user match-scope highlights, user line-mode highlights — should style the structured Room panel sections the same way. Two things flow from this: (1) **the parser's `captureSegments` must carry the same styling fields as `pushSegment`** (currently: `bold` from B117; future styling sources will need to be added to both). When you add a new styling field to TextSegment (a `class`, `linkType`, whatever), update both the main-scroll `pushSegment` AND the capture path in `text()`'s `captureSegments.push`. (2) **RoomPanel's `renderSegments` must pass every kind of rule that TextLineRow passes** — `matchRules` (B111), `lineRules` (Rakkor v0.8.8), contacts, contact templates, nameRegex. The line-style is computed PER-SECTION (objects/players/creatures/extra each compute their own `getLineHighlightStyle` off their own joined text) so a rule that matches a player name paints only the Players section, not the others. `desc` deliberately stays out of line-style scope because it's multi-sentence prose where a single match would over-paint a large block. **B111's original "lineRules excluded on purpose" exclusion was overcautious and got overturned in v0.8.8** — the documented "lobster paints the whole section" objection turned out to be the wrong call: in the main scroll the same content gets that same paint when the user authored a line-mode rule, and consistency between surfaces beat the theoretical objection. Future "should the Room panel apply X?" questions should default to YES if the main scroll applies X for the same content. **(v0.14.7, F52: the panel now renders these sections as PROSE lines — the game's own sentences verbatim, no labels, exits as a clickable "Obvious paths:" text line last, matching all three sibling clients. The rule above is unchanged — "per-section" is now per-prose-line; the paint pipeline is identical. Exit links send FULL direction words — the compass token `dn` is not a valid DR command. Don't reintroduce buttons/labels without a fresh tester ask.)**

45. **UI that should scale with `Settings → Font Size` must use `em` (inheriting from `.game-toolbar`) or `var(--game-font-size)` directly. Never `rem` for game-area UI.** Established in B113 (text weight pass), reinforced in v0.8.8 Mode button fix. `rem` is anchored to the browser root font-size (~16px) and ignores the user's per-character `settings.fontSize`. So a button declared as `font-size: 0.75rem` renders at a fixed 12px regardless of whether the user picked 8 or 24 in Settings. Three sizing categories in the codebase: **(a) toolbar buttons** like `.btn-debug` / `.btn-theme` / `.btn-settings` use `font-size: 1.0em` and inherit from `.game-toolbar` (which itself scales). New toolbar buttons should match this pattern — the Mode button shipped with `0.75rem` and visibly drifted smaller as users bumped their font size; v0.8.8 fixed it to `1.0em`. **(b) Portaled popovers** (Mode switcher menu, contact popover) can't inherit from `.game-toolbar` because they're mounted to `document.body` via React portal. Use `var(--game-font-size)` directly with a multiplier (e.g. `calc(var(--game-font-size) * 0.85)` for smaller sub-text). **(c) Text-line content** uses `var(--panel-font-size, var(--game-font-size))` to support the F31 per-panel override with a fallback to the global. When adding any new UI surface in the game area, grep for `rem` in the new CSS before committing — every `rem` is a fixed pixel size that won't track user preference. App chrome (settings panels, modal headers, etc.) can use `rem` deliberately if it should NOT scale with game font, but that's the exception, not the default.

46. **DR's room-transition data arrives in TWO independent XML tags; the parser must read both, not just one.** Established in B126 (v0.8.8). When the player moves to a new room, DR usually emits both: (a) `<streamWindow id='main' subtitle='[Title - rmId]'/>` — carries the room title and room id together inside the subtitle bracket, parsed in [StormFrontParser.ts:441-484](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts#L441-L484), and (b) `<nav rm='X'/>` — carries the new room id as an attribute, parsed in [StormFrontParser.ts:523-548](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts#L523-L548). For most transitions both arrive together so reading just `<streamWindow>` is sufficient. **But some transition shapes (teleports, NPC-induced moves, certain scripted moves) emit ONLY `<nav rm>` and skip `<streamWindow>` entirely.** For those, a front-end that reads only `<streamWindow>` will have `roomState.title` and `roomState.roomId` frozen on the prior room until a manual `LOOK` forces a re-emit. Lich's `$room` variable is correct the whole time because Lich's scripting reads `attrs.rm` from `<nav>` independently — that's the canary: when `;e $room` shows the right room but the Lichborne map shows the wrong one, we missed a `<nav rm>` somewhere. **The fix shape**: a separate `RoomIdEvent` (not an overloaded `RoomTitleEvent`) — emit `{ type: 'room-id', roomId: N }` from the `<nav>` handler when `attrs.rm` is numeric. The handler in GameWindow routes it into `roomUpdates.roomId` ONLY — leaves title / desc / sub-streams alone, because forging an empty string for fields we don't have would wipe the only data we have (the prior room's title is at least *something* to display until a real `<streamWindow>` arrives). **Don't overload RoomTitleEvent with an empty title for the `<nav>` case** — `GameWindow`'s `case 'room-title'` does `roomUpdates.title = evt.title` unconditionally; an empty title would clear the prior title and the Room panel would go blank. Two events with different invariants is the right separation. **Scope of the Lich Map fix**: it's not a fix for the Room panel's title-display (only `<streamWindow>` carries the title string), and not a fix for Genie Map (its resolver is title+desc+exits-based, not roomId-based — the Genie data has no room ids; the exit-aware cross-zone hold in `resolveGenieRoom`, pitfall #70, handles Genie's variant of the symptom). **General rule**: when extracting data from a stateful XML stream, audit every place the same data could appear. Room id is in two places (streamWindow subtitle + nav rm); both need handlers. The same audit should apply for any future "data appears in multiple tags" case.

47. **Save calls on multi-category data sources must be gated per-type on `incoming.length > 0`.** Established in B127 (v0.8.9). The import wizard's `doImport` writes to four independent per-character stores: highlights, triggers, macros, aliases. Plus four F29-native stores: groups, modes, contacts, contactTemplates. Different source types fill different subsets of these — Wrayth's parser returns `[]` for triggers and aliases (Wrayth's XML doesn't carry them); Frostbite returns `[]` for triggers, aliases, and contacts; Genie returns all five; F29 returns whatever the source character had. Pre-v0.8.9, BOTH the Append and Replace branches in [ImportWizard.tsx](src/renderer/components/ImportWizard.tsx) `doImport` called `saveX(character, mapped.X)` (or `[...existing, ...keepX]` in Append) for ALL four rule types regardless of whether `mapped.X` was empty. The catastrophic failure mode was Replace: `saveTriggers(character, [])` wipes the user's existing triggers when the current import has no triggers. Append was mathematically a no-op for empty arrays but indistinguishable in correctness from a future regression — the right shape is to gate the save itself, not rely on save-array math being benign. **The fix shape**: every save call (rules AND F29 native data) gated on `mapped[type].length > 0` (or `result.nativeX.length > 0` for native data — the outer `result.nativeX && Array.isArray(...)` check passes for empty arrays too because `[]` is truthy and `Array.isArray([])` is `true`, so a Lichborne F29 export from a character with no groups would have wiped the recipient's groups on Replace pre-fix). **When adding a new rule type** to the import system (e.g. a future "scene", "snippet", "schedule"…), follow the same pattern: gate every `saveX(...)` call on the corresponding `mapped[type].length > 0`. The Append-branch dedup math (`[...existing, ...keepX]`) is still correct for non-empty incoming and should run normally. **When adding a new parser** that doesn't carry some rule types (like Wrayth doesn't carry triggers), explicitly return `[]` arrays for the missing types — don't omit the field from the result object, because every consumer assumes the field exists. The per-type guards mean the empty array just no-ops the save; no special handling needed at the parser level.

48. **Genie's complete `#command` catalog lives at [Genie4 source Command.cs:270](C:\temp\Genie4-Dev\Genie4\Core\Command.cs#L270) (`switchExpr = oArgs[0].Substring(1).ToLower()` then ~100 case branches). When adding a new import-side recognizer, check the full catalog first to identify aliases — Genie has multiple `#commands` for the same operation.** Established in B133 (v0.8.9). The clean mappings to Lichborne action types are deliberately narrow because most Genie commands have no front-end equivalent: **(a) Game commands** — `#send`, `#put`, `#q`, `#que`, `#queue` → `command` action; **(b) Variables** — `#var`, `#variable`, `#setvar`, `#setvariable`, `#tvar`, `#tempvar`, `#tempvariable`, `#svar` → `variable` action (Lichborne doesn't distinguish var scope at the action layer — temp/saved/string/server vars all collapse to the same action); **(c) Sounds** — `#play`, `#playsound`, `#playwave` → `sound` action; **(d) Beep** — `#beep`, `#bell` → `beep` action; **(e) Flash** — `#flash` → `flash` action; **(f) Echo** — `#echo` → `echo` action; **(g) Log** — `#log` → `log` action. **Everything else gets dropped with a "Unsupported actions skipped: #X, #Y" note in the import preview** via the catch-all `else { dropped.push(part) }` at the end of `parseActionParts` in [genie.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/genie.ts). The non-mappable categories: **rule manipulation** (`#trigger`, `#untrigger`, `#alias`, `#unalias`, `#macro`, `#unmacro`, `#highlight`, `#unhighlight`, `#class`, `#unclass`, `#name`, `#unname`, `#gag`, `#ungag`, `#sub`, `#unsub`, `#substitute`, `#unsubstitute`, `#ignore`, `#unignore`, `#squelch`, `#unsquelch`, `#unvar`, `#unvariable`, `#unsetvar`, `#unsetvariable` — modify rules at runtime, which Lichborne's static rule model doesn't support); **UI/window control** (`#statusbar`, `#window`, `#position`, `#layout`, `#show`, `#hide`, `#close`, `#edit` — Genie-specific UI); **connection control** (`#connect`, `#disconnect`, `#exit`, `#reconnect`, `#lc`, `#lconnect`, `#lichconnect`, `#ls`, `#lichsettings` — would let a trigger forcibly disconnect; user should do this from the UI); **system/config control** (`#plugin`, `#load`, `#save`, `#reload`, `#unload`, `#config`, `#set`, `#setting`, `#settings`, `#profile`); **movement/mapping** (`#mapper`, `#map`, `#walk`, `#walkto`, `#go`, `#goto`, `#path` — could partially map to Lich `;go2` but routing differs); **scripting flow** (`#if`, `#parse`, `#regex`, `#regexp`, `#do`, `#goto`, `#true`, `#false`, `#wait`, `#waitfor`, `#pause`, `#abort`, `#resume`); **math/random/eval** (`#math`, `#evalmath`, `#random`, `#eval` — Lichborne variable actions only store, don't compute); **custom Genie events** (`#event`, `#events`). **`##escape` syntax** — Genie uses `##text` to send a literal `#text` to the game (escape for the `#` prefix); the parser strips the leading `#` and treats as a plain command. **Explicit no-ops** — `#nop` and `#comment` are silently dropped without "Unsupported" warning since the user never intended them to do anything; flagging them would scare users with a useless note. **`#send #X` / `#put #X` recursive shape** — see pitfall #X (TODO if separate, otherwise documented inline in [genie.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/genie.ts) at the COMMAND_PREFIX_RE branch). When the inner content of a send/put wrapper itself starts with `#`, recursively process via `parseActionParts` instead of treating as a DR command — this handles user-error shapes like `#send #flash` (Jaded's B130 case).

49. **`STREAM_FALLBACK` and DR's native protocol duplication can double-count.** Established in B136 (v0.8.10). DR's XML protocol sends some streams TWICE per server event — once inside a `<pushStream id="X"/>` block (which routes to the X panel), and once OUTSIDE the block to main directly. **Speech and whispers do this; thoughts / arrivals / deaths / etc. do not.** A `say hi` produces literally: `<pushStream id="talk"/><preset id='speech'>You say</preset>, "Hi."<popStream/><preset id='speech'>You say</preset>, "Hi."` — two complete copies, the second going to whichever stream is active outside the pushStream block (typically `main`). Lichborne's [`STREAM_FALLBACK`](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx) routes unwatched stream content to a fallback (typically `main`) so important text doesn't get silently buffered. **Adding a STREAM_FALLBACK entry for a stream that DR already natively duplicates to main produces double-counting** — the inside-pushStream copy gets fallback-routed to main on top of DR's outside-pushStream copy. Symptom: "You say, Hi." appears twice in main when no panel watches that stream. **Rule**: when adding a new stream to STREAM_FALLBACK, FIRST check whether DR natively emits an outside-pushStream copy for that stream. If yes (speech / whispers — and any future stream that follows that pattern), DO NOT add a fallback entry. If no (thoughts, arrivals, deaths, custom Lich script streams that emit only inside the pushStream block), add the fallback. The B136 fix removed `conversation: 'main'` from STREAM_FALLBACK for exactly this reason; the comment block at the STREAM_FALLBACK declaration documents the principle inline. **How to check**: open Debug → Raw XML, do a `say test`, look for two consecutive copies of the speech in the XML capture — one inside `<pushStream id="talk"/>...<popStream/>`, one immediately after. If you see that pattern, the stream is natively duplicated and shouldn't have a fallback.

50. **Stream id aliases live in [`src/shared/streamAliases.ts`](src/shared/streamAliases.ts); use `normalizeStreamId(id)` everywhere a stream id crosses a boundary.** Established in B135 (v0.8.10). Pre-v0.8.10, the parser had its own inline `STREAM_MAP` constant for translating server / legacy / sibling-client stream names to Lichborne panel ids (e.g. `talk` → `conversation`, `death` → `deaths`). When we needed the same translation in the renderer's `echoToStream` (so imported Genie triggers with `#echo >talk` would land in the right panel) and in the import parsers (so legacy plural references on imported triggers got rewritten), the choices were either (a) duplicate the map in each module — error-prone drift risk — or (b) extract to shared. The shared module is `STREAM_ID_ALIASES` (the bare map) + `normalizeStreamId(id)` (helper that returns id unchanged if not aliased). Used at: parser's `<pushstream>` / `<streamwindow>` handlers, parser's `<clearstream>` handler (uses `STREAM_ID_ALIASES[id]` directly to preserve COMPONENT_STREAM fallback chain), renderer's `echoToStream` in GameWindow, Genie parser's `parseEchoAction` (normalizes `>stream` tokens at import time), F29 `lichborne.ts` parser (normalizes legacy `watchStream` / `echoStream` on imported triggers). **When adding a new alias** (e.g. a future Lich script emits a new variant id you want to merge into an existing panel), add ONE entry to `STREAM_ID_ALIASES`. All five call sites pick it up automatically. **When adding a new builtin panel type**: add the canonical id to [`PanelFrame.tsx`](src/renderer/components/PanelFrame.tsx) `PanelType` / `PANEL_LABELS` / `ALL_PANEL_TYPES` AND add a switch case for it. If multiple ids should route to it, add aliases too. **When renaming an existing panel id** (B135's `conversations` → `conversation` precedent): write a localStorage migration in [`src/renderer/localStorageMigrations.ts`](src/renderer/localStorageMigrations.ts) that walks per-character tabs / activeIds / panelFontSizes keys / trigger watchStream values. **Case-insensitive matching** in the migration is important — user data may include custom-typed tabs created from a discovered stream id with arbitrary casing (e.g. `'Conversations'` if Lich emitted `<streamWindow id='Conversations'/>` at some point). **Dedupe pass after rename** is also important — if a user had both the builtin tab AND a custom variant, both collapse to the new id and the duplicate should be dropped, not left as two visible duplicate panels. **Migration flag bumping** (e.g. `conversationRename` → `conversationRename2` → `conversationRename3`) is the recovery mechanism if a draft migration ships with a bug — bumping the flag re-runs the (now-fixed) migration on every user's next launch. **When writing a rename migration, walk NESTED fields too — not just top-level**. The v0.8.10 retroactive sweep caught a real example: the trigger handler in `localStorageMigrations.ts` originally only renamed `t.watchStream` but a `TriggerRule` also has `t.actions[]` with `echoStream` on echo actions. A pre-v0.8.10 user with a trigger that echoed to the legacy panel id had stale `echoStream` left after the migration — functionally OK via runtime alias normalization but the trigger editor showed the legacy value outside its dropdown options. Fix: extend the handler to walk `actions[].echoStream` too, bump flag to `conversationRename3`. **General rule**: when a rename touches a domain object (Contact / Trigger / Macro / etc.), enumerate ALL fields where the renamed string could appear — including nested arrays — and rename in all of them. The runtime alias map in `STREAM_ID_ALIASES` is a safety net, NOT a substitute for clean data; users editing rules through the UI need the stored value to match the displayed options.

51. **Macro `@` is the universal cursor-position marker; `\@` escapes to literal `@`.** Established in B137 (v0.8.10). Genie ([`FormMain.cs:1140`](C:\temp\Genie4-Dev\Genie4\Forms\FormMain.cs#L1140) `ParseInputBox` + [`FormMain.cs:4079`](C:\temp\Genie4-Dev\Genie4\Forms\FormMain.cs#L4079) `ClassCommand_SendText`) and Wrayth both use `@` as the cursor-position marker in macro commands. The presence of an unescaped `@` switches the macro from "send immediately" to "type into the input box and wait for the user to finish typing" mode. **Lichborne's canonical helper** is [`parseCursorMarker(command)`](src/renderer/macros.ts) in `macros.ts` — walks the string char by char, treats `\@` as a literal `@` in the output (escape), strips all unescaped `@` chars from the typed text, returns `{ text, cursorPos }` for the first unescaped `@`'s position. Returns `null` when no cursor marker is present (caller sends normally). **Runtime in the macro fire path** ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)): for each command, check cursor marker FIRST (before token check). If found: flush any pending send-mode commands, `setCommand(text)` + sync `commandRef.current`, wait one rAF for React to commit the input value, then `inputRef.focus()` + `setSelectionRange(cursorPos, cursorPos)`. Stop iterating remaining macro commands (the user must hit Enter to send what's in the bar; anything after the cursor command would never fire). **Wrayth `\r` translation at import time** ([wrayth.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/wrayth.ts) `parseWraythAction`): Wrayth's `\r` is the explicit "send / Enter" marker; absence of `\r` means "type and wait."
