To map Wrayth's signal into Lichborne's universal `@` convention, the importer tracks whether the raw action ended with `\r` — if NOT, and the last command doesn't already have an unescaped `@`, append `@` so the runtime treats it as type-and-wait. Jaded's `<k action="&apos;}"/>` (decoded `'}`, no `\r`, no `@`) imports as `'}@` and works correctly. **Genie imports**: Genie macros use `@` natively, but Genie's file format ALSO uses Level-1 escape sequences (`\\` → `\`, `\}` → `}`, `\{` → `{`) for content that contains the argument-delimiter characters. Pre-v0.8.10 our `parseArgs` used `line.indexOf('}')` and terminated arguments at the first `}` even when escaped — a Genie compound macro like `{\\x;'\}sekmeht @}` parsed as `\\x;'\` (the `\}` was treated as the terminator) and the rest got dropped. v0.8.10 rewrites parseArgs to walk char-by-char and resolve Level-1 escapes during extraction. **`\x` handling — deliberate simplification (Sekmeht 2026-06-01)**: Genie's runtime has a two-mode model where `\x` triggers "clear + type" and `@`-without-`\x` triggers "insert at cursor in current input." Lichborne picks ONE mode — "always clear and type when there's an `@`" — because (a) it's simpler and more predictable for testers and (b) every real-world `\x` macro from Jaded's file also has `@`, so the simplification covers the common case. So in Lichborne: **`\x` is purely import-time noise** — `splitAction` strips it from each part and lets empty parts get filtered out. **Only `@` triggers wait-mode**, not `\x` alone. `\\x;hide` (hypothetical) imports as just `hide` and auto-sends; `\\x;whisper group @` imports as `whisper group @` and waits (because of `@`). **The "insert at cursor" mode SHIPPED in v0.13.3 (B170, JadedSoul) as a composition-aware rule, not a per-macro flag:** when a cursor-marker macro fires while the command input is FOCUSED and NON-EMPTY (the user is mid-composition — e.g. sitting in the gap a previous `get @ from my pack` template left), the macro's text is INSERTED at the caret (replacing any selection, caret landing at the inserted text's `@` offset) — Wrayth's type-into-the-entry-box model, enabling macro-within-macro composition (`Alt-T` template + `Ctrl-2` `second @` → `get second from my pack`). An EMPTY or unfocused bar keeps the v0.8.10 replace behavior (template fire starts fresh). Consequence: re-firing a template macro while still focused in its own non-empty output INSERTS again (Wrayth-faithful) — clear the bar first if you want a fresh template. Git-verified: the fire path had been replace-only and byte-identical from v0.8.10 through v0.13.2 — the v0.11.9/v0.12.0 Genie/macro import work never touched it, so any earlier "it worked" memory was Wrayth itself or different macro data. **Genie variables** (`$speak`, `$whisper`, `$emote`, etc.) are NOT expanded by Lichborne — they pass through `interpolate` (which only handles names that match Lichborne's reserved variable list) and stay as literal `$varname` text in the imported command. Future feature. **Multi-command behavior**: if a macro has both send-mode and wait-mode commands, the send-modes fire first, then the wait-mode command deposits text and stops; commands AFTER the wait-mode command are silently skipped (matches Genie's behavior — once the cursor is in the input box, the macro is "done" until the user hits Enter, which sends only the box contents). **Backward compat for manually-created Lichborne macros** with literal `@` in the command text (uncommon — usually for DR's `SAY @person message` syntax, but people typically type that directly): post-v0.8.10 the `@` is a cursor marker; users with such macros need to change `@` to `\@` to preserve literal `@` send-mode. **When adding a new macro feature** that interacts with command text (variable interpolation, command chaining, etc.), be aware that `parseCursorMarker` runs AFTER interpolation (`resolveMacro` interpolates `$varname` before returning) — so a variable that expands to text containing `@` would trigger cursor-marker handling. Could be a feature (variable-driven cursor positioning) or a bug depending on intent.

52. **`;vars setup` (and Lich GTK setup-window scripts in general) crash Lich on user interaction; route testers to Lichborne's SQLite vars viewer instead.** Investigated 2026-06-01 (v0.8.11). The `;vars setup` script lives at `Ruby4Lich5/Lich5/scripts/vars.lic` (it's a core Lich script, not a dr-script — `dr-scripts/` has no `vars.lic`, only `setupaliases.lic`). It opens a GTK window via `Gtk.queue { Gtk::Window.new ... window.show_all }` and blocks on `wait_until { done }` until the `delete_event` handler fires. The window DOES paint under Lichborne (which contradicts the older "kill-counter shape" assumption that all such windows fail to render — see updated architecture note above). **What crashes Lich:** [`vars.lic:136-141`](C:\Ruby4Lich5\Lich5\scripts\vars.lic#L136-L141) spawns a `Thread.new { ... sw.vadjustment.value = ... }` block that mutates a GTK widget (`sw.vadjustment`) from a non-main thread inside the "focus-in" event handler that fires when the user clicks the "(new var name)" textbox. This directly violates the warning at [`gtk.rb:4`](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lib\common\gtk.rb#L4) — "Calling Gtk API in a thread other than the main thread may cause random segfaults." Under Lichborne's launch (`ruby lich.rbw --stormfront --dragonrealms`) the race appears to manifest reliably; under Genie's launch it apparently doesn't (GTK runtime timing differs between front-end environments — both run the same `vars.lic`, so the difference is in how the GTK loop is hosted). The failure shape: user focuses new-var textbox → `Thread.new` launches and mutates the scrolled-window adjustment from off-thread → GTK widget state race → Ruby/GTK segfault → Lich process exits → Lichborne's [LichConnection](src/main/connection/LichConnection.ts) sees the socket close and emits `disconnect`. **This is a Lich-script bug, not a Lichborne bug.** It cannot be fixed from Lichborne's side without forking Lich's `scripts/vars.lic`, which is out of scope (Principle: not a Lich-replacement; we don't ship script forks). **Lichborne-native replacement SHIPPED in v0.9.0** — the Lich Dashboard → Variables tab is now a full add / edit / delete editor (see pitfall #53). It deliberately did NOT take the approach this pitfall originally speculated (a Marshal *serializer* + direct `lich.db3` write): a direct DB write is unsafe while Lich is running because Lich's in-memory `@@vars` is authoritative and its next auto-save would clobber it (vars.rb). Instead writes go THROUGH Lich's public `Vars` API via `;eq Vars['name'] = value; Vars.save`, which mutates Lich's memory AND forces an immediate flush — no Marshal serializer needed, no race with Lich's auto-save. Read still uses the SQLite/Marshal path (`lich:get-vars`). **When a tester reports the `;vars setup` disconnect:** confirm root cause matches (window opens fine, disconnects only on adding/editing), explain it's a Lich-script GTK race that manifests under the `--stormfront` launch shape, and route them to the existing vars viewer for read access plus the script's NON-GTK sub-commands `;vars set NAME=VALUE` / `;vars delete NAME` / `;vars list` (vars.lic:41-75 — these don't touch GTK at all and work fine). **Related discovery, correcting CLAUDE.md drift:** the older "Known limitation — Ruby GTK script windows don't render" architecture note claimed "force-mode (`--stormfront`) skips Lich's entry GUI, which is what starts the GTK main loop" — that's factually wrong. [`lich.rbw:135`](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lich.rbw#L135) calls `Gtk.main` UNCONDITIONALLY when `defined?(Gtk)` (i.e., whenever the `gtk3` gem loads), and [`gtk.rb:148-155`](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lib\common\gtk.rb#L148-L155) registers a `GLib::Idle.add { sleep 0.01 }` yield so Ruby's I/O threads can run while the GTK loop spins. So the loop IS running under `--stormfront`. The kill-counter family does NOT "never appear" either — Sekmeht confirmed (v0.9.0 testing) that `kill-counter.lic`'s window surfaces **intermittently** (often after a start→kill→restart cycle), so the shared root cause is GTK-runtime timing/threading flakiness under `--stormfront`, not a missing pump and not a categorical no-paint. A painted kill-counter window is still unsafe — interacting with it can crash Lich the same way `;vars setup` does. Don't repeat either the "no main loop" or the "windows never appear" claim without re-verifying. The architecture-section paragraph above has been corrected in the same v0.8.11 update. **General principle for future Lich-GTK-script disconnect reports:** read the actual `.lic` source first (the user's live install at `Ruby4Lich5/Lich5/scripts/` is the canonical location; `dr-scripts/` does NOT contain core scripts like vars/log/repository), look for `Thread.new` blocks that touch GTK widgets from off-thread, and check `gtk.rb` for the thread-safety contract before blaming the front-end launch shape. The disconnect signature in Lichborne is the same regardless of cause (Lich exits → socket closes → `LichConnection` emits `disconnect`); the diagnostic value is in the .lic source, not the front-end.

53. **Editing Lich state writes THROUGH Lich's runtime API, never into `lich.db3` directly — and force a save so the read view doesn't lag.** Established by the v0.9.0 editable-variables feature in [LichDashboard.tsx](src/renderer/components/LichDashboard.tsx) `VarsTab`. The shape generalizes to any future "edit a thing Lich owns" feature (vars, settings, the repository list, etc.). **Why not write the DB:** while Lich is connected, its in-memory copy is authoritative (for vars, the `@@vars` hash in [vars.rb](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lib\common\vars.rb)); Lich persists to `lich.db3` only on its own schedule (vars: a 5-min auto-save, and only when the md5 changed) and rewrites the WHOLE blob via `INSERT OR REPLACE`. A direct Lichborne DB write would be silently clobbered the next time any Lich script touches a var. So Lich's memory is truth and the DB is just its persistence — same inversion as Principle #1's "YAML is truth, localStorage is a working copy," but here Lich owns the truth. **The write path:** send a single atomic `;eq <ruby>` (ExecScript — `;e`/`;eq` is dispatched at [global_defs.rb:2319](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lib\global_defs.rb#L2319), `;eq` = the quiet form) that BOTH mutates via Lich's public API AND forces the flush in one statement list: `;eq Vars['name'] = value; Vars.save` (delete = `... = nil; Vars.save`). One `;eq` (not two separate commands) because two commands race — a standalone `Vars.save` could run before a separate `;vars delete` finished, persisting the pre-delete state and leaving the DB stale until the 5-min timer. `Vars.save` is mutex-guarded (vars.rb:78) and rewrites the whole blob, so a deleted key actually leaves storage and the SQLite read view is correct on the next refresh. `Vars[]=`/`Vars.save` are Lich's documented public API (as stable as the `;vars` command, and what `;vars` calls internally) — this is NOT "running arbitrary Ruby," it's the same API surface. **Escaping:** values/names are injected into Ruby single-quoted literals via `rubyLit(s)` (escape `\` and `'` only — those are the only specials in a Ruby `'...'` string) so values with quotes/spaces/backslashes survive. Mirror Lich's own coercions (vars.lic coerces literal `true`/`false` to booleans — so do we, for display parity). **Silent send:** the `;eq` runs via a no-echo path (`onRunCommand` wired to `window.api.sendCommand(sessionId, cmd)` directly, NOT the echoing `sendCommand`) so the raw Ruby doesn't spam the game window — the optimistic UI update is the user-facing feedback. **Read stays SQLite** (`lich:get-vars` + Marshal) — structured display of lists/hashes/times, cross-scope browse, graceful per-row parse-error degradation. The read/write asymmetry is deliberate and correct: read wants structure + any-scope browsing (the Marshal storage format is a far more stable contract than the cosmetic `;vars list` output, and command-read would need a stream-capture/suppress mechanism like the `;listall` poll); write must mutate live memory. **Two gates on edit controls**: (a) `session.useLich` AND (b) the selected scope equals the connected character's own scope (`${game}:${character}`) — `;eq Vars[...]` only touches the CONNECTED session's memory, so editing while viewing another character's scope would silently write the wrong character's vars. Viewing other scopes is read-only with a note. **Optimistic overlay** (`pendingRef`, keyed by scope → name → change) bridges the sub-second gap between the write and the next DB read so ↺ / reopen never flicker an edit back to its old value; it survives a refresh by re-applying over the DB read, and is discarded on modal close (the forced save makes the DB authoritative-fresh by then, so this is belt-and-suspenders). **When adding a new "edit Lich state" surface**: follow this exact shape — write through Lich's public Ruby API + force its save in one `;eq`, read through whatever structured path exists, gate on connected-own-scope, send silently, overlay optimistically. Don't reach for a direct DB writer or a Marshal serializer; the race with Lich's in-memory authority is the trap.

54. **(Removed v0.9.x — number kept as a tombstone.)** This pitfall documented the v0.9.0 GTK-script advisory: a `client-notice` IPC channel that injected `--- Lichborne:` lines into the stream, plus a `maybeWarnGtkScript` / `GTK_CODE_RE` / `resolveLichScriptFile` detector in [main.ts](src/main/main.ts) that scanned a started script's `.lic` for GTK code and warned the user. **All of it was removed** when the GTK-friendly launch shape shipped (see the "Ruby GTK script windows" architecture note + the launch section) — the advisory assumed GTK was broken, which is no longer the operating assumption. The `client-notice` channel (its only consumer was this advisory), the `onClientNotice` preload/`global.d.ts` binding, the GameWindow subscription, and the per-session `gtkChecked`/`useLich`/`lichPath` Session fields are all gone. **Transferable lesson worth keeping** (this is why the number isn't just deleted): *any* future feature that reacts to "the user started script X" — a per-script setting, a script-specific panel, a fresh advisory — must resolve the script the way Lich's `Script.start` does ([script.rb:65-84](C:\temp\lich-dev\lich-5\lib\common\script.rb#L82)): build the candidate list (custom/ root + subdirs, then scripts/ root, each sorted by basename) and match **exact first, then prefix** — because users abbreviate script names constantly (`;kill-cou` starts `kill-counter.lic`). Don't assume `;typed` maps to `typed.lic`. **And if you ever need to inject a client-authored line into the stream again** (the old `client-notice` pattern): a segment with `bold: true` and NO `preset` renders as monsterbold yellow, because `renderSegment.tsx` resolves `preset = seg.preset ?? (seg.bold ? 'bold' : undefined)` — an explicit preset (e.g. `internal-system`) WINS over the bold fallback and gives you a dim gray-bold line instead. Rebuild the channel from scratch if needed rather than expecting the old wiring to still exist.

55. **A themed dialog must use the SAME background vars as the canonical `.sp-modal` / `.sp-header` chrome — `--bg-raised` and `--bg-sunken` can collapse to near-identical values on light themes.** Established v0.9.2 (Sekmeht, Classic Light). The wizard chrome ([wizard.css](src/renderer/styles/wizard.css)) styled `.wiz-modal` body with `var(--bg-raised)` and `.wiz-header` with `var(--bg-sunken)`, while the Settings modal ([settings.css](src/renderer/styles/settings.css)) used `var(--bg-base)` body + `var(--bg-hover)` header band + `var(--accent)` title. On the dark theme this looked fine (the four vars are visibly distinct), so it shipped — but Classic Light defines `--bg-base #fff`, `--bg-raised #efefef`, `--bg-sunken #fafafa`, `--bg-hover #e8e8e8`: the wizard body went grey instead of white and the header band (`#fafafa`) was indistinguishable from it, so the Lich Setup dialog had **no visible title bar and a "wrong" greyed body** while the Settings window next to it looked right. Fix was to align the wizard chrome to the exact vars the Settings modal uses (`--bg-base` body, `--bg-hover` header, `--accent` title). **General rule**: there is one canonical modal-chrome var recipe (body `--bg-base`, header/footer band `--bg-hover`/`--bg-sunken`, title `--accent`); reuse it for every dialog rather than picking "semantically nice" raised/sunken vars per-dialog. **And always eyeball new dialog chrome on a light theme (Classic Light, Ivory, Parchment, Mist)** — the raised/sunken/base/hover scale is spread out on dark themes but compressed near white on light ones, so a var choice that looks distinct in the default theme can vanish on a light one. Related: this same release converted [login.css](src/renderer/styles/login.css) (the shared `.login-form` / `.advanced-panel` chrome behind LichSetupFields) from hardcoded dark hex to theme vars — same lesson as pitfall #34 (write `var(--x)`, not a literal hex that happens to equal the dark-theme value), but for form/dialog chrome rather than panel body text. Semantic status banners (the discovery ok/warn/error chips) use `color-mix(in srgb, <fixed-hue> N%, var(--bg-base/--text-primary))` so the hue stays meaningful while the background + text contrast self-correct per theme — the right pattern when a color must stay a fixed semantic hue but still adapt to light/dark. **Crucially — when you change a SHARED chrome var, audit the inner elements that referenced the OLD value, because their contrast was relative to it.** `.wiz-modal` is shared by the Add Character wizard, and flipping its body `--bg-raised → --bg-base` collided with two inner rules keyed to the old relationship: the selectable tiles (`.wiz-radio`/`.wiz-game`/`.wiz-char`) were `var(--bg-base)` (raised *above* a `--bg-raised` body) and went flat once the body was also `--bg-base` — fixed by moving the tiles to `--bg-raised` (now raised above a `--bg-base` body); and `.wiz-close:hover { background: var(--bg-hover) }` became invisible once the header band was `--bg-hover` — fixed with a `color-mix(... var(--text-primary) 14%, transparent)` overlay (a theme-agnostic darken/lighten that's always visible regardless of the surface under it; note `--bg-active` was NOT an option — classicLight defines it but `darkBase` does not, so it'd be `transparent` on the default theme). Both regressions were silent on the dark theme and only surfaced in a cross-feature read during the v0.9.2 bug check — the canonical example of why changing a shared var means re-reading every consumer of it, not just the dialog you were fixing. **Modal SIZE standardization (v0.11.2, separate from chrome):** the big management windows (Panel Manager, Automations + standalone Highlights/Triggers/Macros editors, Lich Dashboard/Profile/Scripts, Settings, Session Log, Contacts, Theme Picker/Editor, **Import Wizard** `.iw-modal` — added v0.11.9 because the old fixed 780px squished the Genie highlights table's columns) all set `width: var(--modal-w-standard)` / `height: var(--modal-h-standard)` (88vw × 86vh, matching the Maps overlay `.map-overlay-window`) — two layout tokens in [global.css](src/renderer/styles/global.css) `:root`, NOT theme colors. Retune all modal sizes in one place. This is the SAFE slice of the deferred modal-chrome unification (size only — no bg/header/backdrop/close-button changes, so no pitfall-#55 light-theme risk). **Heads-up — `.tp-` is a shared prefix collision (a real, live trap):** BOTH `theme-picker.css` and `triggers.css` declare `.tp-modal`/`.tp-body`/`.tp-backdrop`/`.tp-close`/`.tp-header`/`.tp-list`/`.tp-list-item`/etc., and BOTH components render those classes — so since CSS is global, every `.tp-*` rule from either file applies to the OTHER panel too, with conflicts resolved by bundle load order. v0.11.2 made them agree on `--modal-w-standard`/`--modal-h-standard` so SIZE is harmless. But the resize work exposed a layout bug: theme-picker's `.tp-list { width: 210px }` was leaking onto the Triggers rule list (only theme-picker sets `width` on the shared class, so it applies regardless of order) — it coincidentally fit when the triggers sidebar was also 210px, but broke once the sidebar widened. **Fix technique (when two components share a class and you can't rename yet): scope by a structural ancestor with the child combinator.** theme-picker's list is `.tp-body > .tp-list` (direct child); triggers' is `.tp-body > .tp-sidebar > .tp-list` (grandchild). Scoping theme-picker's rule to `.tp-body > .tp-list` makes it match ONLY theme-picker's list (the `>` excludes the nested triggers list) AND raises its specificity (0,1,1) so neither leaks onto the other. **If you ever touch ANY `.tp-*` chrome/color/layout rule, it hits BOTH the Theme Picker and the Triggers panel — scope it to a structural ancestor, or do the real fix and rename one prefix (e.g. triggers `.tp-` → `.trg-`).** The other still-colliding classes (`.tp-body`/`.tp-backdrop`/`.tp-close`/`.tp-header`/`.tp-list-item`) are currently compatible by luck; don't trust that.

56. **Platform-wide profile import has TWO write paths — YAML read-merge-write for inactive targets, localStorage + remount for active ones — and writing only the YAML for an ACTIVE target gets erased on logout.** Established by F38 (v0.10.0, JadedSoul) in [profileTransfer.ts](src/renderer/profileTransfer.ts) `applyProfileImport`. The feature fans an import out to many characters at once; each target is either *inactive* (no open session — only a `{Character}.yaml` on disk) or *active* (has an open session, focused OR backgrounded). The two need different writes:
- **Inactive → YAML read-merge-write** (the `setCharacterGame` pattern, [Launcher.tsx](src/renderer/components/Launcher.tsx)): `readCharacterProfile` → merge selected categories into `state` (+ `theme`) → `writeCharacterProfile`. **NEVER** call `buildCharacterProfile`/`exportCharacterProfile` for a non-active character — they rebuild `state` from localStorage, which for an unopened char is empty, so they'd wipe its settings (Launcher already documents this).
- **Active → localStorage working copy + remount.** Write each selected category into `lichborne.{target}.*` scoped keys, then bump that session's reload nonce in App.tsx (`reloadSession(characterId)` → it's part of the GameWindow `key`) so the GameWindow remounts and re-reads everything from localStorage. **Why not just write the YAML:** the live GameWindow is still holding the *pre-import* state, and `exportCharacterProfile` (debounced save + logout flush) rebuilds the YAML from localStorage — so a YAML-only import would be silently overwritten on the next save/logout (JadedSoul's exact concern). Writing the working copy makes the imported state the live state; logout then persists it correctly. **"Active" includes backgrounded tabs** (pitfall #24: hidden ≠ unmounted) — they hold their own stale localStorage-seeded state, so the import loop must `reloadSession` EVERY target with an open session, not just the focused one. Remounting a hidden tab is safe (its 0×0 DOM re-measures on show via the GenieMapView ResizeObserver). ~~Tradeoff: the remount clears in-memory game-text scrollback~~ **Fixed v0.13.3 (B165 hole #2):** main's `session:reload` handler arms a pitfall-#60 replay (`replayTarget`/`holdingForReplay`) before triggering the remount, so the remounted GameWindow restores scrollback AND every sticky state — hands included (a long-parked held item never re-sends a hand tag, so pre-fix it could never self-heal post-remount; found while chasing B165, see pitfall #78 for the attribution nuance).

**Non-destructive guarantee:** import writes ONLY into `state` (per-key, never a whole-`state` replace) + the top-level `theme`. Every identity/launcher field (`account`, `character`, `game`, `useLich`, `hidden`, `favorite`, `guild`, `circle`, `notes`, `profileVersion`) is a top-level YAML field outside `state`, so it's structurally unreachable — the spread `{ ...existingProfile, state: merged }` preserves them all. **Theme is the one quirk:** Lichborne's current theme is a single global `lichborne.theme` key, and `exportCharacterProfile` rewrites an active char's YAML `theme` from that global on every save — so you CAN'T independently pin an active target's theme (it reverts to global). Theme applies cleanly to *inactive* targets (YAML `theme` field, applied on their next connect via `importCharacterProfile`); for active targets it CANNOT be pinned (an active char's YAML theme is rewritten from the global on the next save), so it's flagged "app-wide — not changed for a connected character; pick it from the theme menu." The custom-theme *definition* always goes into shared `myThemes` regardless (so it's available in the picker everywhere), and the import flushes `_shared.yaml` so it persists. **The `settings`/`panelFontSizes` split:** Display category owns `settings` minus `panelFontSizes`; Layout owns `panelFontSizes`. On apply, Display preserves the target's existing `panelFontSizes` and Layout merges its own into `settings` — Display runs before Layout so both can touch the `settings` key without clobbering. When adding a new transferable setting, register it in `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` (the single allowlist); a key not listed there is simply not transferred (safe default).

57. **Per-session React contexts and per-session UI state live INSIDE GameWindow — app-level chrome (the app-bar, the native menu) cannot consume them, and must drive per-session behavior through the action bridge instead.** Established by the Phase 2c app-bar (v0.10.0). `GroupsProvider`, `CharacterProvider`, and the `HighlightsContext`/`ContactsContext` providers are wrapped **per-session** (`GroupsProvider`/`CharacterProvider` around each GameWindow in [App.tsx](src/renderer/App.tsx); the Highlights/Contacts providers *inside* GameWindow's render) — that's the per-character isolation model (pitfall #6). So anything rendered at **app level** (the [AppBar](src/renderer/components/AppBar.tsx), App's modals) **cannot call `useGroups`/`useCharacter`/`useHighlights`/`useContacts`** — there's no provider above it. This is why **ModeSwitcher had to stay in the per-session Icon Bar** (it reads `useGroups()`) rather than move into the app-bar with the other buttons, and why the app-bar's buttons are **plain triggers that dispatch `lichborne:session-action`** to the active GameWindow rather than reading/showing per-session state directly. The **per-button active-state highlight** (e.g. "Maps is open" glow) is the canonical example of the *reflect-via-snapshot* rule below: the app-bar can't read the active session's `showMapOverlay` etc. directly (those are GameWindow `useState`), so GameWindow **reports them up through `useSessions`** — a `SessionStatus.panel*` flag per toggle button, pushed by a GameWindow `updateStatus` effect and read by AppBar to apply `btn-*--active` for the active session (shipped in v0.10.0 deferred-polish; this is exactly the "surface a minimal snapshot through `useSessions`" pattern, not lifting GameWindow state to app level). **Rule:** when you need app-level chrome to act on the active session, route an action through the bridge (`menu-action` IPC for the native menu / `lichborne:session-action` DOM event for renderer UI) and add a case to GameWindow's `runSessionActionRef`; do NOT try to lift a per-session context to app level (it breaks the isolation model) unless you genuinely intend every session to share that state. When you need app-level chrome to *reflect* active-session state, surface a minimal snapshot through `useSessions` (as the connection dot does via `status.connected`) rather than reaching into GameWindow.

58. **Game-area font scaling has two traps: the panel-root anchor and the own-font `em`.** Established fixing the icon bar / vitals / Mode button / Lich Scripts panel (v0.10.0). Settings → Font Size sets `--game-font-size` ([settings.ts](src/renderer/settings.ts)); to follow it a surface must use `var(--game-font-size)` / `em`-off-an-anchored-container, never `rem` (Principle #9). Two specific traps bit during this work:
    - **(a) Panel content scales only if that panel-type's OWN root anchors to `var(--panel-font-size, var(--game-font-size))`.** `.panel-frame-tabs` carries the game-font anchor — but that only sizes the **tab labels**; `.panel-frame-body` (the content wrapper) has **no** font-size, so each panel's root must set the var itself (as `.exp-panel` / `.stream-panel` do). The Lich Scripts panel (`.sl-panel`) shipped without it and silently ignored *both* the global font and the per-panel +/− (its `.sl-*` children were `rem`). **New panel type ⇒ anchor its root to `var(--panel-font-size, var(--game-font-size))` and size children in `em`,** or it won't scale. **The v0.14.7 audit (B201) caught two more variants of this class:** the Genie map's SVG landmark labels read `var(--game-font-size)` DIRECTLY — the global font worked but the A+/A− override didn't (reading the game var without the panel var IS this pitfall, even when it looks font-wired); and the Debug panel was `rem` throughout (ignored both). Both fixed (map labels/tooltip/legend on the chain via a `PANEL_FONT` anchor — SVG node GLYPHS stay geometry-sized on purpose; debug.css rem→chain+em). Every other panel root verified chained in the same audit.
    - **(b) `em` on `width`/`height` is relative to the element's OWN `font-size`, not its parent's.** A chip that sets `font-size: 0.84em` and wants "72px at default" needs `width: 7.14em` (72 ÷ its own 10.08px), NOT `6em` (= 6 × its own font). The icon bar's `.status-bar` hit exactly this. Elements with no own font-size (`.vital-bar`, `.row-sep`) inherit the container's game font, so their `em` dims are relative to that — simpler. Conversion to preserve the default look: `em = rem × 16/12` (rem is the 16px html root; the default `--game-font-size` is 12px).
    - **(c) Per-panel font overrides (F31) PIN a panel.** Once `A−/A+` writes `settings.panelFontSizes[tabId]`, that absolute size wins over the global Settings font, and there's currently **no reset-to-global** (`onAdjustPanelFontSize` always writes, never deletes the key). So a panel you've adjusted stops tracking the Settings slider — **by design (override wins) but surprising.** If a user reports "panel X ignores the font setting," check for an override before assuming a bug (that was the exp confusion). A `next === settings.fontSize ⇒ delete the key` reset (or a relative-delta model) would let adjusted panels rejoin the global font — but Sekmeht **decided to leave it as-is** (2026-06-04): an override pins the panel, full stop. Don't "fix" this without a fresh ask.
    - **(d) Two surfaces share `lich-panels.css`.** The Lich Scripts **panel** (`.sl-*`, a zone panel) scales with the game font; the Lich **Dashboard modal** (`.ld-*`, opened by the Lich button) is deliberately fixed `rem` like every other modal (Settings, Automations, …). Don't confuse them — converting the modal to scale was explicitly declined (modals are the chrome-sizing exception; Principle #9).

59. **Decouple moves a session's WINDOW, never its socket — and that only works because GameWindow unmount doesn't disconnect.** Established by the multi-window feature (v0.11.0). `session:move-window` ([main.ts](src/main/main.ts)) reassigns `ownerWindowId`; the source window drops the tab via `session-release` → renderer `removeSession` (local-only — it does NOT call `destroySession`), which unmounts that GameWindow. The session's socket/parser/LichBridge in main are untouched, so the target window mounts a fresh GameWindow for the SAME `sessionId` and main re-routes its events there. **This is load-bearing on GameWindow's unmount cleanup containing no teardown of the session** — verified: the IPC-subscription cleanup only unsubscribes listeners + cancels rAF/timers ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)); `window.api.disconnect` lives only in `handleDisconnect` (a button), never an unmount path. **If you ever add session teardown to a GameWindow unmount effect, decouple/re-home will silently kill the character on every move.** Don't. Closing a *secondary window* IS a logout (`runSecondaryWindowClose` graceful-disconnects then destroys), but that's the window 'close' handler in main, not the GameWindow unmount. Per-BrowserWindow renderers are fully isolated JS contexts (separate heaps) — only localStorage is shared (same partition) — so module-level renderer state (theme hook, etc.) can't bleed across windows; that isolation is why the move is clean. The roster (`session-roster`) is the cross-window awareness mechanism; the render source stays `SessionsContext`-local driven by acquire/release/pull (NOT roster-driven) to avoid the connect-flicker that a fully roster-derived render loop would cause.

60. **A render-only "replay" reseeds a window taking over a session — gate it at the side-effect choke points, snapshot sticky state, and HOLD live delivery during the handoff.** Established by the multi-window state-transfer (v0.11.0), refined across three tester-found bugs. A freshly-mounted GameWindow starts blank; to make decouple/re-home seamless, main replays the session's recent history to the window that took it over. Three things make this correct, each from a real bug:
    - **(a) Gate side effects, don't reprocess them.** The replay batch carries `replay: true` ([GameEventBatch](src/shared/types.ts)). The renderer rebuilds display + game state from it but MUST NOT re-fire triggers (would re-send commands!), re-log the session, or re-count fires. All trigger firing funnels through `processLineRef`/`processVariableChangeRef` and logging through `logToSession`/`logHighlightFiresRef`, so gating those FOUR choke points on a `replayingRef` (set true at the batch top in `onGameEvent`, reset false at the bottom) covers every call site at once — far safer than threading a flag through the ~14 individual call sites. The room/vital STATE setters (setVitals etc.) are NOT gated (rebuilding state is the point).
    - **(b) Snapshot sticky state — a ring buffer alone loses unchanged vitals.** Main keeps per-session `stateSnapshot: Map<key, GameEvent>` (latest of each vital/indicator/RT/CT/stance/spell/hand/room/exp/injury/exits, via `snapshotKey`) PLUS a bounded `historyBuffer` (scrollback text). The first design was a single ring buffer of recent events — but a vital sitting at 100% hadn't emitted a `vital-update` recently, so it fell off the end and restored BLANK (only actively-changing bars survived). The snapshot keeps the latest value of every bar regardless of age; replay sends snapshot FIRST then history.
    - **(c) Only replay to a MOVED-into window, and HOLD live during the handoff.** Replaying on EVERY GameWindow mount doubled the login stream on a fresh connect (the replay overlapped the live stream still filling the buffer). Fix: a session only earns a replay when DELIBERATELY REMOUNTED — `replayTarget` is set on `session:move-window` (decouple/re-home) and, since v0.13.3 (B165 root cause), on `session:reload` (the profile-import remount) — one-shot, checked in `session:request-replay`; a fresh connect never gets one. AND because a session can still be actively streaming *during* a move (bulk-connect logs in then decouples), `holdingForReplay` stops live `game-event` sends to the window from the moment of the move until the replay is delivered (events accumulate into the buffer, the replay delivers them once, then live resumes) — otherwise the in-flight login lines show live AND in the replay. A 5s `scheduleReplayHoldRelease` safety net resumes live if the window never requests its replay. The buffer is filled at FLUSH time (events actually sent), kept disjoint from the pending `eventQueue`, so a replay can't double a not-yet-flushed event either. **When adding a new "rebuild a window from history" path, reuse this shape: gate side effects via a replay flag, snapshot sticky state separately from scrollback, and never let live + replay overlap.**

61. **Two import-wizard traps, both from completing the Wrayth importer (B146, v0.11.1). (a) Don't copy `parseNames`' pattern-only dedup onto a HIGHLIGHT parser — it's data loss.** `parseNames` dedups by pattern because two contacts with the same name make no sense (one contact). But HIGHLIGHTS legitimately repeat a pattern with DIFFERENT colors (Wrayth had `shirt` @54 and `shirt` @26), and Lichborne supports multiple same-pattern highlights (priority-ordered). When `parseStrings` was first written by copying `parseNames`, its pattern-only dedup silently dropped the color variant (147 strings → 146). Fix: dedup highlights by **full visual identity** (`pattern + textColor + bgColor`), so only truly-identical rows collapse. **Any new highlight-producing parser must dedup on visual identity, not pattern alone.** **(b) `max-width` + `text-overflow: ellipsis` is a NO-OP on an inline element.** `.iw-pattern` ([import-wizard.css](src/renderer/styles/import-wizard.css)) is a `<span>` in a table cell with `max-width: 320px` + ellipsis to keep long patterns from blowing out the table. That silently did nothing for years because Genie/Frostbite highlights are short words — but Wrayth `<strings>` are full sentences, so the Pattern cell expanded to the full string and pushed the Color/Status columns off-screen (the symptom looked like "colors didn't import" — they had, just scrolled off behind a horizontal scrollbar). Fix: `display: inline-block` so `max-width`/ellipsis apply. **When truncating text with `max-width`+ellipsis, the element must be block/inline-block** — and when a tester says "X didn't import," verify against the parsed data (a quick node script replicating the parse) before assuming a parse bug; here the data was correct and the bug was layout. General Wrayth-format reminders for future import work: highlights are in `<strings>` (NOT `<highlights>`); colors are `@NN` palette refs resolved through `<palette>`; `&apos;`/`&quot;` are decoded by `getAttr`→`decodeXmlEntities` (don't add a second decode); `bgcolor="skin"`/empty means "inherit" → treat as null.

62. **A line-number gutter and its content MUST share an ABSOLUTE per-line height, never a unitless `line-height` — different font-sizes silently drift them apart (B147, v0.11.2).** The Lich Dashboard YAML editor renders line numbers in a separate gutter column (`.ld-line-num`) beside the content (`.ld-yaml-preview` view / `.ld-yaml-editor` textarea). The gutter font is intentionally smaller (`0.75rem`) than the content (`0.79rem`) — fine — but all three used a **unitless** `line-height: 1.65`, which multiplies each element's OWN font-size. So the gutter's per-line height (12px×1.65 = 19.8px) ≠ the content's (12.64px×1.65 = 20.86px): ~1px/line of drift that ACCUMULATES, leaving the numbers ~2.5 lines off the content they label by line ~50. The tester's phrasing ("line spacing bleeding through") was exactly this. It also made *search* feel wrong: `scrollElementToLine`/the overlay read `getComputedStyle(pre).lineHeight` (the content's 20.86px) so they scrolled to the correct *content* line, but the gutter number next to it was misaligned, so the user read the wrong number. **Fix:** pin the gutter, the preview pre, AND the editor textarea to ONE absolute `line-height: 1.3rem` — per-line height is now font-size-independent and identical across all three, and the computed value the search/overlay reads matches the gutter. **Rule for any future gutter/aligned-column UI:** the gutter and the content it indexes must use the same ABSOLUTE line-height (px/rem), kept in lockstep with a comment on each rule; a unitless `line-height` shared between two different font-sizes is a drift bug waiting to happen. Same trap would bite any future "minimap", "diff gutter", or aligned two-column code view.

63. **A self-correcting `--syntax-*` palette: define a color ONCE in `darkBase` as `color-mix(fixed-hue, var(--text-primary))` and every theme inherits a per-theme-correct value with no override (v0.11.2).** Syntax-highlight palettes (the Lich Dashboard YAML/var preview, the Debug panel event types, the Fires log) need ~8 distinct token hues. Hardcoding VS-Code-dark hex (`#9cdcfe` etc.) is the pitfall-#34 light-theme bug at scale — light-blue keys vanish on white. The fix is NOT to add 8 vars × 20 themes; it's to add the 8 `--syntax-key/string/number/literal/comment/meta/type/symbol` vars to `darkBase` ONLY, each as `color-mix(in srgb, <fixed-hue> N%, var(--text-primary))`. Because the nested `var(--text-primary)` resolves in each element's (theme's) context at use time, one definition yields a readable, hue-distinct value on every theme automatically. Consumers just say `color: var(--syntax-key)`. **When you need a palette of fixed-meaning hues that must stay legible across themes, define them once in `darkBase` as color-mix-toward-`--text-primary`, not per-theme.** (Status/semantic single colors follow the same idea via `color-mix(fixed-hue, var(--bg-base/--text-primary))` — pitfall #55.) Related v0.11.2 work: the per-theme `--text-dim`/`--text-faint` ramp was compressed toward `--text-muted` (the dim tail was below readable contrast on several surfaces), and `classicLight` had an inverted ramp (`dim`/`faint` = pure black, more prominent than body text) — a reminder that the 5-level text ramp must be monotonic toward the bg on light themes too.

64. **Per-window state delivered by PUSH-only IPC is race-prone for a freshly-opened window — pull it on mount too (B149, v0.11.2).** Multi-window state (the session roster) is broadcast from main on every change (`broadcastRoster` → `session-roster`), including on a window's `did-finish-load`. But a brand-new window's renderer registers its `onSessionRoster` listener only AFTER React mounts (a `useEffect`), so it LOSES the `did-finish-load` broadcast — and if no further change fires (a stable connected session emits no status events; `session:set-name` only broadcasts on a name *change*), the empty value never self-heals. Symptom: Quick Send (which renders nothing when the cross-window roster is empty) did nothing via Ctrl+Shift+Enter in a decoupled window — the hotkey fired, but `RosterContext.roster` was `[]`. `SessionsContext` never had this bug because it **pulls** owned sessions on mount (`get-owned-sessions`) in addition to reacting to push (`session-acquire/release`); `RosterContext` was left push-only — the oversight. **Fix shape (the rule):** every per-window context that mirrors main-owned state must **PULL the current value on mount AND subscribe to future pushes** — never push-only. Added `get-roster` (returns `buildRoster()`) called in RosterContext's mount effect next to the subscribe. When you add a new cross-window broadcast channel, add its pull-on-mount handler at the same time. (Pull-resolves-after-subscribe ordering is fine: a push arriving between subscribe and pull isn't lost, and a late pull just reasserts the same authoritative list.)

65. **DR carries the room id in the `<streamWindow>` subtitle in TWO formats — parse BOTH, and treat its absence as normal (B151, v0.11.2).** The subtitle (which also carries the room title) can be either `[Whistling Wood, Barrows - 9479]` (id INSIDE the brackets after ` - `) OR `[Arthelun Ruins, Courtyard] (56107)` (title in brackets, id in PARENS after them). The parens form is the StormFront-standard `[Title] (uid)` — it's DR's **Simutronics room-id flag** display, an account setting the player can toggle; `(**)` means "room has no id" (unmapped, e.g. `[The Heavens] (**)` during a Moon Mage telescope flip). Pre-v0.11.2 the parser ([StormFrontParser](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts) streamWindow handler) only parsed the dash form, so flag-on players got `roomId: undefined` → the Lich Map's instant `lichDb.get(roomId)` lookup never fired (forcing the fragile title+desc path — the "location lost during movement" symptom) and `$roomid` was empty. Fix: when the dash form misses, also match `\]\s*\((\d+)\)` after the closing bracket. **Crucial constraint — the flag is OPTIONAL, so id-absence must stay a no-op:** when neither form is present (flag off) OR the id is `(**)`, `roomId` MUST remain `undefined` exactly as before, and the whole downstream pipeline must keep working id-free (MapPanel falls back to `findRoom` title+desc; `$roomid` renders empty; `triggerCtxRef.roomId` only updates when `evt.roomId != null`). Never make a parsed room id load-bearing — it's a bonus signal when present (and the Genie map can't use it at all; its data has no game room ids, pitfall in §19 / B148), never a requirement. The companion id source is `<nav rm='X'/>` (pitfall #46) — when present it agrees with the subtitle; the telescope case shows DR sometimes sends an EMPTY `<nav/>` and relies on the subtitle parens, which is exactly why both subtitle forms must be parsed. **`u`-prefixed parens form (handled since v0.16.1, surfaced during the Lich 5.18 review): when a player has Lich's `display_uid` setting on, Lich REWRITES the native parens form to `[Title] (u12345)` — a `u`-PREFIXED id.** The parens regex is therefore `/\]\s*\(u?(\d+)\)/` (the `u?` is optional, so bare-digit `(56107)` still matches AND `(u12345)` parses to `12345` — the same game uid the native flag emits, so the `lichDb` lookup is identical). Non-numeric parens (`(**)`, `(unknown)`) still miss → `roomId` stays `undefined`, preserving the id-absence no-op. This was PRE-EXISTING (not a 5.18 regression — the `u`-prefix rewrite and the `display_uid` auto-enable at Lich's `xmlparser.rb:501` both predate 5.18); pre-v0.16.1 it silently degraded the Lich Map to the title+desc path for `display_uid`-on players. `display_lichid` instead injects the LICH id INSIDE the brackets as bare digits (`[Title - 500]`), which the dash regex already handles.

66. **Text selection across a virtualized list loses unmounted rows on copy — keep a generous `increaseViewportBy` buffer (B152, v0.11.2).** The story window is react-virtuoso; it mounts only the visible rows plus a small overscan and UNMOUNTS off-screen rows. A browser text selection lives on DOM nodes — when a selected row unmounts (you scroll while drag-selecting), it silently leaves the selection. So the mouseup auto-copy (`getSelection().toString()` → `window.api.writeClipboard` in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)) captures only the rows still mounted at release — "a portion from the end" (the final viewport + overscan). The pragmatic, low-risk fix is `increaseViewportBy={{ top: 3000, bottom: 3000 }}` on the Virtuoso so ~150 rows each side stay mounted, keeping several screenfuls of selection intact through the auto-scroll (rows are memoized + `lines` is capped, so the extra DOM is cheap; scroll math is untouched). **Known ceiling:** a selection scrolling >~3000px past its start still can't be fully captured by a DOM-selection copy — the real ceiling-free fix is to reconstruct the selected text from the `lines` DATA MODEL (capture the anchor line id + char offset at mousedown — before it can unmount — map the focus at mouseup, slice `lines[anchor..focus]`), which was deferred as too intricate for the delicate scroll path. **General rule:** any copy/select/Ctrl-A feature over a virtualized list must either (a) carry a large enough mounted buffer for the expected selection size, or (b) reconstruct from the data model — never trust `getSelection().toString()` to span the full logical list. (Don't "fix" this by un-virtualizing the list — that's the perf foundation of the whole text window.)

67. **A sticky header only lines up with the rows below it if the scroll container reserves the scrollbar gutter — and table rows only stay column-aligned if every row is the same height (v0.11.5, Debug panel).** The Debug panel ([DebugPanel.tsx](src/renderer/components/DebugPanel.tsx) / [debug.css](src/renderer/styles/debug.css)) is a header-over-rows table inside one `overflow-y: auto` scroller (`.debug-scroll`), with the header `position: sticky; top: 0` and rows sharing the SAME `grid-template-columns`. Two traps, both shipped-then-fixed here: **(a)** the header and rows are different children of the scroller, so the moment the list overflows and a vertical scrollbar appears, the *rows* lose scrollbar-width of content box but the *sticky header* doesn't necessarily — columns shift ~15px and stop lining up. Fix: `scrollbar-gutter: stable` on the scroller so the gutter is always reserved and both share one content width. **(b)** the fire-log rows used `align-items: start` + unbounded wrapping (`overflow-wrap: anywhere`) on the matched/detail cells, so a long match made one row 3–4 lines tall while its short cells floated at the top — a ragged, "misaligned" grid even though the templates matched. Fix: `align-items: center` + single-line ellipsis per cell (`white-space:nowrap; overflow:hidden; text-overflow:ellipsis; min-width:0`) with the full value in a `title` tooltip → every row is one line tall and columns read as a real table. **General rule for any header+rows table in a scroll container:** reserve the scrollbar gutter, give the header and rows the *same* column template, and keep rows uniform-height (truncate, don't wrap) unless you deliberately want variable-height rows. Related, same feature: the panel renders in **two modes from one component** — docked bottom strip (`resizable` prop true → drag-handle + per-character height via `scopedKey(character,'debugPanelHeight')`, which round-trips into YAML `state.*` for free per Principle #1) vs. inside a panel zone (`resizable` false → `.debug-panel--fill` fills the zone, no handle, no fixed height). When a component can be hosted in both a fixed-strip and a flex-zone context, gate the fixed/resizable sizing behind a prop rather than baking a height into its root class.

68. **The story window's pin lives in TWO layers — the flex layout must not overflow, AND we (not Virtuoso's `followOutput`) own the bottom-scroll. Both were broken; B153's single-source view was incomplete (v0.11.6, B155).** This is the resolution of a long debugging chain (Sekmeht + Binu) that the earlier B153 (#43) fix only partly addressed. Three distinct bugs, fixed in three distinct places — don't conflate them:
    - **(a) LAYOUT — the flex column overflowed by ~one line (the real "clipped under the vitals bar" root cause).** `.game-main` and `.text-window` ([game.css](src/renderer/styles/game.css)) were `flex: 1` children of flex **columns** but lacked `min-height: 0`. Default `min-height: auto` = content height, so a flex child refuses to shrink below its content and the column runs taller than the window — the bottom (last line / vitals-bar boundary) is clipped. The tell that pinned this after rounds of scroll-math dead ends: **moving the vitals bar top↔bottom shifted the main window by a line** (the overflow flipping ends), and "text feeds beyond its boundary." Fix: `min-height: 0` on both. This is the canonical flexbox scrollable-child trap — **any new flex-column scroll container needs `min-height: 0` on its flex children.** B153 (and B122 before it) treated the clip as purely a scroll-math problem and never found this; with the overflow gone, the clip is gone.
    - **(b) AUTO-FOLLOW — `followOutput` is now OFF; we scroll synchronously.** Virtuoso's `followOutput` aligns the last row to the bottom but UNDER-MEASURES it at fractional heights (the viewport is fractional — vitals/command bars scale by `em`), landing ~one notch short; our correction then snapped it down a frame later — the visible **"scrolled up a notch, then jumps to bottom" two-step** (and once the layout overflow in (a) was fixed, this became visible on EVERY line because the viewport went cleanly fractional). Fix: `followOutput={false}`; when pinned, `totalListHeightChanged` sets `scrollTop = scrollHeight − clientHeight` **SYNCHRONOUSLY (before paint)** so the last line is flush in the same frame the content renders — no short-landing for anything to correct, no jump. A rAF backup only fires if Virtuoso's heights were still settling (estimated rows); if the sync write was exact it's a no-op (no visible motion). `scrollHeight − clientHeight` is the DOM-truth lever (immune to followOutput under-measurement — the one B153 lesson that survived). **Do NOT re-enable `followOutput`** — it and a manual correction will always fight into the two-step.
    - **(c) DISCRETE RELAYOUTS — a settle loop for transitions, a PASSIVE observer for resizes.** Relayouts that reshape the scroller don't settle in one frame (Virtuoso re-measures rows + the flex layout reflows over several frames), so a one-shot correction reads mid-settle. `resnapToBottom()` ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)) re-issues the DOM-truth scroll each frame **until `scrollHeight` stabilizes** (12-frame cap), arming `suppressUntilRef` synchronously and gating on `pinnedRef` throughout (a scrolled-up reader / mid-settle `onWheel` un-pin is never yanked down; rAF tracked in `resnapRafRef`, cancelled on each new resnap + unmount). Wired to the DISCRETE triggers: badge/End (`scrollToBottom`), the font/line-height/large-print effect, an `isActive`-becomes-true effect (tab show — inactive tab is `display:none`→0×0, pitfall #24), a mount-once `window 'focus'`+`document 'visibilitychange'` listener (focus regain after rAF-throttling, guarded `!document.hidden && isActiveRef.current && pinnedRef.current` — Binu's alt-tab case), and **after a replay batch** (`batch.replay === true && pinnedRef.current` in `onGameEvent` — the decouple/split-window path, pitfall #60: a replay fills `lines` in one burst with no follow-up line for `totalListHeightChanged`, and the new BrowserWindow is still settling its first paint; the `isActive` mount effect runs with `lines` empty and the new window's initial focus fires before the listener mounts (B149 race), so this is its own required trigger). **For continuous viewport-height changes** (vitals strip appearing at login — it renders empty ~0px until vitals arrive — compact↔regular toggle, vitals/icon-bar position toggle, window resize) a **`ResizeObserver` on the scroller** re-snaps, but it MUST be passive: gate on an actual integer `clientHeight` change and do a SINGLE bare `scrollTop` write — **never call `resnapToBottom()`/`scrollToIndex()` from it**, because those re-render → nudge the scroller size → re-fire the observer → visible idle **"jumping/scaling fighting itself"** (a ResizeObserver→layout→ResizeObserver loop; the bare `scrollTop` write resizes nothing, so it can't loop).
    - **(d) CONSOLIDATION — `resnapToBottom` + the inline sync+1rAF + the inline ResizeObserver write were merged into ONE primitive `stickToBottom(reindex?)` (v0.11.8, B158).** B155 (b/c above) still left an intermittent "rests one line short, wheel down once to fix it": the per-batch path used a SYNCHRONOUS write + a SINGLE rAF backup, but Virtuoso measures the just-appended last row ASYNCHRONOUSLY (its ResizeObserver fires a frame or two after the row mounts), so `scrollHeight` keeps growing past that single rAF and the correction converged on the short pre-measure bottom. Meanwhile three different correctors (per-batch inline, `resnapToBottom`, the resize-observer write) raced the same target. **`stickToBottom`** ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)) is a self-cancelling rAF **settle loop** that re-asserts `scrollTop = scrollHeight − clientHeight` every frame until `scrollHeight` is **stable for TWO consecutive frames** (or a 20-frame cap) — the two-frame requirement is what guarantees the async measurement grow is always captured. Per-batch (`totalListHeightChanged={() => stickToBottom()}`) keeps the synchronous-first-write-before-paint (flush in the same frame) then runs the loop for the tail; `reindex=true` (badge/End, font change, tab-show, focus-regain, replay) issues ONE `scrollToIndex({index:'LAST'})` first for off-screen targets. The loop writes ONLY `scrollTop` (no re-render), so the scroller `ResizeObserver` now calls `stickToBottom()` directly without the re-render→re-fire loop the old `scrollToIndex` resnap would have caused. Cancel+restart per batch keeps the loop alive across a flood (bottom flush every frame → bursts read as continuous scroll, not chunky jumps). **Trade-off:** during an active flood `suppressUntilRef` is continuously armed, so only `onWheel` (wheel-up) un-pins; scrollbar drag/arrow un-pins once the flood pauses — intended ("stay stuck until the user manually scrolls up").
    - **Rule for the next person:** if the bottom line is *clipped*, suspect LAYOUT first (flex `min-height: 0`, pitfall #43's "scrollable past the API's bottom ⇒ layout not math") — do NOT add more scroll math. If the view *lands short then jumps*, that's `followOutput` fighting a correction — keep it off. If the view *rests one line short intermittently*, that's the async last-row measurement outrunning a one-shot correction — the **settle loop** (`stickToBottom`, two-stable-frames) is the fix, not another bespoke rAF. **There is now exactly ONE auto-scroll primitive — route every new pinned-scroll path through `stickToBottom` (`reindex=true` for a discrete relayout / off-screen target, no-arg for per-batch + continuous resize); do NOT add a fourth mechanism or split it back apart.**

69. **A GameWindow is keyed by `characterId`, NOT `sessionId` — so an in-place reconnect REUSES the same component; per-session local state must reset on the `sessionId` PROP CHANGE, not on a connection-status event (v0.11.6, tab-menu Reconnect).** The session render in [App.tsx](src/renderer/App.tsx) keys each GameWindow `${characterId}:${reloadNonce}`. The tab-menu **Reconnect** ([CharacterTabBar.tsx](src/renderer/components/CharacterTabBar.tsx) → App `handleReconnectTab`) tears down the dead session then re-runs `runConnect`; on success `addSession` REPLACES the record by `characterId` with a fresh `sessionId` (its documented reconnect-in-tab path). Because the key is `characterId`, the GameWindow does **not** remount — it stays mounted and just receives a new `session.sessionId` prop. That's deliberate (preserves scrollback), but it means any per-session LOCAL state in GameWindow (the `dropped`/`disconnecting` flags, and anything gated on them — e.g. `useLichBridge(sessionId, !dropped)`) carries over from the *previous* session and must be explicitly reset. **Do NOT reset it from the `onConnectionStatus` 'Connected' handler** — main emits 'Connected' around when `login()` resolves, which can race AHEAD of the renderer's `sessionIdRef` update, so the event gets filtered out against the stale id (`s.sessionId !== sessionIdRef.current`) and the reset never runs (the v0.11.6 bug: a reconnected tab stayed greyed + Lich bridge stayed off; a remount via "move to another window" looked fine because that IS a fresh mount, which masked it). **The fix is to reset on the `sessionId` change itself** — the effect that maintains `sessionIdRef` compares old vs new and, on an actual change, `setDropped(false)`/`setDisconnecting(false)`. This is deterministic (a React prop-change effect, not a racy IPC event) and a new `sessionId` for the same `characterId` always means a fresh LIVE connection (`addSession` only swaps the id after login succeeds). **General rule:** when a component is keyed by a STABLE identity but receives a CHANGING resource id as a prop (the reconnect-in-place pattern), reset that resource's derived local state on the prop change, and don't depend on an async event whose ordering vs. the prop update isn't guaranteed. Two more notes on the tab menu: it lists only ACTIONABLE options (no greyed rows), ordered window-options-first then the connection toggle LAST below a divider so the destructive Disconnect isn't the top item under the cursor (Binu kept fat-fingering it): "Open in new window" only when >1 char shares the window, "Move to main window" only when `useRoster().isPrimary === false` (a decoupled/secondary window), then Reconnect XOR Disconnect by `status.connected` (divider added only when a window option precedes it). Disconnect uses `window.api.disconnect(sessionId)` DIRECTLY (not the `lichborne:session-action` bridge, which only reaches the *active* GameWindow) so it works on any tab. The "Reconnecting…" spinner is a per-tab indicator driven by an App-owned `reconnectingIds` set (added on reconnect start, removed when `runConnect` settles) — the launcher's connecting overlay isn't visible for a tab reconnect.

70. **Genie Map room-matching mirrors GenieMaps' own client: NAME + EXIT-SET + DESCRIPTION — and the inline `<preset id='roomDesc'>` description must be captured for it to work (v0.11.7, Whistling Wood/Barrows).** Two coupled facts. **(a) DR streams the room description INLINE in `main` as `<preset id='roomDesc'>…</preset>`, NOT as a `<component id='room desc'>`.** The parser tags that segment `preset:'roomdesc'` ([StormFrontParser.ts](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts) preset close) and it flows to the `main` stream — so the ONLY code that wrote `roomState.desc` (the `stream === 'room'` branch in [GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx), fed by `COMPONENT_STREAM['room desc']='room'`) fired only on the rare `<component id='room desc'>` re-emit. Result: `roomState.desc` was empty/stale during normal play, so the Genie matcher's description tiebreaker had nothing to work with and fell through to file order — picking the wrong one of 40+ identically-titled "Whistling Wood, Barrows" nodes. **The fix is renderer-side and batch-ordered:** GameWindow's event loop collects any `preset==='roomdesc'` main-segment text into a batch-local `batchRoomDesc`, then applies `roomUpdates.desc = batchRoomDesc` *after* the loop — so it overrides the B121 `clear-stream 'room'` (`roomUpdates.desc=''`) that lands later in the same batch on a real room entry (the inline desc is emitted BEFORE the `<streamWindow>` that triggers the clear, so an in-loop assignment would be wiped). Do NOT try to fix this in the parser by ordering — the inline-desc-then-streamWindow order makes any emit-time approach race the clear; capture in the renderer and apply last. This also improves the **Lich Map**'s `findRoom` title+desc fallback for free. **(b) The real GenieMaps client (`Node.Compare`/`CardinalCount` in [NodeList.cs](C:/temp/Genie4-Dev/Genie4/Mapper/NodeList.cs)) identifies a room by name + the SET OF EXITS + description, all three** — exits being a strong, always-fresh signal (DR sends the compass every room) that survives a stale description while running. Lichborne ignored exits entirely. Now `roomState.exits` (abbreviated compass tokens) is threaded `GameWindow`/`PanelFrame → MapPanel → GenieMapView` and the pure resolver `resolveGenieRoom` (NOT a memo — see the Architecture note below) resolves an ambiguous title via a ladder: (1) description-EXACT unique over the pool, (2) exit-set EQUALITY unique, (3) description-SUBSTRING unique, (4) graph-adjacency over the FULL pool (preferring an exit-matched neighbour when several qualify), (5) exit-aware conservative-cross-zone-fallback. The exit set excludes only `go`/`climb` arcs (up/down/out DO count — mirrors `CardinalCount`); canonicalize Genie's full words and DR's abbreviations to one token form (`cardinalExitSet`/`liveExitSet`/`exitsEqual`/`exitsSuperset` in [GenieMapView.tsx](src/renderer/components/panels/GenieMapView.tsx)). The two strong signals back each other up — a fresh description nails it outright, the exit set carries it while running — which is what gets the indicator to near-100%. **CRITICAL: exits are used ADDITIVELY, never as a pre-filter that removes candidates before adjacency.** A first cut narrowed the pool by exits before running adjacency; because Genie maps occasionally have imperfect exit data for a room (and DR's live exits can differ for a frame), that EXCLUDED the correct neighbour and broke the adjacency match that worked before exits existed — the marker fell to the conservative hold and stranded ("some room text doesn't match anymore" / "stuck at the Shard healer while hunting elsewhere"). The fix: adjacency runs over the full pool; `exitMatched` only (a) chooses the best blind guess and (b) corroborates a cross-zone move. And the conservative hold (B110) is now **exit-aware** — it COMMITS to the new-zone guess immediately when the guess is exit-corroborated OR when `prev`'s own exits no longer match the live exits (so `prev` provably isn't where you are), and only HOLDS `prev` when exits are unknown or still consistent with `prev`. This kills the false-stall on recall/teleport/walk-through-unmapped while keeping B110's protection against blind file-order teleports. **Architecture (the resolver is now PURE).** The whole thing is a module-level pure function `resolveGenieRoom(pool, normDesc, liveExits, prev, sourceFileToZoneId, staleCount) → { match, staleCount }` (deterministic, no refs, no side effects — testable against real map XML), driven from a SINGLE `useEffect` that owns the breadcrumb (`prevLocationRef`) and the cross-zone hold counter (`staleCountRef`) and advances them in exactly one place after the resolve. The previous design was an impure `useMemo` that **mutated `staleZoneCountRef` and read `prevLocRef` as it computed** — fragile because React may re-invoke a memo and **StrictMode double-invokes it in dev** (`npm start`), so the hold counter double-counted and the cross-zone behavior differed between dev and packaged builds. `currentLocation` is now `useState` set by the effect (one-frame lag, imperceptible for a map). The effect has an **idempotency gate** (`lastResolveRef` compares pool-identity + desc + exits) so StrictMode's double-mount-invoke doesn't advance the refs twice. **Don't move resolution back into a memo, and don't mutate refs mid-render** — pool (the title-matched candidate list) stays a pure memo, but the stateful resolve lives in the effect. `pool`/`roomDesc`/`roomExits` all derive from one `roomState`, so they're coherent per render. **`--stormfront` vs `--genie` is irrelevant** to this: the front-end flag doesn't change the room title/desc/exits we receive; matching on desc+exits works under stormfront. When adding a new map-matching signal, prefer it as another rung in this ladder over replacing the desc/exit conjunction. The Genie map's data has NO Lich/Simu room ids, so it is fundamentally title+desc+exits (the Lich Map matches by roomId first); don't try to add roomId matching to the Genie path.

71. **Critical STATE must not be gated behind `requestAnimationFrame` (or timers) without a hidden-window fallback — Electron throttles/pauses rAF + timers for a minimized/occluded/backgrounded window, which FREEZES any state applied through them (v0.11.7, B157, "idle/minimized loses my map location").** The map indicator kept going stale and stranding on the room the player occupied when the window went idle/minimized — scripted movement didn't move it, but a `LOOK` after restoring the window snapped it to the correct room. Root cause was NOT the matcher: `roomState.title/desc/exits` (everything the matcher reads) is applied through the **rAF room pump** (`roomQueueRef` + `requestAnimationFrame`, pitfall #20), and Electron's `webPreferences.backgroundThrottling` **defaults to `true`**, which throttles rAF and timers to ~1fps (or pauses them) once the window is minimized/occluded. Game events keep arriving over IPC and queue into `roomQueueRef`, but the rAF pump that drains them into `setRoomState` is frozen → room state sticks on the last room → the matcher (correctly) shows the last data it has → `LOOK` after un-minimizing re-runs the pump and snaps. This is a whole CLASS of bug for a client that processes a live stream while backgrounded (multi-session background characters, pitfall #24, are the same shape). **Two-layer fix:** (a) **`backgroundThrottling: false`** on every `BrowserWindow` ([main.ts](src/main/main.ts) `createWindow`) so the renderer stays fully live when minimized — the right call for this app, which is *designed* to keep processing the game stream in the background (socket stays connected; the cost is normal CPU while minimized, which is exactly what a connected MUD client should do); (b) the room pump itself checks **`document.hidden`** and, when hidden, drains the queue **synchronously** (coalesced to the latest state, cancelling any pending rAF) instead of scheduling rAF — so room-state correctness never depends on platform throttling behavior (some OS/Electron versions still pause rAF for a *minimized* window even with throttling off). The visible-window path keeps the one-room-per-frame rAF pump (pitfall #20's anti-skip behavior — which only matters when someone is watching). **General rule: rAF and `setTimeout`/`setInterval` are for COSMETIC pacing (scroll snaps, map animations, smooth camera) — never the sole delivery path for STATE the app must keep current while backgrounded. If you add a new rAF/timer-throttled state pump, gate it on `document.hidden` with a direct-apply fallback, and remember `backgroundThrottling:false` is already keeping the rest of the renderer alive.** When debugging "state goes stale only when the window is idle/minimized/in the background, and a manual refresh fixes it," suspect a throttled rAF/timer feeding that state before suspecting the consumer. **Second instance of this class — the scroll PIN (B191, v0.14.1, Sekmeht):** `stickToBottom`'s rAF settle loop keeps the story window pinned by re-arming `suppressUntilRef` each frame and chasing Virtuoso's async last-row measurement. When the window is OCCLUDED (another app covering Lichborne — NOT minimized; occlusion throttles rAF too), the loop stalls, the +300ms suppress expires before the async measurement grows `scrollHeight`, and the late `scroll` event un-pins the active char via `handleVirtuosoScroll` → a spurious "New Lines" badge that survives the return (`onRefocus` re-snaps only `if (pinnedRef.current)`). Fix wasn't a synchronous drain (like the room pump) but a GUARD: **`handleVirtuosoScroll` returns early when `document.hidden`** — a user can't scroll a hidden window, so any scroll signal there is layout, not intent. The general lesson generalizes: not just "deliver state without rAF while hidden" but also "**don't let rAF-throttle-induced layout events drive user-intent state transitions** (pin/un-pin, focus, selection) while hidden — gate those on `document.hidden` too." Background (`display:none`, 0×0) characters are immune to this whole family by construction; it's an ACTIVE-window-only bug class.

72. **Qt `@Variant` blobs use MINIMAL hex escapes (`\x1`, not `\x01`) — a fixed-width 2-char decoder corrupts every byte after the first single-digit escape (v0.11.9, B159, Frostbite import).** Frostbite stores highlight colours and the `options` bitarray as QSettings-INI `@Variant(...)` byte blobs, byte-escaped like `\0\0\0\x43\x1\xff\xff…`. The shared decoder `parseQtEscapes` ([colorUtils.ts](src/renderer/import/colorUtils.ts)) read **two** chars after `\x` (`s.slice(i+1,i+3)`) and advanced by a fixed **3** — but Qt writes the *minimal* hex for a byte, so a value of 1 is `\x1` (ONE digit), not `\x01`. On a single-digit escape the 2-char slice grabbed the digit **plus the next `\`**, `parseInt` stopped at the `\` (so the VALUE was right, 1), but `i += 3` **overshot past that `\`**, desyncing every subsequent byte. The colour spec byte is `\x1`, so EVERY colour blob desynced right after it → wrong R/G/B (non-null, so it silently produced wrong colours, never an error — undetected since the Frostbite importer first shipped). It only became visible when the v0.11.9 options-decode used the same `parseQtEscapes` to read the bitarray data byte: the desync frequently set bit 3 (`0x08` = "match groups") → the parser flagged most rows `partial` ("a lot of options showing partial" — the reporter's exact symptom). **Fix:** read **1–2 hex digits greedily** (stop at the first non-hex) and advance by however many were consumed — `i++` past `x`, then `while (len<2 && isHex(s[i])) consume`. This is faithful to Qt's own greedy-hex reader and fixes BOTH the colour corruption and the options byte. **General rule: when hand-decoding any escaped byte stream, never assume fixed-width escapes — Qt (and C, and many INI/serializers) emit minimal-width hex/octal, so consume variable-width and advance by the actual count.** The tell for this bug class: values that *parse to plausible-but-wrong* results (not crashes), and corruption that starts right after the first short escape. Verified by bundling the real parser (esbuild) against the reporter's actual file rather than trusting a reimplementation — do that for any "is the parse correct?" question (the pitfall #61b / Iron-rule lesson: check against parsed data).

73. **A Qt QSettings INI array's `size=N` is UNRELIABLE — iterate the indices actually present, not `1..size` (v0.12.0, mute/sub import audit).** Qt writes an array section as `size=N` plus indexed `N\field` keys, and every Frostbite parser here originally looped `for (i=1; i<=size; i++)`. But real exports carry a STALE size: storm-gray `substitutes.ini` declares `size=88` yet contains a fully-formed entry `89\…` (a Main-target sub) — the size-loop **silently dropped entry 89** (and would drop any entry past a stale `size`, or mis-handle a gap). The Iron-rule check (bundle the real parser, count against the file) caught it: 88 parsed vs 89 present. **Fix:** `arrayIndices(section, field)` ([frostbite.ts](src/renderer/import/parsers/frostbite.ts)) scans the section's keys for `^(\d+)\\<field>$` and returns the sorted distinct indices — robust to a wrong `size` AND to index gaps. Applied to **all three** Frostbite array sections (highlights `\value`, ignores `\pattern`, substitutes `\pattern`). The empty-pattern guard (`if (!pattern.trim()) continue`) still skips blanks. **General rule: never trust a serialized count field as the loop bound when the actual records are independently keyed — derive the bound from the records present.** Same class as #72 (don't trust the format's own framing; verify against the bytes). NOTE: editing a source file with a stray null byte via a `latin1` read/write round-trip **double-encodes every multibyte UTF-8 char** (`─`→`â…`) — strip null bytes at the Buffer level (`buf.filter(b=>b!==0)`); to UNDO a latin1-corruption, `Buffer.from(readUtf8, 'latin1')` recovers the original bytes.

74. **Floating-window layout (Windowed Panels / Free Layout, §33) has four geometry traps — all resolved by making geometry DETERMINISTIC + EXPLICIT, recorded after a long tester-iteration (v0.13.0, Sekmeht). Don't reinvent the dead ends.**
   - **(a) NEVER `height: undefined` (auto-height) on a window.** Chrome bars (command/vitals/icon) were first auto-height so the window hugged the bar — it LOOKED right but an auto-height window measures **0-tall on first paint** and only gets real height on a later re-measure, so the icon bar rendered invisible after conversion, then "popped in" at full height and **shoved the whole layout the first time the user clicked anything**. Fix: FIXED height (the conversion bakes `bar + TITLE_PX` into `rect.h`); user-resize changes that EXPLICIT value, which is fine. A window's height must always be a concrete px/fraction, never browser-computed.
   - **(b) `parseFloat(el.style.x) || fallback` reverts a window snapped to the top/left edge (position 0).** Drag/resize write px to `el.style` during the gesture and commit on mouseup by reading them back; `parseFloat("0px") || start` → `0` is falsy → commits the STALE `start`, not 0. So a window flush at the top/left container edge looked docked but its stored rect was wrong, and the next re-render (e.g. starting a resize) "jumped it out." Fix: a 0-safe `numPx()` (`Number.isFinite` guard) in [FloatingWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/FloatingWindow.tsx). **Any `parseFloat(coord) || fallback` over a position/size is this bug.**
   - **(c) Conversion is a CASCADE, not pixel-for-pixel.** Recreating the panels layout exactly (measure each zone/strip, mint a window there) fights forever — titled windows are bigger than edge-to-edge strips, so they overlap and "scale weirdly" (the bottom command bar constricted the whole layout via a de-overlap/main-shrink pass). Abandoned for `buildWindowsFromCurrentLayout` = default sizes at staggered positions (only chrome HEIGHTS measured). Don't re-attempt measure-and-mint.
   - **(d) Resize handles sit INSIDE the window edges (inset 0), not straddling at negative insets.** With `-3px` insets + the layer's `overflow:hidden`, a window flush at the layer edge had its top/side handles clipped → unreachable ("can't grab the top to resize/move"). Inset-0 handles are always within the layer; title-bar buttons carry `z-index:1` so corner handles don't block them.
   **Meta-lesson:** floating-window geometry breeds emergent layout bugs you can't predict by reading code — the fix is always to make the geometry *deterministic and explicit* (fixed heights, 0-safe coordinate parsing, default-size conversion), not to lean on the browser to compute it.

75. **Map structural colors are force-cascaded from the general palette — a per-theme `--map-*` structural literal is INERT — and overlay text in a tight box must pin `line-height: 1` (B161 / B162, v0.13.1).** Two map/theme traps found together. **(a) The Theme Editor only edits the GENERAL vars** (`--bg-app`, `--text-*`, …), never the specialty `--map-*` set. For years `darkBase` left `--map-bg: var(--bg-app)` cascading, but every OTHER built-in theme PINNED `--map-bg` (and the rest of the map palette) to literals — so editing a built-in theme's App Background moved every surface EXCEPT the map (only the stock **Dark** theme's map followed, because it alone left the vars cascading — that's the diagnostic tell Binu spotted). **Fix: the 12 STRUCTURAL map colors live in `MAP_STRUCTURAL_CASCADE` ([themes.ts](src/renderer/themes.ts)) — one block wired to general vars (`--map-bg`→`var(--bg-app)`, `--map-text`→`var(--text-secondary)`, chrome/border/node-fill/node-stroke/dot→their bg/border/text counterparts) — spread into `darkBase` AND re-applied LAST in BOTH `applyTheme`/`applyCustomTheme`, so a theme's pinned literal can NEVER win.** Consequence: **a structural `--map-*` override in a theme object is now dead code** (force-applied over it); the ~18 built-in themes still carry their old literals (harmless, superseded) — don't add new ones, and don't be confused that they're ignored. Only the SEMANTIC cues stay per-theme and overridable: `--map-arc-*` (directional path lines — need per-background hue/legibility), `--map-current-color` (green you-are-here marker), `--map-select-color`. When adding a new map color: surface/text/border → add it to `MAP_STRUCTURAL_CASCADE` as a `var(--general)`; semantic cue → leave it per-theme. The Lich Map's baked **PNG tiles** are NOT themable this way (image pixels, separate concern). This is the pitfall #34 family (literal that should cascade), but enforced centrally rather than per-theme. **(b) Overlay text centered in a TIGHT box must pin `line-height: 1`.** `.vital-text` ([vitalsbar.css](src/renderer/styles/vitalsbar.css)) had no `line-height`, so it inherited the game-area's (~1.4). The roomy non-compact bar absorbs the extra leading, but the compact bar (`1em`) can't — the taller line-box overflowed it and the baseline shoved the caps/digits optically high ("M: 100%" sat toward the top).
