Flex `align-items: center` centers the LINE BOX, not the glyphs, so inherited leading on a no-descender string reads as "too high" the moment the container is short. Rule: any absolutely-positioned, flex-centered text overlay on a short bar/chip should set `line-height: 1` so it centers on its own glyph box rather than an inherited multiplier.

76. **The Lich Scripts `;listall` auto-poll is gated on a Lich Scripts panel being OPEN — anything Lichborne injects is indistinguishable from typed input to Lich's scripts, so don't poll when nobody's watching (B163, Binu v0.13.1).** The running-scripts list is refreshed by injecting `;listall` from `useLichBridge` ([useLichBridge.ts](src/renderer/hooks/useLichBridge.ts)) every 5s. It was gated only on `connected` and `useLichBridge` is mounted per-session in GameWindow, so it polled for EVERY connected character even with no scripts panel visible. **Why that's harmful, not just wasteful:** Lichborne and Lich share ONE front-end socket, and Lich's `do_client` runs `UpstreamHook.run(client_string)` on every client line BEFORE it checks for `;` commands ([global_defs.rb:2225](C:/temp/lich-dev/lich-5/lib/global_defs.rb#L2225)) — so a script with an upstream hook (dr-scripts automap) sees our `;listall` **byte-for-byte as if the player typed it**. Binu's automap, which records the last command to associate with a room transition, captured a `;listall` that pulsed at the same instant as his movement. **There is NO way to inject a "synthetic" command Lich's scripts won't see** (one socket, no side channel, hooks run first) — the only fix is to not send it. **Fix (Idea A):** a `lichScriptsOpen` memo in GameWindow (a `lichScripts` tab present in an added zone in Static-Panels mode, or in a floating window's tabs in Windowed mode) drives `lichPollRef`; the poll interval reads the ref and injects nothing while closed, and the open transition fires one immediate seed poll (`refresh()`). Panel closed → zero `;listall`. **Don't un-gate this** (e.g. "the panel feels stale on open" — the seed handles that) or move the poll somewhere it runs unconditionally again. The RESPONSE-side intercept (`interceptLine`, pitfall #22) is unchanged — a player-typed `;list` still updates the panel and its output still shows. `useLichBridge` feeds ONLY the `lichScripts` PanelFrame tab (the Lich Dashboard sources scripts separately), so the panel-open check is the complete signal. The "listen to Lich's `active.`/`has exited.` notices to avoid polling even with the panel open" idea was explicitly **deferred** (Sekmeht, don't build it without a fresh ask).

77. **A panel header's BAR HEIGHT, not just its text size, makes it look "giant" — pin the title `line-height: 1` and keep action icons from driving the strip (B164, v0.13.1).** The Lich Scripts "ACTIVE SCRIPTS" header (`.sl-header-title`) shipped at `1.04em` (larger than the game font); shrinking the text to the section-label scale (`0.84em`, cf. `.room-panel-section-label` `0.88em`, with `em` not `px` letter-spacing so it scales) was only HALF the fix. The strip still read 2-3x the text height because the title had **no `line-height`**, so it inherited the game line-height (~1.4-1.5) and ballooned the bar — the **exact pitfall #75(b) trap** (a tight container can't absorb inherited leading). Fix: `line-height: 1` on the title, trim the bar padding (`6px → 2px` vertical), and stop any action icon (the refresh `↻`) from being the tallest child — `font-size: 0.9em`, `line-height: 1`, no vertical padding. The Scripts panel's FOOTER (`.sl-footer`, the "N scripts · …" status strip) had the same disease — `0.96em` text, NO `line-height` — and was actually the taller strip; same fix (`line-height: 1`, smaller metadata font `0.8em`, trimmed padding). **For any panel chrome strip — header OR footer/status: size the text in `em` off the panel root (anchored to `var(--panel-font-size, var(--game-font-size))`, pitfall #58), pin `line-height: 1`, keep buttons/icons at ≤1em with `line-height: 1`, and use minimal (2-3px) vertical padding.** Two smells: a strip's text rendered *bigger* than the body it relates to, OR a strip *bar* much taller than its own text.

78. **DR does NOT push `<right>`/`<left>` hand XML for every action that puts an item in a hand — the parser carries a glance-TEXT fallback; keep its suppression rules intact when touching it (B165, v0.13.2).** JadedSoul's "held item shows as Empty in the hand bar" (right hand more often): the entire in-app path was verified clean against the real parser (bundled `StormFrontParser` fed the exact item incl. quotes/entities/1000-char names — all well-formed shapes parse; renderer/IconBar/replay-snapshot/interceptLine checked too), so the update either never arrived well-formed or was never sent — and the protocol-level gap is REAL: Profanity hard-codes the same inference ([game_text_processor.rb](file:///c:/temp/Profanity/ProfanityFE/lib/game_text_processor.rb), "You glance down at your empty hands." → force both Empty) because custom-verb/event items can land in a hand with no hand tag emitted. **The fallback:** `inferHandsFromGlance` ([StormFrontParser.ts](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts)), called once per `parse()` after the token loop, derives hand events from glance text: the both-hands form, the single-hand forms (the OTHER hand is inferred `Empty` — glance always reports complete state), and the empty-hands form; leading articles stripped (`a bamboo folder…` → `bamboo folder…`) so inferred names read like tag-driven ones. **Five suppression rules, all load-bearing — don't weaken them:** (1) skipped when the same line already emitted a real `hand` event (XML stays authoritative; checked AFTER the token loop, which is why the call site sits after `flushSegments`); (2) never runs when `activeStream !== 'main'` / `streamStack` non-empty / the raw line contains a push/popStream tag (a Lich script echoing glance-shaped text into a panel must not touch the hand bars); (3) patterns are `^`-anchored on the tag-stripped line so quoted speech (`You say, "You are holding…"`) can't match; (4) a cheap `includes()` substring gate runs before any regex/strip work (this fires on every game line — keep the hot path cheap); (5) the single-hand captures reject anything containing another `' in your '` phrase — an unmodeled sentence shape (e.g. a hypothetical left-first ordering) must become a safe NO-OP, not a greedy mis-assignment of the whole tail into one hand. Minor accepted behavior: GameWindow calls `processVariableChange('right'/'left', …)` on every hand event without comparing old value (pre-existing — DR re-sends hand tags on no-change occasions too), so a `$right`/`$left` variable-watch trigger also fires on glance; cooldowns are the user-side lever. Known cosmetic quirk: an inferred name is the glance long form (full tap) vs the tag's short form; the next real tag corrects it. **Support takeaway:** `glance` is now the universal hand-bar re-sync — if a tester's hand bar is wrong AFTER a glance on v0.13.2+, that's a new signal worth a Debug-panel raw-XML capture. The remount-without-replay hole was closed in v0.13.3 (`session:reload` now arms a pitfall-#60 replay, restoring hands and all sticky state) — found while chasing JadedSoul's report, though her clarification (LB restarted several times between import and symptom — a remount desync can't survive a restart) means her actual sightings were most likely the PROTOCOL gap this fallback covers, not the remount. On v0.13.3+ the one remaining signal is a wrong hand bar AFTER a *glance* — that's a new protocol shape worth a Debug raw-XML capture (notably: capture a LOGIN with an item already in hand, to learn whether DR sends hand tags in the login burst at all).

79. **Every "which tabs/streams are visible/watched" aggregation in GameWindow MUST branch on `layoutMode` — the zone arrays are STALE STATE in free mode (B167/B168, v0.13.2).** In Windowed Panels the zone skeleton isn't rendered, but the zone tab arrays (`mainTopTabs`/`topTabs`/`midTabs`/`bottomTabs` + active ids + `*Added` flags) keep their last panels-mode values. Any aggregation built only from zones is therefore wrong in free mode, in BOTH directions: it misses tabs that live in floating windows, and it counts zone tabs that aren't on screen. Three real hits: **(a) `activeIdsRef`** (unread-dot suppression) was zone-only → in free mode the Arrivals dot re-lit even while its tab was visible, and nothing ever cleared it because **(b)** `clearUnread` was wired only to the zone `onActive` handlers — the floating-window `onActiveChange` (in `renderFreeContent`) now clears too (B167, Sekmeht — "unread indicator stays lit in windowed mode"). The same audit found `mainTopActiveId` had been missing from `activeIdsRef` since the Main-Top zone shipped (active Main-Top tab re-marked itself unread). **(c) `watchedStreamsRef`** (STREAM_FALLBACK routing, pitfall #39) was zone-only → in free mode a stream watched only by a window DOUBLE-displayed (fallback also routed it to main), and a stream still in a stale zone array but closed in windows had its fallback BLOCKED — content silently buffered, invisible (B168, found by audit, unreported). **The pattern (use it for any new aggregation):** `layoutMode === 'free' ? <derive from freeWindows[].tabs / freeWindows[].activeId> : <derive from zones gated on *Added>` — exactly what `lichScriptsOpen` (pitfall #76) and `debugOpen` (B166) already do; include `layoutMode` + `freeWindows` in the effect/memo deps. In free mode "visible" = every window's `activeId` (all windows are on screen at once) and "watched" = every tab of every `kind:'panel'` window. **When adding any new per-tab feature (badges, counters, routing, polling gates), grep for these four sites and mirror the branch** — and conversely, do NOT "fix" the stale zone arrays by syncing them to windows; they're deliberately preserved so switching back to Static Panels restores the old layout.

80. **Lich's default `inventory_boxes_off` downstream hook EATS `<right>`/`<left>` hand tags with a greedy regex — Lichborne disarms it by sending Wrayth's `_flag Display Inventory Boxes 1` once per Lich session; don't remove that send, and don't send it on direct-SGE (B169, v0.13.3 — the TRUE root cause of B165).** Lich installs the hook BY DEFAULT for stormfront-style FEs ([main.rb:546](C:/temp/lich-dev/lich-5/lib/main/main.rb)): any server line **starting** with `<container`/`<clearContainer`/`<exposeContainer` gets `gsub(/<(?:container|clearContainer|exposeContainer)[^>]*>|<inv.+\/inv>/, '')` — and the greedy `<inv.+\/inv>` spans from the FIRST `<inv` to the LAST `/inv>` on the line, swallowing anything between two inv blocks, including a hand tag (the exact shape DR emits on a GET from a container when the player's game-side "display all inventory and container windows" account flag is on). Wrayth disarms it at bootstrap with `_flag Display Inventory Boxes 1` (Lich's upstream hook consumes the command — it NEVER reaches DR — removes the eater, and persists player_id in lich.db3 so [xmlparser.rb:604](C:/temp/lich-dev/lich-5/lib/common/xmlparser.rb) auto-removes it at every future login). Lichborne mimics that: [main.ts](src/main/main.ts) `wireSession` sends it ONCE on the first `player-info` event (the `<app>` tag — arrives AFTER `<playerID>`, so the persistence write has a real id), gated on `s.meta?.useLich` + the one-shot `s.invBoxesFixSent`. **Never send it on a direct-SGE connection** — with no Lich to intercept, it goes to DR and flips the player's REAL account flag (changing their Wrayth experience); direct connections have no hook and no bug. The newly-flowing container XML is fully absorbed by the parser (`container`/`clearcontainer`/`exposecontainer` in SILENT_TAGS, `<inv>` capture-discarded, pushStream `inv` deliberately has no main fallback) — zero display change. **Debugging legacy:** this hid as B165's "random items" hand desync (container gets land in the free/right hand → right-hand bias; with the account flag on, the LOGIN dump also rides container lines → "persists through restarts"); only testers with the game-side flag on can reproduce. The parser itself was proven clean by replaying Frostbite's real captured session (`C:/temp/Frostbite-Dev/frostbite/support/mock.xml`, 1225 lines incl. login hand tags) — when a tag-level loss looks impossible in-parser, suspect LICH'S DOWNSTREAM HOOKS next (grep `DownstreamHook.add` in lich-5; `textsubs` and friends rewrite the same stream). The glance fallback (pitfall #78) stays as defense-in-depth for genuine protocol gaps (spell-summoned items).

81. **Scrollback cap-trims use HYSTERESIS via `appendTrimmed()` — never re-introduce a per-batch `slice(-MAX_LINES)` head-trim, and don't reach for Virtuoso's `firstItemIndex` (B171, v0.13.4).** The long-untraceable "text hops at the bottom after a while / pinned hold doesn't last / scroll gets less smooth" was NOT the scroll machinery (pitfall #68's `stickToBottom` architecture is sound) — it was the **MAX_LINES cap**, which is why it only appeared after ~2000 lines and survived every scroll rewrite. Holding `lines` at exactly the cap by trimming the head every batch breaks the pinned hold via two coupled mechanisms (both measured in a post-paint simulation harness replicating GameWindow's machinery verbatim): **(a)** react-virtuoso keys its row-size/offset cache **by INDEX** — `computeItemKey` only stabilizes React DOM reuse, not the measurement cache (verified in the library source) — so an uncompensated head-trim shifts every row's index per batch, staling the cache against variable-height rows; painted content jumps BACKWARD up to ~8 lines (26 jumps/12s at-cap vs zero pre-cap). **(b)** With count constant at the cap (trim N + append N), total list height is ~unchanged, so `totalListHeightChanged` — the ONLY per-batch `stickToBottom` trigger — frequently doesn't fire (~2.0 calls/batch pre-cap → 0.73 at-cap): no correction, no suppress window armed, and a late re-measure trips the 40px deadband → un-pin. **The fix is `appendTrimmed(prev, added)`** ([GameWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx)): grow freely to `MAX_LINES + TRIM_CHUNK` (2400), then ONE cut back to 2000 — between trims the count grows every batch so the height callback keeps firing, and the rare big cut changes height so much the callback always fires and the existing sync-write + settle loop absorbs it in-frame (0 hops in the harness). ALL `setLines` appends route through this one helper (game batches, hard-cap resume, End/badge re-pin, command echoes — echoes used to micro-shift the view on every keypress at cap). **`firstItemIndex` was tested and rejected** — Virtuoso's compensating `scrollBy` races our raw `scrollTop` writes (more off-bottom painted frames in both tested variants); it's the right tool only for lists where Virtuoso owns the scrolling, which ours deliberately isn't (pitfall #68). Selection-copy (B152) is unaffected: the un-pinned path (where users scroll up and drag-select) never trimmed and still doesn't; pinned trims remove only the oldest head lines, now later and far less often. **General rules:** (a) a capped virtualized list must trim in CHUNKS (hysteresis), never per-append at the exact cap; (b) any new bounded buffer rendered by Virtuoso gets the same shape; (c) when "the view misbehaves only after a long session," suspect the buffer cap engaging before suspecting the scroll math — pre-cap vs at-cap is the diagnostic split (repro harness: `tmp-scroll-repro/`, disposable; `node tmp-scroll-repro/build.mjs; npx electron tmp-scroll-repro/main.js`).

82. **The per-line rule-evaluation hot path has FOUR load-bearing perf structures — keep all four when touching rules, panels, or the event pipeline (B172, v0.13.4; "chunky travel" with a 1,544-highlight imported ruleset).** Real user rulesets are huge and regex-heavy (imports: Genie triggers are always regex, Frostbite alternations become regex), so per-line work is multiplied by rules × segments × panels × batches. The four structures, and the rules they impose:
    - **(a) Every rule-evaluation site gates on `fastLower` first** (`lower.includes(cr.fastLower)` before `regex.exec`). `fastLower` comes from ONE decider — `literalGate(mode, pattern)` in [regexLiteral.ts](src/renderer/regexLiteral.ts) — used by BOTH compile sites (`useCompiledHighlights`, `useTriggerEngine`). Regex-mode rules get `extractRegexLiteral`: a CONSERVATIVE walker returning a literal **guaranteed present in any match** (null on top-level alternation; optional atoms excluded; required groups mined recursively; `\xHH`/`\uHHHH` decoded). **Invariant: a wrong literal silently kills a rule; a missed literal only costs speed — when editing the walker, always err toward returning null**, and re-run the `tmp-scroll-repro/check-literals.mjs` validation (bundles the real extractor against the real profile, asserts zero gate-vs-regex disagreements). Text-mode gates on the LONGEST TOKEN, not the whole pattern (tokens compile joined by `\s+`, so the full string isn't a guaranteed substring — that was a latent over-gating bug). New rule-evaluation loops MUST copy the gate.
    - **(b) Line-wide match scanning runs ONCE per line** via `computeLineMatchRanges` ([renderSegmentFull.tsx](src/renderer/utils/renderSegmentFull.tsx)); per-segment `renderSegmentFull` calls receive the shared ranges and just intersect (TextLineRow, RoomPanel sections). Don't add a render path that calls `renderSegmentFull` per segment WITHOUT precomputed ranges on multi-segment content — that re-runs the whole ruleset × segment count (the pre-B172 shape).
    - **(c) Panels are memoized; their props must stay referentially stable.** StreamPanel/RoomPanel/ExpPanel/MapPanel are `memo()` — so PanelFrame's `renderPanel` uses module-level `EMPTY_ARRAY`/`EMPTY_SET`/`NOOP` fallbacks (never inline `?? []`/`?? new Set()`/`?? (() => {})`), StreamPanel's `onClear`/`onToggleTimestamp` take the `streamId` as an argument (no per-render `() => f(id)` closures), and the GameWindow callbacks that feed panels are `useCallback`. **The two context provider values (`HighlightsContext`, `ContactsContext`) are `useMemo`'d in GameWindow — never revert them to inline `value={{...}}` literals** (that re-renders every consumer on every render and silently defeats ALL panel memos; it's invisible until a big ruleset makes it expensive). When adding a panel: memo it, check every prop's identity, and remember a consumed context value is part of that check.
    - **(d) Main coalesces event floods** — `scheduleFlush` ([main.ts](src/main/main.ts)) is a leading-edge throttle (`FLUSH_COALESCE_MS` 16ms): immediate when idle, ~one batch per frame during a Lich flood, so the renderer renders once per frame instead of once per socket chunk. Don't revert to bare `setImmediate`, don't make it trailing-only (adds latency to sparse interactive lines), and don't lower it below a frame.
    Diagnostic split for "the client feels chunky during floods": measure whether the cost is per-BATCH (too many renders → d), per-LINE (rule evaluation → a), per-SEGMENT (scan multiplier → b), or per-RENDER (tree breadth → c). The profile-driven numbers that motivated this are in BUGS.md B172.

83. **Never gate the MOUNTED-NESS of stateful children on a live-measured size — a hidden character tab measures 0×0, and "size is 0" must mean "don't paint geometry yet," never "unmount" (B174, v0.13.4).** WindowLayer rendered its FloatingWindows behind `{size.w > 0 && size.h > 0 && ...}` with `size` fed raw from a ResizeObserver. Correct-looking — until a character tab goes `display:none` (pitfall #24): the layer measures 0×0, the observer pushes it, and React UNMOUNTS every floating window of the hidden character. Every tab switch silently destroyed and rebuilt the hidden character's whole windowed UI (map reloading the Lich DB + Genie zones, Virtuoso rebuilding the text — the "everything redraws / blips" report). The pattern that fixes it: **the measure callback ignores 0×0 and keeps the LAST REAL size**, so the render gate degenerates to a first-mount-only "never measured yet" guard; stale px geometry while hidden is harmless (the ancestor is display:none — nothing paints) and the observer re-fires with the true size on re-show. When adding any container that converts fractional/relative child geometry via a measured size (an overlay layer, a future Experiences layer §34, a minimap), apply the same shape. **Companion trap (same bug):** an effect like `useEffect(() => { if (version === 0) return; reload() }, [version])` re-fires on every REMOUNT once version ≥ 1, doubling the mount-time load — guard "changed since mount" with a ref initialized to the mount-time value (`lastRef = useRef(version)`), not with a `=== initialValue` check. **Debugging lesson:** when a remount is observed but every key/provider/conditional reads stable, stop theorizing and drop temporary mount/unmount `console.log`s at the suspect levels — one reproduction beat several hours of static analysis here (the `[diag]` pattern: GameWindow/panel mount+unmount, replay delivery, loader starts).

84. **Constant-size UI must NOT render inside a transform-scaled (or em-rescaled) subtree — counter-scaling it in place is whack-a-mole; render it in a sibling PIXEL-SPACE layer instead (B182, v0.14.0, the Tableau bubble layer).** The Living Tableau scales its figures two ways (a per-figure `transform: scale(--fig-sc)` for depth, plus an `.tableau-scene--large` em-rescale for the amphitheater), and speech bubbles originally rendered INSIDE the figure divs — so they inherited every scaling layer, and each "make the text bigger" fix (em bumps, absolute `var(--game-font-size)`, an inline `scale(1/figScale)` counter-transform) fixed one inheritance path while another kept shrinking them ("bubbles still tiny at >12 people"). The durable fix: bubbles moved OUT of the figure tree into a flat layer in scene-PIXEL space — the component measures its container with a ResizeObserver (**0×0-guarded, pitfall #83** — hidden tabs measure 0×0) and positions each bubble itself, which makes constant sizing true BY CONSTRUCTION and unlocks what in-figure rendering never could: **collision-aware placement** (newest bubble takes the spot nearest its speaker; earlier ones get pushed up; nothing overlaps) with the tail offset (`--tail-dx`) still aiming at the speaker and the speaker's NAME inside the bubble for when it had to drift. Layout-geometry ESTIMATES (char-count × font-size) are fine for SPACING — CSS still does the real text wrapping; a generous estimate is just generous spacing — don't reach for measure-then-relayout passes. When any future surface needs "this child stays readable regardless of how its parent scales" (HUD readouts over the Spar Arena figures, radar labels, X6 captions), start with the sibling-layer pattern, not a counter-transform.

85. **Two auto-detection traps from the B184 guild-badging saga (v0.14.0) — both bit a real tester within the hour.** (a) **A stored preference that rides `TRANSFER_CATEGORIES` is NOT proof of an explicit user choice for THIS character** — Profile Transfer copies the raw scopedKey, so a transferred value is byte-identical to a hand-picked one. The exp panel's Badging first shipped with "stored `focus` wins forever over guild detection," and Sekmeht's cleric was permanently stuck on a Moon Mage badging that Transfer's viewPrefs category had planted — his corrective `info` was *correctly ignored* by the broken rule. The fix: fresh authoritative GAME data (the character's own `info` sheet) OVERRIDES the stored value (`handleFocusChange`, so it persists); a manual pick holds only until the next own-sheet detection. **When auto-detection and a stored preference conflict, ask whether the stored value could have arrived via Transfer/import before granting it permanent supremacy** — "explicit wins forever" is only sound for keys that can ONLY be written by direct user action on that character. (b) **DR's `info` sheet Name field is the FULL TITLED name** — `Name: Soul Reaver Cordio Hawt-Seord, Divine Hammer of Elanthia   Race: Dwarf   Guild: Cleric` — titles BEFORE the first name, hyphenated surname + comma honorific after. Any "is this sheet about our character" check must match the character name as a whole WORD anywhere in the field (escaped, case-insensitive); a first-token compare rejects the player's OWN sheet. Related verbatim-mirroring detail: Lich's `NameRaceGuild` regex (drparser.rb:10) uses GREEDY captures with a trailing `\b\s+` anchor — a lazy port captures "Moon" instead of "Moon Mage". The titled line is a permanent harness case; the `character-guild` event is deliberately NOT behind the §35.6 Experience gate (badging works without Experiences), and `detectedGuild` is deliberately NOT transferable (guild is character identity).

86. **Every command-send closure in GameWindow MUST send through `sessionIdRef.current`, never a captured `session.sessionId` — AND a build + tsc pass does NOT prove a side-effecting call still exists (B189/B190 + a self-inflicted regression, v0.14.1).** Two intertwined lessons from the Morress (macros) / Sekmeht (automapper) "command echoes but nothing happens, and no `>` prompt comes back" reports. **(a) The architecture rule.** A GameWindow is keyed by `characterId`, and a tab Reconnect swaps in a NEW `sessionId` WITHOUT remounting (pitfall #69). So any send closure that *captures* `session.sessionId` goes stale after a reconnect — main's `SEND_COMMAND` handler does `getSession(sessionId)` and **silently `return`s if it misses**, so the command is dropped while the renderer-side echo (`setLines`) still paints `>cmd`. The held-stale closures were: the macro keydown handler (mounted ONCE, `[]` deps — calls `sendCommandSequence` directly), the `sendCommand` `useCallback` (`[]` deps — drives map-walk / room-exit / Quick Send), and the `triggerCallbacks` `useMemo`. Typed commands never broke because the command-bar handler is re-created every render with the live id. **Fix: route ALL of them through `sessionIdRef.current`** (a ref synced every render at the `[session.sessionId]` effect, line ~288) — it reads the live id even from a first-render closure. When you add ANY new command-send path, send via `sessionIdRef.current`, not `session.sessionId`. The diagnostic signature for this whole class: *a command echoes but the game never responds and no prompt returns, while typed commands still work* → a stale session id in a held closure. **(b) The process lesson (the actual time-sink here).** While ADDING the explanatory comment to `sendCommand`, an Edit **replaced the `window.api.sendCommand(...)` line with the comment text** instead of putting the comment above it — leaving the echo but NO send. **`npm run build:renderer` AND `npx tsc --noEmit` both passed**, because a *deleted side-effecting statement* is still perfectly valid code (unlike the dangling-reference case Check-zero already catches). It shipped to the tester and made the bug WORSE (before: dropped only after reconnect; after: never sent at all). The "I verified the fix is in place" grep confirmed the *comment* was present and never re-read the function BODY. **Lesson: after any Edit that touches a function body — ESPECIALLY one that replaces a line with a comment — re-read the WHOLE body, not a grep for the changed token; build + tsc do NOT catch a removed call.**

87. **An absolute SERVER timestamp must be timed against the SERVER's own clock (the `<prompt time>` tag), NEVER the local `Date.now()` — client clock skew is a real, common, invisible-to-us failure mode, and getting this right is a CLIENT-QUALITY bar, not an edge case (B192, v0.14.2).** DR sends `<roundTime value=N>` / `<castTime value=N>` as an absolute Unix-seconds END time, and its OWN current time in every `<prompt time=T>`. The RT/CT bar used to compute `rt = (N*1000 − Date.now())/1000` — comparing the server's clock to the LOCAL clock. Aubrey's PC was ~1–2 min behind the game server (stale NTP), so `rt = realRT + skew`: the bar maxed (`rt`/`rtMax` inflated equally → `rtPct≈100`) and drained `skew` seconds too late. We could never reproduce it (our clocks were fine), which is exactly why this class is dangerous — **a user's wrong clock manifests as "the client is broken," and the symptom is intermittent (NTP re-syncs and drifts) and survives updates (it's not code).** The fix is to anchor to the server: defer the duration calc to the next `<prompt>` and compute `expires = Date.now() + clamp(N − T, 0, 300s)*1000` — duration from the server (`N − T`), the local clock only as the countdown anchor (and the renderer compares against that same local clock, so the skew cancels). `lastPromptTime`/`pendingRtEnd`/`pendingCtEnd` on the parser carry this; reset on login. **Both siblings do exactly this — Frostbite `xmlparserthread.cpp` (`t_to = N − promptTime`, 300000ms cap) and Genie `Game.cs` (`rt = m_iRoundTime − m_iGameTime`); neither touches the local clock.** That convergence is the tell that server-clock anchoring is the *correct* design, and matching a quality client's behavior here is part of *being* a quality client — a visibly-wrong RT bar reads as a broken client even when the bug is the user's PC. **General rule: any feature that compares a server-supplied absolute time to `Date.now()` (timers, "X minutes ago", cooldowns, expiries) is a latent clock-skew bug — anchor it to the server's clock via the prompt time (track the offset once: `serverNow*1000 − Date.now()`), and prefer a server-derived DURATION over a server-vs-local absolute comparison.** The diagnostic signature: *"a timer/bar is wildly wrong only for one user, intermittently, and updates don't fix it"* → check that user's system clock against real time FIRST (10-second confirm), then anchor the code to the server clock so no one's clock can break it again. **The DR Aim Timer (`firingTimer`, v0.14.3) is the THIRD lane on this exact pattern** — `<dialogData id='AimTimerDialog'><timer id='firingTimer' value='N'/>` carries an absolute END time, deferred + anchored on the next `<prompt>` via the same `pendingAimEnd`/`anchoredExpiry` shape (`value='0'` → emit `expires:0` = clear). Any future server-pushed countdown (a new timer dialog, a buff/debuff duration) MUST join this lane — add a `pending*End`, anchor it in the prompt handler, never compute `value*1000 − Date.now()` inline.

88. **A MUTE (and any display-layer line drop) must be applied at the SAME layer that decides prompt emission, or it orphans the trailing `>` — Lichborne fixes this by replaying the parser's prompt-dedup in the renderer AFTER mutes (B194, v0.14.3).** Cherisse muted her mana-regen messages and saw bare `>` prompts pile up (`>` / `>>` / `>>>…`). Root cause is a LAYER MISMATCH: DR fires a `<prompt>` after every server turn, and the parser already suppresses a prompt identical to the last main text (`lastMainText` in [StormFrontParser.ts](src/main/parser/StormFrontParser.ts) `case 'prompt'`, line ~904) — so consecutive identical prompts collapse upstream. But MUTES are a **display-only renderer concern** (DESIGN §31): they run in GameWindow's `applyTextMods` a layer LATER, after the parser already emitted the prompt. A turn of `<regen msg>` + `>` parses as real-text-then-prompt (so the parser correctly emits the `>`); the mute then removes the regen line, leaving an orphaned `>`, and several muted regens in a row pile up because the parser saw distinct real text between each prompt and never deduped them. **Both sibling clients avoid this by construction — the gag/ignore check runs at the DISPLAY layer, before the prompt is committed:** Genie's `PrintTextToWindow` (`Game.cs` ~2938) `return`s on a gag match so the line never reaches the window, and prompt logic is a separate path a gagged line never touches; Frostbite's `MainLogger::onProcess` (`mainlogger.cpp`) runs `if(alter->ignore(text,…)) return;` BEFORE its `prevType==PROMPT` bookkeeping, and models the prompt as a LAZY marker (`>` emitted only right before the next real content), so consecutive prompts collapse and an ignored line never updates the prompt state. **Lichborne's fix keeps mutes in the renderer** (Principle #2 — display concern, must work without Lich, portable, clean import target) and instead **replicates the parser's identical-prompt dedup at the display layer, after the mute pass**: the parser tags each prompt line `prompt: true` ([types.ts](src/shared/types.ts) `StreamTextEvent`/`TextLine`); GameWindow carries it onto the `TextLine` (`mkLine`), and a collapse pass right after `applyTextMods` drops a prompt line whose text equals the previous DISPLAYED main line when both are prompts, tracked across batches via `lastMainLineRef`. **Three constraints make it safe:** (a) it gates on the `prompt` flag, so repeated REAL content (two identical lines with muted content between) is never collapsed; (b) it matches on prompt-text EQUALITY, so statusprompt drift (`H>`→`R>` with no content between) is preserved — only a redundant identical prompt is dropped; (c) it runs whenever `newMain` has content so the cross-batch ref stays current even when nothing is dropped — and because the parser already deduped identical consecutive prompts upstream, this pass is a NO-OP in the no-mute case (it only ever fires when a mute removed the content the parser saw between two prompts). **The raw XML still streams and the Session Log still captures the raw line** (the log records are built from the pre-mute `lineText`, unchanged) — nothing is lost, satisfying "XML must still stream for stability." **General rule: any feature that DROPS a display line (mutes, a future client-side gag, conditional hiding) must account for adjacent state the upstream parser computed assuming that line was present — prompts are the live example; a dropped line that the parser used as a `lastX`-dedup boundary will orphan whatever the parser emitted after it.** Don't try to fix this by moving mute evaluation into the main-process parser (it would break the renderer-side Session Log capture and force all the group-gating/stream-restrict renderer state into main) — collapse at the display layer instead.

89. **Substitutes are a LINE-level rewrite, but DR fragments a STYLED line into multiple segments — a per-segment substitute can't match a regex (esp. one with capture groups) that spans a preset boundary (B195, v0.14.3).** Cherisse's Gweth-thought substitute `^\[(.*)\] Your mind hears (.*) thinking,\s*"<to you>" (.*)` → `[Gweth][$1][$2] to you: $3` never fired on the GAME's own thoughts, though it worked on lnet thoughts. Root cause: a DR thought arrives as TWO segments — `<preset id='thought'>[Personal] Your mind hears Itheron thinking, </preset>` + `"<to you>" "Test"` — and `applySubstitutesToSegments` ([substitutes.ts](src/renderer/substitutes.ts)) ran the regex **per-segment**, so a pattern spanning the boundary matched neither half. lnet thoughts come through Lich as ONE unbroken segment, which is exactly why those "worked" and the native ones didn't. (Highlights had already been fixed for the same fragmentation in B115 — `computeLineMatchRanges` scans the JOINED line and intersects ranges per-segment — but highlights only STYLE ranges, which map back cleanly; substitutes REPLACE text with capture-group reordering, which can't map back, so they were left per-segment.) **Both siblings substitute on the whole plain-line text** (Genie `ParseSubstitutions`, Frostbite `alter->substitute`) and re-emit the result as one styled unit. **Lichborne's fix (in [substitutes.ts](src/renderer/substitutes.ts), keeping substitutes in the renderer per Principle #2):** run the per-segment pass FIRST (an in-segment match — recolor a word, fix a name inside a monsterbold span — keeps every segment's styling, NO regression), then run a JOINED-line pass; if the joined result differs from the per-segment result, the match crossed a boundary, so COLLAPSE the line to ONE segment carrying the joined-substituted text styled like the first non-empty segment (its primary preset, e.g. `thought`/`speech`) — VISUAL fields (`preset`/`bold`/`fg`/`bg`) only, never link fields (`cmd`/`href`), so a reshaped line can't inherit a stray click target. A single-segment line skips the joined pass (no boundary); an unchanged line returns the SAME array reference (caller's identity check skips the rebuild). Verified against the real captured segments by bundling the actual `substitutes.ts` (Iron rule — a heredoc backslash-escaping artifact made the FIRST string-pattern test falsely "fail," so re-test regex logic with regex LITERALS / `String.raw`, not shell-written pattern strings). **WYSIWYG note (and a sharp Iron-rule lesson): users match against the RENDERED text, and rendered === the regex's match text** because (a) the PARSER trims a segment's trailing whitespace (the `<preset>thought, </preset>` span becomes `thought,` — no trailing space) and (b) `.text-line` is `white-space: pre-wrap`, so the joined segment text displays character-for-character. So Cherisse's literal `thinking,"<to you>"` (no space) is CORRECT — it matches what she sees. **I initially gave the WRONG advice (add `\s*`) by reasoning from the RAW XML (which still carries the preset's trailing space `thinking, `) instead of the PARSER OUTPUT (which trims it).** When reasoning about what text a renderer-side regex (highlight/substitute/trigger) sees, the source of truth is the parser's segment output, NOT the raw socket XML — bundle `StormFrontParser` and dump the segments (a 10-line harness settled it; the raw XML had a space the parser removes). **General rule: any display-text transform that REPLACES text (substitutes, a future rewrite rule) must operate on the joined line for correctness; styling preservation is a best-effort layer ON TOP (in-segment keeps spans, cross-segment collapses) — don't ship a per-segment replacer and expect cross-preset regexes to work. Mutes' `match` scope has the same per-segment shape but is lower-risk (it strips, doesn't reorder); revisit it the same way if a tester hits a cross-segment mute.**

90. **localStorage is the per-character rule store and it has a ~5MB ORIGIN quota shared across ALL characters — a bare `setItem` that hits the quota THROWS and silently loses the write; route every rule save through `safeSetItem` (B197, v0.14.4).** A power user with a huge imported ruleset (JadedSoul: Wrayth+Genie → 3436 highlights) × several characters in one localStorage can blow the quota. The symptom is nasty and misleading: a `saveHighlights`/`saveTriggers`/etc. throws `QuotaExceededError`, the delete/edit never persists, and on reopen the OLD list loads back — reads exactly like *"I deleted a rule but it came back / it's duplicating."* **Fix:** all six rule saves (highlights/triggers/macros/aliases/mutes/substitutes) go through `safeSetItem(key, value)` ([characterScope.ts](src/renderer/characterScope.ts)) — a try/catch that, on failure, logs, shows a ONE-SHOT `window.alert` pointing the user to Automation Analytics → "Remove duplicate copies", and returns `false` instead of throwing. **Investigation discipline that applies generally (this was the B197 process):** when a "data gets duplicated / doesn't persist" bug can't be found by reading, PROVE the pure data path with a harness before touching it — `tmp-dedup-repro` bundled the REAL `loadHighlights`/`saveHighlights` + the full `localStorage → YAML (`exportCharacterProfile`/`buildCharacterProfile`) → reload + restart (`importCharacterProfile`)` round-trip with a mock localStorage + in-memory `window.api`, and showed delete is correct and STABLE across reopen+restart (IDs unique via `nanoid`, `exportCharacterProfile` REPLACES `state`, not appends). That RULED OUT the data layer and pointed at quota / the React layer — far better than shipping a speculative "fix." Temporary `[hl-diag]` console logging (HighlightsPanel mount + delete: state count, post-save localStorage count, dup-id count) is the next step to pin a non-reproducible UI-layer bug on a reporter's machine; remove it once confirmed. **General rule: any localStorage write that can grow unboundedly (rule lists, logs, caches) must be quota-guarded; and a "duplication/persistence" bug is a data-path question first (harness it) and a UI question second.**

91. **When hand-decoding a format with a back-reference table (Ruby Marshal's object links), register EXACTLY the entries the reference implementation registers — an extra, missing, or misordered entry silently shifts every later reference to a plausible-but-wrong value (B202, v0.15.1).** [marshalParser.ts](src/main/lichbridge/marshalParser.ts)'s `'I'` (ivar-wrapper) handler pushed its own placeholder into the object table AND let the inner string register itself — but Ruby's `TYPE_IVAR` gets NO table slot (marshal.c registers only the inner value). One extra entry per I-wrapped value meant every subsequent `@` object link resolved one-plus slots early: moonwatch's `UserVars.sun` hash decoded with its `timer` key REPLACED by some other var's name (`"hunting_nemesis":177`, `"almanac_last_use":93` — a different wrong key per blob), which broke the Weather & Moons sun seed and had silently corrupted link-heavy blobs in the Lich Dashboard Variables tab since v0.5.0. The `'U'` branch had the sibling ORDERING bug (registered after reading its payload; Ruby registers before). **Why it hid for so long:** first-occurrence literals decode perfectly — only back-references (repeated/frozen strings, shared objects) mis-resolve, and they resolve to *valid-looking values of the right type*, not errors. This is the #72 family (don't trust your model of a serialization format — verify against real bytes), with a sharper tell: **corruption that varies per blob and substitutes plausible sibling values is a reference-table desync, not a data problem.** The fix protocol: read the reference implementation's registration rules (marshal.c `r_entry` call sites), match them slot-for-slot (inner-registers-not-wrapper; register-before-payload), and verify by re-dumping REAL data (all 22 uservars blobs) rather than synthetic cases — synthetic tests rarely produce enough repeated objects to exercise links.

92. **NEVER bound a TIME window with a LINE count — and never let two features answer the same question from two different sources.** *(v0.16.0, Catch Me Up. The naive log build was reverted then, but **v0.17.1 re-added log-backed Catch Me Up** the right way — `buildCatchupDigest` filters the TIME window in MAIN and returns a compact digest, exactly the architecture this pitfall demands. Both lessons below are LIVE in that code: the window is a time range, never a line cap, and the welcome-back card + catchup share their gather.)* Two bugs, one report (Sekmeht: *"the welcome-back card said 1599 lines but `/ai catchup 11m` said 763 — why don't they match?"*). **(a) The line-cap.** `readLogWindow` asked main for "the last `CATCHUP_LOG_TAIL` (8000) lines of the day-file" and then filtered by timestamp in the renderer. But N is a LINE cap being used to satisfy a TIME window, and the conversion rate is the character's log VOLUME — which varies by orders of magnitude. Measured against the real file: **Agan logs ~820 lines/min** (81k lines/day, mostly `inv`/`spells` state spam), so an 8000-line tail reached back **6.2 minutes**. An `/ai catchup 11m` therefore silently summarized ~6 minutes and reported the truncated count as if it were the whole window — **worst exactly where the log matters most** (a busy character). The fix is architectural, and the codebase already had the right precedent (`session-log:build-export`: *big data never crosses IPC, only the spec and the result*): a **`session-log:read-window(character, fromTs, toTs, maxRows)`** handler that filters **in main** and returns only the matching rows. `maxRows` is a *transport guard applied as a tail*, never the window bound. **When you find yourself converting a time question into a line count, stop — push the time filter down to whoever owns the data.** **(b) Two sources, one question.** The welcome-back card counted the **in-memory buffers** while Catch Me Up read the **log** — so they could never agree, and worse, the memory path was silently *under*-counting because `lines` is capped at `MAX_LINES` (2400) and an 11-minute burst had already trimmed. Both now go through ONE `gatherWindow(from, to)`. **If two surfaces describe the same window, they must share the gather function — a shared *invariant* in a comment is not enough** (this exact invariant WAS written down — "both read through one `collectHistory()`, so they can never disagree" — and then broken three edits later by adding log-sourcing to only one of them). **(c) The skip-list is load-bearing and easy to under-populate:** `spells` was missing from `CATCHUP_SKIP_STREAMS`, so 1,173 lines of clear+rewrite spell-list state per 11 minutes were being fed to the model as events. State-readout streams (`exp`/`inv`/`spells`/`activespells`/`percwindow`/`moonwindow`/`lichscripts`) contribute a stale TABLE, never history — when a new state stream appears, add it. **Diagnostic lesson:** this was unresolvable by reading (I theorized four wrong causes); it took **30 seconds of measuring the real log file** (`node -e` over `%APPDATA%\lichborne\Logs\{Char}\`) to make it obvious. When a discrepancy is a DATA question, go measure the data — don't reason about it.

93. **A floating CHROME window (command/vitals/icon) must NOT auto-size its own height — and any measure→persist loop that rewrites a saved rect is a data-corruption vector, not just a render tweak (v0.17.0, Sekmeht).** The command window read as too tall next to the slim chrome, so an "auto-hug" was added to [FloatingWindow.tsx](src/renderer/components/FloatingWindow.tsx): a `useLayoutEffect` measured the bar's content height and, when it differed from the rendered height, called `onChange({ rect: { …, h } })` to shrink the window to fit. It **built clean, converged in one step in theory, and was WRONG in three ways.** (a) **It's the pitfall #74 family** — chrome height is meant to be explicit/deterministic *precisely because* content measurement is racy (the icon/vitals bar can measure short mid-render before data lands), and the hug shrank the vitals window enough to CLIP the bars ("smashed"). (b) **It PERSISTS.** `onChange` → `updateWindow` → the freeWindows `saveFreeWindows`+`saveProfile` effect, so every (possibly-wrong) measured height was written into the character's saved layout — **per character, as you used each one.** Reverting the *code* could not un-write the *data*; affected characters stayed smashed until a manual delete+re-add / drag-resize / Rebuild-from-panels. (c) **It resized on interaction** — the effect ran on every render, so *moving* a window (which re-renders) re-measured and resized it, which the tester saw as "it's larger until I move it, then it snaps." **Rules that stick:** chrome windows keep an explicit height (the conversion/default size, user-resizable); if a "hug the content" behavior is ever genuinely wanted, it must (i) never shrink below a measured-safe floor, (ii) guard the racy 0/short measurement, and (iii) **NOT write the result back to persisted state on a timer/every-render** — a one-shot correction gated behind an explicit user action at most. The general lesson beyond windows: **an effect that MEASURES the DOM and PERSISTS the result is a feedback+corruption risk — treat "measure→setState→save" with the same suspicion as a render-phase side effect.** And since it never shipped (test-session only), the fix is to tell the affected tester to re-add the windows, NOT to add a migration that would reset every released user's legitimately-sized chrome.

94. **A text `<input>` in the game area inherits `--game-line-height` (the PROSE setting), and the text CARET is as tall as the line box — so pin an explicit `line-height` on any game-area input, especially one with elements pinned to its edges (v0.17.0, B216).** The command bar's `.command-input` set no `line-height`, so it inherited `--game-line-height` (the per-character PROSE line-height, typically 1.4–1.6). The blinking text caret is as tall as the line box, so at a large prose line-height the caret grew tall enough to overlap the **RT/CT/aim timer strips** pinned at the input's top/bottom edges (`.cmd-bar` / `.cmd-chip`, `position:absolute; top/bottom:0`). **Fix:** pin `.command-input { line-height: 1.2 }` (a tight fixed value, independent of the user's prose setting) so the caret stays short at any line-height, and size the input's vertical padding to clear the edge strips (padding ≥ strip height; the two were tuned together — input padding 7px vs 5px bars / 6px chips). **Rule:** game-area inputs should NOT inherit the prose line-height — pin it. The prose setting is for READING multi-line text; an input is a single line and wants a tight, predictable caret. Same font-scaling family as pitfalls #45/#58 (use `em`/`var(--game-font-size)`, not `rem`), but for the vertical/line-box axis. Any future game-area input with edge-pinned decorations (a search box, an inline editor) must pin its line-height and clear its edges the same way. **The clearance is FONT-SIZE-ROBUST by construction** (verified in the v0.17.0 bug check): the input's wrap height scales in lockstep with the caret (both are `1.44·gameFont`), so the strip edges move down exactly as fast as the caret grows — every clearance comparison reduces to fixed-px padding (7px) vs fixed-px strip, a CONSTANT margin at any font (1px chips / 2px bars). Don't "fix" it for large fonts — it can't degrade there. **Caveat kept on radar:** chips-mode margin is only **1px** — positive, but zero slack for a font's ascent/descent metrics or subpixel rounding painting the caret ~1px taller than its box. If a chips-style tester ever reports a hairline caret↔chip touch, the cheap fix is `.cmd-chip` height 6→5px (→2px, matching bars) or `.command-input` padding 7→8px — NOT a bar-mode concern (2px).

95. **`url(#id)` resolves to the FIRST matching id in the WHOLE DOCUMENT — so any SVG def id (`<linearGradient>`/`<radialGradient>`/`<filter>`/`<clipPath>`/`<mask>`) shared across multiple mounted instances of the same component CROSS-HIJACKS; make every def id per-instance-unique with React `useId()` (B217, v0.17.0).** The Moons experience can be mounted more than once at the same time — a floating window AND a panel tab, or (the tester's repro) the SAME character's Moons on one tab while ANOTHER character's Moons sits mounted-but-`display:none` on a background tab (pitfall #24 — hidden ≠ unmounted, its SVG is still in the DOM). Every instance's `<svg>` declared gradients with the SAME literal ids (`lb-ground`, `lb-shade`, `moon-xibar`, `sun`, `glow`, …). An SVG paint reference (`fill="url(#lb-ground)"`) is resolved by document order against the first element with that id — so once a second instance mounted, half the first instance's fills pointed at the second instance's gradient defs; when that second instance was on a `display:none` tab, its gradients still resolved but painted nothing usable, and the first instance's sky/moons/rays/shade went **flat/blank** (the tester's screenshot: switch char1→char2 moonwatch→back to char1 = stripped visuals). **Fix:** `const uid = 'm' + useId().replace(/[^a-zA-Z0-9]/g,'')` once per component, a `gref = (name) => \`url(#${uid}-${name})\`` helper, and every `id="lb-x"` → `id={\`${uid}-x\`}` with every `url(#lb-x)`/`fill={...}` → `gref('x')`. `useId()` is stable across renders and unique per mounted instance, so no two instances collide. **The ONLY safe exception is a def that is byte-identical AND static across every instance** (the Moons `lb-fog` gradient — same stops always, so cross-instance resolution paints the same thing); even then, prefer uniquifying unless there's a reason (e.g. it's referenced from a sibling module-level sub-component that has no access to the parent's `uid`). **General rule: any component that can mount more than once AND uses SVG `url(#…)` references MUST namespace its def ids per instance** — grep a new SVG component for `id="` / `url(#` before shipping. This bug is INVISIBLE with a single instance (the tell is "visuals break only after opening the same feature twice / on a second character") and it's a whole class: gradients, filters, clipPaths, masks, and `<use href>` all resolve by first-in-document id. `useId()` is the fix, not hand-rolled counters (SSR-safe, collision-free, stable).

96. **A scroll listener CANNOT tell a user scroll from a library/layout one — so never un-pin on a single scroll event; require the distance to PERSIST. And react-virtuoso actively scrolls you UP after a scrollback trim (B223, v0.17.1).** The years-long intermittent "the story window un-pins itself, scrolling locks, the 'New Lines' badge appears, and it never recovers" bug. The decisive tester clue was **"the scrollbar thumb quivers — tries to move then snaps back down"**: that's two writers fighting over `scrollTop`. **Mechanism (traced into react-virtuoso's source):** `appendTrimmed` cuts 400 lines in ONE slice (2400 → 2000, recurring every ~400 lines once the buffer is full — pitfall #81). That collapse makes Virtuoso compute `scrollDirection === 'up'`, which is **precisely the gate for its upward-scroll compensation**, while its index-keyed size tree is stale by 400 rows (we deliberately don't pass `firstItemIndex`). Its rAF-batched row re-measures then issue `scrollBy(-k)` — **a scroll nothing in our code suppresses** — and `stickToBottom`'s settle loop slams the bottom back each frame (THE QUIVER). Any compensation landing after that loop exits (2 stable frames) plus the ~250ms suppress tail reached `handleVirtuosoScroll`, whose `dist > 40` branch has **no way to know a human didn't do it** → spurious un-pin. **THE RULE: the un-pin branch must require the >40px distance to still hold ~2 frames later** (`unpinConfirmRef`, a double-rAF re-check that cancels if the distance collapses back). A library compensation is undone within a frame or two; a real user scroll holds forever. This is safe by construction because **wheel-up (`onWheel`) and PageUp/Home set `pinnedRef=false` DIRECTLY and never reach this branch** — only scrollbar drag/arrow/track and touch go through it, and they merely commit 2 frames later. Keep it **source-agnostic**: it must hold whether the mover is Virtuoso, the browser clamping a shrunken scrollHeight, or a stalled-rAF window — do NOT re-write it to depend on identifying the source. **Second half — a spurious un-pin must be able to HEAL:** `onRefocus` used to be gated on `pinnedRef.current`, so once un-pinned it refused to act and the badge survived every return to the window. It now re-pins when `unpinAtRef > lastBlurAtRef` — the un-pin happened **while the window was away**, so it cannot have been the user. **Use that timestamp comparison, NOT "did we observe a user input?"** — detecting a scrollbar-drag `pointerdown` is not something we can rely on, and guessing wrong yanks a reader who HAD scrolled up (the never-un-pinned default of 0 fails the comparison, which is the safe direction). **Two findings that came out of this investigation and change how you read older pitfalls:** (a) **`backgroundThrottling: false` ALSO affects the Page Visibility API** — Electron 43's own typings say so verbatim — so `document.hidden` very likely stays FALSE while minimized/occluded, meaning **the `document.hidden` guard B191 added to `handleVirtuosoScroll` (pitfall #71) is probably inert**, and `visibilitychange` may never fire (the room pump's hidden-drain leans on the same signal). That's WHY the B223 fix was built not to depend on it; if you ever need a real hidden signal, verify it empirically first — don't trust `document.hidden` in this app. (b) **`overflow-anchor: none`, which BUGS.md B20 documented on `.text-window`, is GONE from `src/`** (zero hits) — Chromium scroll anchoring is still neutralized only because react-virtuoso stamps `overflow-anchor: none` on every item element, so the app-level guarantee no longer exists; if you ever stop using Virtuoso for this list, restore it. **Deliberately NOT done (don't "finish" these without a fresh ask):** the root trigger is untouched — the quiver is still visible, because stopping it means changing how the trim interacts with Virtuoso's compensation (risky, and the pin is now safe regardless); and a user-intent gate was designed and HELD precisely because of the unverifiable `pointerdown`-on-scrollbar assumption.

97. **A WOUND and a SCAR are different states — and "healthy" must be derived from the ABSENCE of a known marker, never from a sentinel equality (B224, v0.17.1).** A tester's Injuries panel showed wounds that "stayed persistent since she died", while `HEAL` reported *"no significant injuries"* and full strength. It read exactly like a stale-panel/refresh bug; **it wasn't — the panel was updating fine and mis-reading the protocol.** DR encodes each body part in the `<image name>` inside `<dialogData id='injuries'>`, and per **Lich's parser (`lib/common/xmlparser.rb` ~681-690 — the authority, mirror it VERBATIM like the combat/assess regexes in §32.1):** `Injury<n>` = an ACTIVE wound of rank n; **`Scar<n>` = that wound HEALED (Lich sets `wound = 0`) and left a scar of rank n**; `Nsys<n>` = nerve damage. Lichborne's panel treated **any** name `!== the part id` as a wound and pulled its trailing digit as severity — so `Scar2` rendered as a permanent "Moderate" **wound**. Every row in her screenshot was a SCAR (which is why HEAL disagreed, and why they survived death: scars persist). **Two transferable rules:** (a) when a protocol has multiple KINDS of state in one field, parse the KIND explicitly — never treat "not the healthy sentinel" as one catch-all bad state, and never scrape a severity digit off an unrecognized string; (b) derive HEALTHY from the absence of every known marker (`/^(injury|scar|nsys)(\d)/i` didn't match ⇒ healthy), not from `name === id` — that way an unhurt part clears correctly whichever sentinel DR uses (`head`, `Body`, `Injury0`, …). **Display rule (polish standard #1):** a scar is healed HISTORY, not damage — show it muted/neutral (no wound hue, no fill) and keep "No active wounds." accurate whenever no WOUND is present even if scars remain, or the panel contradicts the game's own `HEAL` output. **Process lesson:** the DESIGN protocol table had documented the name as the part id plus a digit (`"head1"`) and never mentioned scars — the code faithfully implemented a wrong spec, so the docs propagated the bug. When a parser and a tester's report disagree, check the SPEC against the reference implementation (Lich), not just the code against the spec; the DESIGN entry is now corrected. **Two related gaps left UNCHANGED on purpose (want a raw-XML capture around a heal before touching):** the parser only emits `injury-update` when the dialog contains ≥1 `<image>`, so a genuinely EMPTY injuries dialog can never clear the panel; and the renderer REPLACES the whole injury map while Lich MERGES per-part — replace is wrong if DR ever sends deltas, merge is wrong if a part can only be cleared by omission. Don't "fix" either by guessing; one capture settles both.

---

## Proactive bug-checking

The goal is to find bugs before testers do — both new bugs the current change might introduce, and **latent bugs from prior versions that are still living in the current code**. Lichborne is single-developer with a small tester pool; every bug we ship is one a tester has to find and report, costing them and us time. Two complementary practices.

### Iron rule: read the actual code, not memory or docs

Every claim you make about how the code behaves must come from reading the file you're claiming about, IN THIS SESSION. Not from CLAUDE.md, not from pitfalls, not from a Tracker.md entry describing the code, not from "I remember how this works." Documentation describes the code's intent and history; only the source describes what it currently does. The B114 false-positive that prompted this rule (v0.8.7 retroactive sweep): pitfall #33 described the theme-overlay re-apply hook pattern, I worked from that description, claimed a multi-character bug existed, and was wrong — the actual effect at [GameWindow.tsx:954-973](src/renderer/components/GameWindow.tsx#L954-L973) had `isActive` in its deps and re-applied overlays directly on tab switch, which the pitfall didn't mention because the pitfall was scoped to a different scenario. Acting on the false positive would have shipped a redundant fix and possibly introduced a real new bug. The fix-cost of a false positive is higher than the fix-cost of doing the read.

**Verification protocol** when claiming a bug exists or doesn't exist:
- Grep for the specific function / state / effect you're reasoning about.
- Read the relevant lines yourself (Read tool with line offsets, not just the grep snippet — grep context can mislead by hiding deps arrays, guard clauses, or cleanup returns).
- Confirm the deps array of any `useEffect` you reason about — pitfalls describe patterns, not necessarily the current deps list.
- Confirm the cleanup function — pitfalls describe what's supposed to happen, not necessarily what does.
- If a pitfall and the current code disagree, **the code wins** — and the pitfall needs updating.

This rule has no "n/a." Every retroactive sweep claim, every "this is safe because…" assertion, every "no concerns" sign-off must be backed by a read in this session. The cost is 30 seconds of grep + read per claim; the benefit is not shipping false-positive fixes (and not missing real bugs that contradict your memory of how something works).

### Investigating a reported bug — build a fact chain, don't pattern-match a fix

When a tester reports a bug, the job is a **real, hard bug-check of the actual code** — not "this smells like the last bug, ship a plausible patch." The discipline that worked for B189/B190/B191 (and that you should repeat):

1. **Reproduce the symptom precisely, in the tester's words, and note what DOESN'T happen.** "Active char only, not background tabs" / "echoes but no `>` prompt" / "only after tabbing away, not minimizing" — each negative is a clue that *eliminates* whole hypotheses. Write down the exact discriminator before touching code.
2. **Trace it end-to-end by SCANNING THE CODE, link by link** (grep → read the real lines, Iron rule). Build an explicit chain: source → … → effect. Each link is either **confirmed from code** (you read it this session) or **an inference** — and you must label which. B191's chain was 5 confirmed code links + ONE labelled inference (occlusion ⇒ `document.hidden`, which the room pump already relies on). Never present an inference as a fact.
3. **Decide how the cause is knowable:**
   - **Glaringly obvious from the read** (a deleted call, a wrong var, a missing gate) → fix it, then re-read the whole function body (pitfall #86 — a green build is not proof the behaviour survived).
   - **Logic/resolution bug** (which string, which branch, which match) → confirm with the **harness** (`tmp-cmd-harness` / `tmp-scene-harness`), or add a case to it; if there's no harness for that logic, that's a signal to build one.
   - **Timing / environment / lifecycle-dependent** (rAF throttle while occluded, reconnect-in-place, replay race, async measurement) → you usually **cannot** prove it statically. Either **simulate the condition** (a `tmp-*` repro like `tmp-scroll-repro`, or reason from an existing mechanism the codebase already trusts for that condition — e.g. the room pump's `document.hidden` branch *is* the evidence that occlusion throttles rAF), or **drop a temporary `[diag]` log** at the suspect link and have the tester reproduce (pitfall #83's lesson: one real reproduction beats hours of static analysis).
4. **Prefer a fix that is provably safe regardless of the residual uncertainty.** B191's guard (`document.hidden` → skip un-pin) can only PREVENT a state transition that's impossible-by-definition while hidden, so it cannot regress the visible path even if the exact trigger were mis-identified. When you can find such a fix, the one unproven inference stops mattering.
5. **State the residual honestly.** Name the single thing you did NOT prove, say what would confirm it (the diagnostic), and ship the safe fix anyway. Don't pretend certainty you don't have, and don't withhold a safe fix waiting for certainty you can't cheaply get.

The anti-pattern this guards against: the v0.14.1 macro "fix" that pattern-matched "stale sessionId" (a real latent issue) onto a symptom whose *actual* immediate cause turned out to be a deleted send line — and a comment-edit regression then made it worse. Chain-of-evidence + re-read-the-body would have caught it before the tester did.

### Pre-merge checks

**Check zero (mechanical, ALWAYS): `npm run build:main` + `npm run build:renderer` + `npx tsc --noEmit`.** Vite/esbuild only TRANSFORM TypeScript — they do **not** typecheck, so a reference to a deleted variable sails through both builds and crashes at runtime (B166's first draft shipped a dangling `debugDockHeight` through two "successful" builds; only `tsc` caught it). `tsc` is now CLEAN (0 errors) — the 2 long-standing `HTMLElement | Window` errors in GameWindow's Virtuoso scroller typing were fixed in v0.17.1 (they were real un-narrowed-union holes — `el.clientHeight` / `ro.observe(el)` used outside the `HTMLElement` guard; fixed by widening the `scrollerRef` guard from `if (el)` to `if (el instanceof HTMLElement)`, which our scroller always is). ANY tsc error is now yours — there is no baseline noise to look past. Especially mandatory after REVERTING or REWORKING a change mid-session (that's the dangling-reference window). **But Check zero is NOT sufficient: build + tsc do NOT catch a DELETED side-effecting statement** — removing a `window.api.sendCommand(...)` / a `setState` / an effect's `return` cleanup leaves perfectly valid code, so both pass green while the behavior is silently gone (v0.14.1: an Edit replaced `sendCommand`'s send call with a comment; both builds passed; the command echoed but never sent — pitfall #86). **After any Edit that touches a function body — especially one that replaces a line with a comment — RE-READ the whole body, not a grep for the token you changed.** A green build proves it compiles, never that it still *does* the thing.

Before declaring a change done, run through these five questions. ~30 seconds per change, catches the classes of bug this codebase has actually shipped (B114 cross-tab overlay drift, B121 cross-feature state writes, the kind of stale-state-vs-new-code mismatches that come from incremental migrations). The right answer to any of these can be "n/a" — the point is to have considered it.

1. **What state does this write that other code reads?** List every var / ref / state your change writes. For each, grep one consumer and read it. Cross-feature state is where the bug class lives: B121 cleared `roomState.desc` and three other subsystems (Room panel, Lich Map findRoom, Genie Map resolver, contacts effect) read it. The pre-check found the same-batch behavior was already absorbed by existing protections (B109 timer, F34 early-return); the after-the-fact discovery would have shipped as B12X. If your change writes nothing other code reads, the answer is "n/a" — say so.

2. **What cleanup runs on unmount vs. on hide?** Tabs in Lichborne don't unmount when you switch — they go `display:none` (pitfall #24). So `useEffect` cleanup only fires on real unmount (close session), not on hide. Anything that should re-fire on *show* (re-apply per-character settings, refresh layout-dependent measurements, reset transient state) needs an explicit activeId-watcher in App.tsx, NOT just a mount-effect in GameWindow. B114 shipped with this gap: theme-overlay re-apply only ran on theme change, not on tab switch, so two characters with different accessibility overlays bleed into each other. If your change relies on a mount/unmount lifecycle, ask "does this need to fire on show/hide too?"

3. **Does the current code handle state written by older versions of itself?** YAML profile files, localStorage entries, the genie parse cache, the panel layout state, custom themes — all of these were written by some prior Lichborne version a user already ran. When your change reads any of this data, what happens if the field is missing (older write), has a different shape (intermediate refactor), or has a value the new code doesn't expect? **Backward compatibility we care about runs in one direction only**: current code reading prior-version state. We do NOT care about older clients reading newer files — testers run the current build, not v0.8.4. The right answers: (a) treat missing fields as their type default (most optional YAML), (b) bump GENIE_CACHE_VERSION when the cached shape changes (pitfall #16), (c) write an explicit migration in `profile-migrations.ts` by SOURCE version when a field is renamed / restructured. The wrong answer is reading stale state and crashing / silently dropping data the user previously saved.

4. **Does this change the `CharacterProfile` or `SharedProfile` shape — and if so, where's the upgrade guardrail?** This is the mandatory profile-safety check; a user's whole setup lives in `profiles/*.yaml` + `_shared.yaml`, and corrupting it on upgrade is the worst bug class we can ship (pre-v0.6.4 wiped everyone's profiles, principle #8). **Always ask it, even when the answer is "no change."** Walk it explicitly:
   - **Did I add/rename/restructure a field on `CharacterProfile` or `SharedProfile` ([profile-types.ts](src/renderer/profile-types.ts)), or change what a `state.*` suffix means?** Adding a NEW *optional* field is non-breaking — it loads as `undefined` on old profiles and needs no migration (just a sensible default at the read site). Renaming, removing, retyping, or changing the meaning of an existing field IS breaking.
   - **For a breaking change**: bump the version constant (`SHARED_PROFILE_VERSION` / `CHARACTER_PROFILE_VERSION` in [profile.ts](src/renderer/profile.ts)) AND register a migration in [profile-migrations.ts](src/renderer/profile-migrations.ts) keyed by the SOURCE version. Migrations must be PURE (the file isn't rewritten unless every step succeeds). The forward guardrail already exists for free: `runMigrations` returns `null` for a future-version file so a downgrade preserves it on disk rather than clobbering it — don't defeat that.
   - **For a NEW sidecar file/format** (like the v0.10.0 `.lb.yaml` Transfer bundle, or the genie cache): give it its OWN `formatVersion` and reject newer-than-known on read (`parseProfileExport` rejects `formatVersion > current`; genie cache bumps `GENIE_CACHE_VERSION`). New folders (e.g. `Exports/`) need no migration but must be created on demand (`ensureExportsDir`).
   - **For a new per-character setting**: it's a new `state.*` suffix — non-breaking by construction (the dynamic `state:` map round-trips it), but decide whether it belongs in the Profile Transfer allowlist (`TRANSFER_CATEGORIES`, pitfall #56) and the `_shared.yaml` vs per-character split.
   The output is one line: "no profile-shape change" OR "added optional field X (default Y)" OR "breaking: bumped to vN + migration registered." Never leave it unstated — a silent schema drift is how a profile-eating bug ships.

5. **Does this change add or alter a user-facing capability — and is its slash-command surface in lockstep?** (Principle #11.) Walk it explicitly:
   - **New capability**: decide its `/command` (or record "no command because X" in the feature's DESIGN section) — new rule types get the full `add`/`remove`/`list`/`edit` verb set + `openRuleId` plumbing; toggles get the `/timestamps` shape; new completable values extend `SlashLiveData`.
   - **Changed capability**: `grep slashCommands.ts` for the feature's noun. Update executors, options, hints, examples, summary formatters, and error messages to match the new behavior — stale command help is a shipped bug, same class as a stale tooltip. Re-run the `tmp-*` slash harness cases if the resolution logic moved.
   - **Removed/renamed capability**: remove the entry (fail-closed covers users' muscle memory with a `/help` hint) or keep the old noun as a `nounAliases` alias.
   The output is one line: "slash surface: added /X" OR "updated /X entries for the new option" OR "n/a — no user-facing capability change" OR "no command by design: <reason>, recorded in DESIGN §N."

These are not a substitute for testing — they're a substitute for the bug report you'd otherwise get next week. The right output is either "no concerns" + a one-line note in the commit message, or a tracked issue if a concern surfaces that's out of scope for the current change.

### Retroactive sweeps at version boundaries

When cutting a new version (or whenever there's a natural pause), do a focused read of the last 3–5 versions' Tracker entries with a different question: **not "did the change work" but "what could a tester still hit that hasn't been reported yet?"** The pattern that ships dormant bugs in this codebase:

- A new feature (Fxx) writes state or uses an effect lifecycle in a way that's correct for its own scope but interacts unexpectedly with an OLDER subsystem the author wasn't focused on.
- The bug is silent — no exception, no obvious wrong rendering. Just a corner case where state drifts (B114), focus jumps unexpectedly (F32 edge cases), or stats accumulate against the wrong target.
- It takes a specific user configuration to trigger: multi-character + accessibility overlay (B114), Ctrl+Tab from a modal text input (F32), Lich script with both `<streamWindow>` and `<pushStream>` for the same id (B123).

For each recent feature, ask the five pre-merge questions retroactively (incl. #5: does its slash-command surface exist and still match the feature's current behavior?). Read the consumers of any state it writes. Verify the cleanup story on show/hide. Check whether older saved state still loads correctly. Don't refactor on speculation — log a real concern with a repro path, or call it clean. The retroactive sweep done for v0.8.7 found B114 (real, fixed in v0.8.7) and noted F32 edge cases (deferred, not fix-worthy without a tester report). That's the right output shape: distinguish "real bug worth fixing" from "future-feature concern" from "minor papercut without a clean fix" and don't conflate them.

**When to do this**: at the cut of every minor version (v0.x.0 → v0.x+1.0) at minimum, and ideally before each patch release when a meaningful feature shipped recently. The cost is one focused review session; the alternative is a tester finding it cold and the trust hit that comes with shipping obvious-in-retrospect bugs.

---

## Commands

```
npm install              # one-time
npm start                # build main + renderer, launch Electron
npm run build            # build only, no launch
npm run build:main       # esbuild → dist/main/main.js, preload.js
npm run build:renderer   # vite → dist/renderer
npm run dev:renderer     # vite dev server on :5173 (NODE_ENV=development)
npm run dist             # build + electron-builder NSIS installer → release/
```

No unit-test framework — verify changes by running `npm start` and exercising the UI, guided by the current version's `testplans/` checklist (whose `[auto]`-tagged items are locked by the harnesses below — run them before packaging). **Three machine-local regression harnesses exist for the trickiest pure logic** — the two below plus **`tmp-rules-harness`** (`node tmp-rules-harness/run.mjs`), which bundles the REAL rule/profile modules with Node stubs (localStorage / document / window.api) and locks the v0.15.2 global-rules stack: ruleIdentity keys, `asGlobalRules` + the `_global` virtual-scope store, `applyProfileImport`'s global-awareness (merge/idempotency/global-skip/Replace-never-wipes-globals), the `_shared.yaml` bridge round-trip, and `planReconnect` (F62's account law — extracted to [reconnectPlan.ts](src/renderer/reconnectPlan.ts) precisely so it's harnessable). Run it after touching ruleIdentity/profileTransfer/profile shared-lists/reconnect logic. The older two (gitignored under `tmp-*/` because they embed verbatim corpus/player data; rebuild from each one's README/recipe if wiped): **`tmp-scene-harness`** (SceneParser capturers vs the real captured session — recipe in DESIGN §35.4) and **`tmp-cmd-harness`** (`node tmp-cmd-harness/run.mjs`) which bundles the real `macros.ts` and asserts the command-RESOLUTION core that feeds the send path — `resolveMacro` / `resolveAlias` / `parseCursorMarker` / `matchKeyCombo` (incl. the numpad mapping behind Morress's `Num+`→LOOK) / `interpolate` / `getMacroToken`. Neither harness reaches the React component send call itself (pitfall #86 — that's caught by re-reading the body); they lock the testable logic underneath. Run `tmp-cmd-harness` after touching macro/alias/cursor resolution or key-combo matching.

Releases ship via `node publish.mjs` (needs `$env:GH_TOKEN`). Cleans `release/`, builds, **PRE-CREATES the draft release**, packages, uploads, verifies, patches release body from `release-notes.md`, prints the draft URL. **Do NOT create git tags manually** — the tag is only created when the draft is published (a pre-created DRAFT does not tag). The script **refuses to publish if release-notes.md doesn't mention the current version** and warns on a dirty/unpushed git tree. **The pre-create step is load-bearing (Sekmeht hit this):** electron-builder's GitHub publisher creates the release lazily on the FIRST artifact upload and uploads in PARALLEL — two uploads can race the creation, and GitHub allows duplicate drafts on one tag, splitting artifacts across TWO draft releases (the "blockmap in its own release" bug). Pre-creating makes every upload target one release; the script also post-verifies (deletes empty duplicate drafts, refuses on asset-bearing duplicates, and checks the exe/blockmap/latest.yml set is complete before you publish).

**Packaging rules (v0.15.0 hygiene pass):**
- **Check for platform updates periodically (a standing recommendation — do it at version boundaries or every few weeks, Sekmeht 2026-07-21).** Run **`npm outdated`** and read it in three tiers: **(1) within-major "Wanted" bumps** (e.g. electron 43.0→43.2, `@electron/rebuild`, `@types/node` patch, `react-virtuoso`) are low-risk security/bugfix updates — take them, then re-run Check zero (build:main + build:renderer + tsc) and a launch smoke; an Electron patch inside the SAME major keeps the bundled Node/Chrome line, so no esbuild-target/@types/node change and (same ABI) usually no rebuild, though `npx electron-rebuild -f -w better-sqlite3` is the safe habit. **(2) Held majors** — **React 19, Vite 8/`@vitejs/plugin-react` 6, TypeScript 7, better-sqlite3 13, `@types/node` 26** are deliberate, breaking migrations; do NOT bump them casually — each is its own dedicated effort with its own testing. **(3) An Electron MAJOR** (43→44…) is the FOUR-things-in-lockstep ritual below. Record the check + what you took in the version's notes so the next person sees the cadence. **Verified baseline (2026-07-21): Electron 43.0.0 = Node 24.17 / Chrome 150; esbuild `node24` + `@types/node 24` aligned; `dependencies` = `better-sqlite3` only.**
- **`dependencies` = TRUE runtime externals ONLY** (currently just `better-sqlite3`). Everything else is bundled by esbuild (main — see `external` in [build-main.mjs](build-main.mjs), the source of truth) or Vite (renderer) and belongs in `devDependencies` — a bundled package listed in `dependencies` ships a SECOND, dead copy in the asar.
