Adding a new npm package? devDependencies unless it's native/unbundleable, in which case also add it to esbuild's `external`.
- **Electron upgrades move FOUR things in lockstep:** `electron`, `better-sqlite3` (new ABI → may need its own major), esbuild `target` in build-main.mjs (match the bundled Node: `ELECTRON_RUN_AS_NODE=1 electron -p process.versions.node`), and `@types/node`. Then `npx electron-rebuild -f -w better-sqlite3`, and run the verification ladder: builds → tsc → launch smoke → a DIRECT better-sqlite3 in-Electron diag (it's lazy-loaded in [sqliteReader.ts](src/main/lichbridge/sqliteReader.ts), so a launch alone doesn't prove the ABI) → `npm run dist`. Pre-flight grep for the release-notes' breaking-changes APIs before starting.
- **`ELECTRON_RUN_AS_NODE` trap (cost a phantom bug hunt in the v0.15.0 upgrade):** with that env var set, electron.exe runs as plain Node — `require('electron')` then resolves the npm package (a path STRING; `ipcMain`/`app` undefined) and the app "crashes at startup" in a way that perfectly impersonates an Electron breaking change. In this dev environment the var can LEAK between shell invocations after a version probe — clear it in the SAME call as any electron launch (`Remove-Item Env:\ELECTRON_RUN_AS_NODE`), and when a fresh Electron "breaks" at `require('electron')`, check the environment before the code.
- **App icon:** `build/icon.ico` (multi-size) is auto-detected from buildResources — exe/installer/shortcuts need NO config. `app.setAppUserModelId('com.lichborne.app')` in main.ts is the matching taskbar identity; keep it equal to `build.appId`.

- **Per major version: rotate the Discord invite link — now in TWO places, keep them in sync.** The invite URL is hardcoded (a) in the native menu's **Help → Discord** item in `setupMenu()` ([main.ts](src/main/main.ts) — search `discord.gg`) and (b) as `DISCORD_URL` in [credits.ts](src/renderer/credits.ts) (the About modal's "Join our Discord" link, v0.17.0). For each major version, generate a fresh invite and update **both** so the link can't go stale/expire on shipped builds (and so we can tell which version a join came from). Update both literals, rebuild, and re-check the link opens from both the menu and the About dialog. (Main and renderer are separate processes, so they can't share one const without a shared-module refactor — hence the two literals.)
- **Keep the Help → About Lichborne credits current — inspect them every release.** As of v0.17.0 the About dialog is a **themed React modal** ([AboutModal.tsx](src/renderer/components/AboutModal.tsx) + [about.css](src/renderer/styles/about.css)), NOT the old native message box — opened via the menu-action bridge (`'about'` in [menuActions.ts](src/shared/menuActions.ts) → `runAppActionRef` in [App.tsx](src/renderer/App.tsx) → `setShowAbout`); the native menu item just `sendMenuAction('about')`s to the focused window. **Credits are the single source of truth in [credits.ts](src/renderer/credits.ts)** — three exports: **`DEVELOPERS`** (`['Sekmeht', 'Binu']`), **`CONTRIBUTORS`** (people who've filed logged reports/fixes), **`TESTERS`** (the rest of the pool — no logged reports yet) — plus `ABOUT_BLURB` + `REPO_URL` + `DISCORD_URL` (the "Join our Discord" link — mirror of the menu invite, see the Discord-rotation rule). **Rules:** (a) the version shown comes from `window.api.getAppVersion()` → main's `get-app-version` handler → `app.getVersion()` — DYNAMIC (reads `package.json`), auto-tracks every release; never hardcode it. (b) When a new person joins the pool, **add them to `TESTERS`**; promote them into `CONTRIBUTORS` once they've filed a logged bug/fix — this two-tier split is a first-class courtesy, not an afterthought (treat "is everyone credited in the right tier?" as part of the release check). (c) **Both lists are ordered by contribution volume** (count logged mentions in BUGS.md, combining aliases — see below); re-sort when the counts shift. (d) Identity notes to honor: **Rakkor ≡ TheTargonian** (list once as "Rakkor", counts combined); ****Illiahanna** is the renamed **JadedSoul** ≡ Jaded (one person — BUGS.md still uses the old handles, so count those toward Illiahanna)** (combined); **Elore ≡ Cherisse ≡ the renamed Aubrey** (ONE person, counts combined → 3rd, list as "Elore"); **Binu is a co-CREATOR** (in `DEVELOPERS`, never in a credits list). (e) It's now **themed** — style it via `about.css` with theme vars / `color-mix` and eyeball it on light themes (Principle #4); don't revert it to a native message box. When someone is promoted (tester → contributor → creator) or two handles turn out to be one person, reconcile `credits.ts` so nobody is double-listed, mis-tiered, or miscredited.
- **About easter-egg MIDI player (v0.17.0) — self-contained, zero deps.** The About modal can play a bundled `.mid` (drop it at `src/renderer/public/about-theme.mid`; Vite copies it to `dist/renderer/`, loaded via XHR arraybuffer — `fetch` of a file:// resource is unreliable in Electron). [midiPlayer.ts](src/renderer/midiPlayer.ts) is a hand-rolled Standard-MIDI-File parser (`parseMidi` → both extracted `notes` AND the raw timed `events`) + two `MidiPlayback`s: **`MidiOutPlayer`** routes the raw events to the OS synth via **Web MIDI** (the Microsoft GS Wavetable Synth — sounds like Windows Media Player; needs the `'midi'` permission, added to main's `setPermissionRequestHandler`), and **`MidiSynth`** is a Web-Audio oscillator FALLBACK when no MIDI output exists. `createMidiPlayer` picks the best. Muted by default (the AudioContext / MIDI access only spin up on the first un-mute — a user gesture). **Do NOT `import` a `.mid` via Vite** (a missing file breaks the build) — reference it by runtime path in `public/`. **`.mid` CANNOT go in an `<audio>` element** (Chromium has no MIDI synth) — that's the whole reason for this. **Two reusable gotchas this surfaced:** (1) **Web MIDI messages sent with future timestamps CANNOT be unsent** — so bounding audio on Mute/close needs a SHORT lookahead + suppressing only real note-ONs (velocity>0, keep note-offs flowing) + an All-Notes-Off sent BOTH immediately AND scheduled past the lookahead window (else a note drones after the About window closes). (2) **Never put side effects inside a `setState(prev => …)` updater** — StrictMode double-invokes updaters in dev; compute the next value from current state and do the side effect outside (the `toggleMusic` fix).
- **Experience ⚙ layers can DEFAULT OFF via `defaultHidden` — but respect it in three places or they disagree (v0.17.0).** An `ExperienceOptionDef` may set `defaultHidden: true` (Moons countdowns/names — the orrery pill covers them). The `hidden` map stores only EXPLICIT choices, so the default applies when the key is absent, and it must be honored identically by: (a) the **component gating** (`hidden?.x === false` = shown-only-if-explicitly-on, matching `optionShown`), (b) the **⚙ checkbox** `checked={optionShown(hidden, opt)}` in BOTH ExperienceLayer (floating) and PanelFrame (tab), and (c) the **toggle**, which must store the EXPLICIT value (`onSetExperienceOption(expId, optId, hidden)`, not a blind `!hidden?.[optId]` flip) and SEED new instances with `defaultHiddenMap(def)` so the default PERSISTS to the profile. `optionShown` / `defaultHiddenMap` in [experiences.ts](src/renderer/experiences.ts) are the single source — use them, don't re-derive. (This is why a blind-flip toggle can't support a default-off layer: from the absent-key default, one flip would set `true` (hide) again, never showing it.)

---

## Documentation discipline

**"Update documentation"** means: **BUGS.md, DESIGN.md, Tracker.md, README.md, CLAUDE.md, the current version's test plan, AND — as needed — three CONDITIONAL docs: AINOTICE.md (whenever the change touched AI processing), Knowledge.md (whenever the change surfaced new VERIFIED Lich-internals / DR-protocol knowledge), and Lichborne-User-Guide.md (when terminology/feature-names/locations change — NOT for every fix)** (CLAUDE.md added to the list 2026-05-17, the per-version test plan 2026-07-10, AINOTICE.md + Knowledge.md + Lichborne-User-Guide.md all 2026-07-23, all at Sekmeht's ask).

**The two conditional docs — ALWAYS ASSESS both, update only when they apply:** AINOTICE.md is user-facing AI privacy; Knowledge.md is the internal Lich/DR knowledge base. **Knowledge.md is where a hard-won, VERIFIED fact about how Lich or DragonRealms *actually works* gets recorded so it isn't re-derived** — the Marshal reference-table registration rules (B202/#91), a Lich downstream-hook that rewrites the stream (`inventory_boxes_off` / `textsubs`, #80), how Lich rewrites the room-id subtitle (`display_uid`/`display_lichid`, #65), a `drinfomon` parse rule or verified game constant we mirror (the `drbanking.rb` coin ratios, the `xmlparser.rb` injury/scar/assess encodings, the combat ladder), or a new Lich-version compatibility finding (5.18/5.19). It captures the LICH/DR *fact* (what the source does, with a `file:line` citation), NOT the Lichborne implementation (that's CLAUDE.md/DESIGN). When a bug-fix or feature is grounded in reading Lich's source or DR's protocol, ask "did I learn a durable Lich/DR fact worth adding to Knowledge.md?" — the pitfall goes in CLAUDE.md, the underlying Lich fact goes in Knowledge.md. Skip it (n/a) when nothing new about Lich/DR internals was learned.

**AINOTICE.md is the AI-processing & privacy notice (user-facing).** It is the one place that explains how Lichborne uses AI, what data goes to the LLM provider, and — critically — that **PII / credentials are NOT sent** (the redaction guardrail: `redactForAI` in [src/shared/redact.ts](src/shared/redact.ts) scrubs the account PIN output, credentials, and account username from the AI copy while the log on disk stays pristine). **When you update documentation, ASSESS whether AINOTICE.md needs it — and it does whenever the change affects: what AI features exist, what data an AI feature reads or sends, when/where it sends, the redaction rules, key storage, or the AI-never-issues-commands guardrail.** ONLY AI-related processing/privacy information belongs in AINOTICE.md — not general features. A new AI feature (or a change to an existing one's data flow) is not "done" until AINOTICE.md reflects it, same bar as the slash-command registry (Principle #11).

| File | Role | When to update |
|---|---|---|
| **CLAUDE.md** (this) | AI-facing guide. Behavior, conventions, pitfalls. | When a subsystem's *shape* changes, when a new pattern emerges, when a pitfall is discovered. Keep tight. |
| **DESIGN.md** | Technical spec, source of truth for *how* things work. | *Before* implementing significant UI / architecture changes. It's a spec, not a journal. |
| **Tracker.md** | Version history. Brief why/how per release. | When a release ships. Reverse-chronological. |
| **README.md** | User-facing. | When behavior visible to users changes. |
| **BUGS.md** | Tester-reported bug ledger (B-numbers). | Open / Resolved tables, with full root-cause notes on resolution. |
| **AINOTICE.md** | User-facing AI-processing & privacy notice. **Only AI data-flow / privacy content** (what's sent, redaction, keys, guardrails). | Whenever a change touches AI processing: a new/changed AI feature, what data it reads/sends, redaction rules, key storage, or the never-issues-commands guardrail. Committed (unlike the test plan). |
| **Knowledge.md** | Internal **Lich / DragonRealms knowledge base**. Verified facts about how Lich5 and DR *actually work* — `lich.db3` schema, Marshal format, feature flags, connection/frontend modes, `drinfomon` parse rules & game constants, and a **Lich version log** (what changed in each Lich release, what it means for Lichborne, and why any fix matters). Cite `file:line` in the source. NOT Lichborne implementation (that's CLAUDE.md/DESIGN). | As needed — whenever a fix/feature surfaced a new VERIFIED Lich/DR fact (a Marshal/hook/room-id/parse detail), OR a new Lich version was reviewed (record the delta + tester impact). Committed. |
| **Lichborne-User-Guide.md** | User-facing **primer / guide** — what Lichborne is, getting started, connecting, a feature tour (what each does + how to configure at a high level), the **With-Lich vs Without-Lich feature matrix**, and appendices (slash reference, Lich-vs-direct, where settings live, troubleshooting). Written for a total newcomer; friendly, concise, GitHub-hosted with internal anchor links. **NOT a changelog** (Sekmeht 2026-07-23: *"we don't need to capture a running list of updates"*). | Do NOT log every fix/feature. DO update when: **terminology changes**, a **feature is renamed**, or something is **retired / moved to a new location** — keep the evergreen tour accurate. Two snapshot sections ARE swapped per release (not appended): "What's New in the Latest Version" (mirrors release-notes' current version) and "On the Horizon (Roadmap)". Committed. |
| **testplans/test-plan-v{version}.md** | The version's manual verification checklist — every feature/fix that lands gets its Do → Expect items the same day it lands, so the pre-packaging feel pass is never reconstructed from memory. **Gitignored (Sekmeht, 2026-07-10) — machine-local like the `tmp-*` harnesses it feeds, not committed.** | Grows WITH the version (each feature/fix adds its items when it ships, not at the end); run before packaging; a NEW file is started when a new version begins (the old one stays as the local record of what was verified). Ordered by risk. Items whose PURE logic is harness-locked carry an `[auto]` tag; the rest is the manual pass. Mine pure-logic items into the `tmp-*` harnesses — the plan doubles as the harness-case backlog. |
| **release-notes.md** | GitHub release body. User-readable changelog. | Separate from Tracker.md (dev-facing). **Holds ONLY the current version's "what's new since the last release"** (Sekmeht, 2026-07-10 — tightened from the earlier "last 1–2 releases" allowance): when a new version begins, replace the file's contents with the new version's section. No running trail; the full version history lives in Tracker.md and git. |

---

## Operational guardrails

- **Never `git commit` without explicit user approval.** Asking is mandatory.
- **Windows + PowerShell** is the host shell. Use PowerShell syntax (`$null`, `$env:VAR`). Bash available for POSIX scripts.
- `profiles/` is gitignored; never commit user data captured during testing.
- `passwords.json` lives in `app.getPath('userData')`, encrypted with Electron `safeStorage` (Windows DPAPI). Don't move it into the repo tree.
- Prefer fixing root causes over adding fallbacks.
- **When proposing a feature, check the principles first.** If it duplicates Lich functionality, say so and ask. If it lives in the display/configuration/profile space, propose freely.
- **Native menu & hotkeys — "never touch" rules (PERMANENT).** These protect a consistent, Windows-native experience; treat them as invariants, not redesign-phase rules:
  - **Never override an Electron-reserved chord with a Lichborne action.** The built-in **role** accelerators stay exactly as-is — don't rebind them and never assign any of them to a Lichborne feature: `Ctrl+C/V/X/Z/Y/A` (clipboard / undo / redo / select-all), `Ctrl+R` & `Ctrl+Shift+R` (reload), `Ctrl+0` / `Ctrl+±` (zoom), `Ctrl+M` (minimize), `Ctrl+W` (close), `Ctrl+Q` (quit), `F11` (fullscreen), `Ctrl+Shift+I` / `F12` (devtools). Overriding any of these makes Lichborne behave unlike every other Windows app.
  - **Never touch the pre-existing in-app Lichborne chords.** `Ctrl+Shift+Enter` (QuickSend), `Ctrl+Tab` (next character), `Ctrl+1–9` (jump to character N, 1-indexed — `Ctrl+1` = first char) are handled in [App.tsx](src/renderer/App.tsx) and must keep working unchanged.
- **Native menu — hotkey policy (PERMANENT).** `setupMenu()` in [main.ts](src/main/main.ts) is the full File·Edit·View·Tools·Lich·Window·Help tree (shipped v0.10.0; Window menu gained the Move-to-New/Main-Window decouple items in v0.11.0). Policy: **(a) do NOT assign keyboard accelerators to native menu items** — Lichborne items are **click-only**; the final hotkey set is still deferred until agreed (don't invent shortcuts). **(b)** Where a native menu item maps to one of the pre-existing in-app chords above, *display* it as a hint via `registerAccelerator: false` (so App.tsx stays the handler — no double-fire) **unless** the chord is Electron-reserved. Lichborne menu clicks route through the `menu-action` IPC → `lichborne:session-action` DOM-event bridge ([src/shared/menuActions.ts](src/shared/menuActions.ts)); `sendMenuAction` targets the **FOCUSED** window — the active GameWindow there handles session actions, App handles app-level ones.
